1001 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johannes


No. 98-2239-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


229 Wis. 2d 215; 598 N.W.2d 299; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 654


May 21, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
June 30, 1999, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Fond du Lac County: HENRY B. BUSLEE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of homicide by negligent operation of a motor vehicle in violation of Wis. Stat. § 940.10, as well as other counts involving causing great bodily harm, sought relief from judgment of the Circuit Court for Fond du Lac County (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of causing a homicide and causing great bodily injury by the negligent use of a motor vehicle. Defendant caused a multiple-car accident, killing two people, and was found slumped over the steering wheel. A factual issue at trial was whether defendant had fallen asleep while driving or had looked away from the road while changing the radio station. Defendant contended that he had no warnings and that his conduct was ordinary negligence, not criminal behavior. On appeal, the court held that an objective standard for criminal negligence was applicable, and the fact that defendant went left of center was sufficient for the jury to conclude defendant was criminally negligent. In addition, the jury did not need to unanimously agree about why the defendant committed the negligent act, as sleep was not a legal defense. The criminally negligent act, and also the critical issue, was the jury's conclusion that defendant crossed the highway's centerline. Therefore, the court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions because the evidence was sufficient as an objective, not subjective, standard for criminal negligence was applicable, and the fact that defendant went left of center was sufficient for the jury to conclude defendant was criminally negligent. Also, the jury did not need to agree unanimously on why the defendant committed the negligent act.

 

1002 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zivcic


Nos. 98-0909 & 98-1381


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


229 Wis. 2d 119; 598 N.W.2d 565; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 725


April 6, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
June 29, 1999, Decided  
June 29, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY K. BRENNAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment entered by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) after a jury convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant. The defendant also appealed an order finding that he improperly refused to provide a breath sample under Wisconsin's Implied Consent Law, Wis. Stat. § 343.305.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol. At the police station, a breath test was administered to the defendant, but the report showed a deficient sample because the defendant did not blow enough air into the machine. A refusal hearing was held, and the trial court found the defendant improperly refused the breath test. The case proceeded and a jury found the defendant guilty. On appeal, the court rejected the defendant's claim that he was entitled to a twelve-person jury because he did not object to the six-person jury during trial. Although the arrest occurred in city limits, the court determined that the county sheriff had legal authority to arrest the defendant because the city was located in the county where the sheriff had jurisdiction. The court also held that the trial court did not erroneously exercise its discretion in ruling there was a sufficient foundation to qualify the officer who administered the breath test as a expert witness. Finally, the court held that the deficient sample of the breath test was admissible because it was not a test result or hearsay. The trial court's judgment and order were affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment entered after a jury convicted the defendant was affirmed because the defendant did not object to the six-person jury at trial, and the county sheriff had jurisdiction to make the arrest. The trial court's order finding that the defendant improperly refused to provide a breath sample was also affirmed because the trial court did not erroneously abuse its discretion in making its finding.

 

1003 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pfeifer


Nos. 98-2592-CR, 98-2593-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


229 Wis. 2d 734; 600 N.W.2d 54; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 675



June 24, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments and orders of the circuit court for Jefferson County: WILLIAM F. HUE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two cases consolidated for review, appellants sought review of Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) convictions of violating Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1), 346.65(2)(c), and 346.65(f). These statutes prohibited, as a felony, the operation of a motor vehicle while intoxicated and the operation of a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration, as a third offense and with a minor passenger under the age of sixteen.


OVERVIEW: In two consolidated cases, appellants were convicted of operating a vehicle while intoxicated and with a prohibited alcohol concentration, as third offenders and with a passenger under the age of sixteen, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63, 346.65(2)(c), and 346.65(2)(f). Appellate court affirmed. These two statutes, when applied in concert, were not ambiguous because the plain language clearly defined the elements of the felony. The elements listed were the only ones that the prosecution had to prove, thus the statutory scheme did not shift the burden of persuasion of an element of the crime to the offender. In addition, the argument that appellants were deprived of equal protection failed because, under the rational relationship test, Wisconsin had an interest in protecting children that provided a basis for the additional penalty. Furthermore, appellants were not actively misled by police's "Informing the Accused" form merely because it did not include the felony they were convicted of in its list of penalties. Lastly, reasonable suspicion existed for the investigatory stop of the first appellant's vehicle and officer justifiably permitted to conduct field sobriety tests.


OUTCOME: Felony convictions of the operation of a vehicle while intoxicated and with a prohibited alcohol concentration, as a third offense, with a passenger under the age of sixteen affirmed. Appellants were not denied procedural due process, nor were they deprived of unequal protection of the law. They were not actively misled by police and after investigatory stop of first appellant's vehicle, officer justified in conducting sobriety tests.

Clark v. Mudge


No. 99-0082


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


229 Wis. 2d 44; 599 N.W.2d 67; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 709


May 4, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
June 23, 1999, Decided  
June 23, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Racine County: RICHARD J. KREUL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin), granting plaintiffs' motion for a voluntary dismissal of their wrongful death suit so that they could avail themselves of the increased damage caps for loss of society and companionship following the amendment of Wis. Stat. § 895.04(4).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendant doctor for wrongful death following decedent's death. Decedent died four days after defendant doctor performed surgery on her. Plaintiffs then filed a motion for a voluntary dismissal so that they could avail themselves of the increased damage caps for loss of society and companionship following the amendment of Wis. Stat. § 895.04(4). The trial court granted plaintiffs' motion. The court affirmed. The court held that the trial court did not erroneously exercise its discretion by granting plaintiffs' motion for voluntary dismissal. The court held further that defendant doctor's claim that the retroactive application of the increased cap was unconstitutional, was not ripe for resolution because the claim was based on future or hypothetical facts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order granting plaintiffs' motion for voluntary dismissal of their wrongful death suit, holding that the trial court did not erroneously exercise its discretion. The court held further that defendant doctor's constitutional claim regarding the retroactive application of the increased cap was not ripe for resolution.

 

1005 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Declerc v. Bellin Mem. Hosp.


No. 98-3298


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


229 Wis. 2d 253; 599 N.W.2d 666; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 672



June 22, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown County: JOHN D. MCKAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint against defendants, hospital, and insurers, for negligence. Plaintiffs argued that the court erroneously concluded that the jury's verdict satisfied the five-sixths rule of Wis. Stat. § 805.09(2).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought a negligence action against defendants, hospital, and insurers, for damages sustained during an enema that plaintiff husband received before a colorectal screening. The lower court submitted liability questions to the jury for special verdict. The jury answered affirmatively that defendant hospital was negligent in providing plaintiff husband's care, with two jurors dissenting. The jury answered the question whether defendant hospital's negligence was the cause of plaintiff husband's injuries in the negative, with two different jurors dissenting. The lower court thereafter dismissed plaintiffs' action, finding that the jury's verdict satisfied the five-sixths rule of Wis. Stat. § 805.09(2). The appellate court affirmed the lower court decision. The court found that the five-sixths rule applied not only to claims, but also to defenses. Thus, when 10 of 12 jurors agreed to a question that disposed of plaintiff's claim, the rule was satisfied. The court held that plaintiffs' claim could not stand, because 10 of 12 jurors agreed that defendant hospital's negligence was not causal, and absent causation, plaintiffs did not have a claim for negligence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed dismissal of plaintiffs' action against defendants, finding that the jury's verdict satisfied the five-sixths rule. The court held that the rule was satisfied, because 10 of 12 jurors agreed to a question that disposed of plaintiffs' claim. The court found that 10 of 12 jurors agreed that defendant hospital's negligence was not causal, and absent causation, plaintiffs' negligence claim could not stand.

 

1006 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Kenosha v. Leese


No. 98-1769


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


228 Wis. 2d 806; 598 N.W.2d 278; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 724


March 26, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
June 16, 1999, Decided  
June 16, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: MARY KAY WAGNER-MALLOY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), finding Wis. Stat. § 800.14(4) unconstitutional because it violated the equal protection rights of the respondent by reserving to the appellant only the right to demand a jury trial in the event of an appeal.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 800.14(4) was amended to provide the losing party in a municipal proceeding the right to demand a jury trial on appeal to the circuit court. Defendant was tried in municipal court and found not guilty on a battery charge. That same day, plaintiff city filed a notice of appeal and a motion for a nonjury circuit court trial pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 800.14. Defendant filed a motion requesting the trial court to declare the statute unconstitutional because it denied a respondent the right to a jury trial. The court granted the motion. The court reversed. The court applied the five-factor Omernik test for determining whether there was a reasonable legislative classification and held that there was a rational basis for the legislature's distinction between appellants and respondents in municipal court appeals. The court held that the characteristics of each class (the appellants and the respondents) were sufficiently different to warrant different statutorily granted rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order finding the statute unconstitutional, holding that there was a rational basis for the legislature's distinction between appellants and respondents in municipal court appeals.

 

1007 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Bauer v. Village of DeForest


No. 98-2163


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


229 Wis. 2d 252; 599 N.W.2d 666; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 629



June 10, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: STUART A. SCHWARTZ, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied her motion for injunctive relief after defendant village mowed the weeds on her property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowner sought an injunction against defendant village after it mowed the weeds on her property. Plaintiff contended that defendant's weed ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court denied plaintiff's motion for injunctive relief. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that even if defendant's ordinance was vague about what weeds were prohibited, the fact that two clearly prohibited weeds were on plaintiff's property made the application of the challenged ordinance neither vague nor uncertain. The court further found that no argument had been raised that the object of the ordinance was in any manner improper. Finally, the court found that the means chosen by defendant to control the weed population were rationally related to defendant's purpose of preventing the weeds from blooming.


OUTCOME: The order denying plaintiff landowner's motion for injunctive relief after defendant village mowed the weeds on her property was affirmed because the means chosen by defendant to control the weed population were rationally related to its purpose of preventing the weeds from blooming.

State ex rel. Ledford v. Circuit Court


No. 99-0939-W


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


228 Wis. 2d 768; 599 N.W.2d 45; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 626


April 9, 1999, Submitted on a Petition  
June 10, 1999, Decided  
June 10, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] MANDAMUS to the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which denied petitioner's writ directing respondents, a circuit court and judge, to grant his petition to waive fees and costs associated with his federal 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, an inmate, filed a mandamus writ directing respondents, a circuit court and judge, to grant his petition to waive fees and costs associated with his 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim. Respondents denied petitioner's request after concluding that he failed to exhaust his administrative remedies because he did not file a notice of claim. Petitioner argued that while the statutory notice of claim procedures may have resulted in settlement, they were not administrative remedies under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1997e (a). Petitioner requested that the appellate court grant his writ petition allowing him to proceed with his federal claim without pre-payment of fees and costs. Appellate court granted petitioner's writ and concluded that a requirement regarding notice of claim procedures did not qualify as an administrative remedy. The court remanded the case to the trial court to determine whether the petitioner was indigent and if the claim was arguably meritorious.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to trial court and granted prison petitioner's writ directing respondents to grant his petition to waive fees and costs associated with his federal claim. The court held that the requirement of notice of claim procedures was not an administrative remedy.

 

1009 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Douglas (In re Douglas)


No. 97-0183


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


229 Wis. 2d 250; 599 N.W.2d 665; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 607



June 8, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DAVID A. HANSHER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed from a ch. 980 commitment order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment, based upon a jury verdict, finding him to be a sexually violent person and committed him to a secured facility for treatment. Initially, the state of Wisconsin had filed a petition alleging that respondent was a sexually violent person eligible for commitment under ch. 980.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a petition alleging that respondent was a sexually violent person eligible for commitment under ch. 980. During a jury trial, expert witnesses gave testimony that defined the substantial probability standard as being "more likely than not" that respondent would engage in acts of sexual violence. The jury found that respondent was a sexually violent person, and the trial court entered the ch. 980 commitment order. On appeal, respondent claimed that ch. 980 was unconstitutionally applied to him on several grounds, all of which the court rejected. Respondent argued that the trial court failed to properly define the substantial probability standard as it should have been defined to mean "extremely likely." Instead, the court found that the trial court's failure to define the term was not error as standard jury instructions were given and the jury was free to disregard the lower standard of that definition as asserted by the expert witnesses. Respondent also waived his right to review the issue because his counsel had used the experts' definition in his case and the court also found that there was sufficient evidence to support the commitment. The order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Ch. 980 commitment order was affirmed as the trial court committed no error in not defining substantial probability as standard jury instructions were given and because the jury was free to disregard the lower standard ("more likely than not") of that definition as asserted by the expert witnesses. Respondent's counsel also used the experts' definition in his case, thus, waiving the issue on appeal, and sufficient evidence supported the order.

 

1010 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. James F.R. (In re James F.R.)


No. 98-0103


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


229 Wis. 2d 250; 599 N.W.2d 665; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 610



June 8, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: THOMAS R. COOPER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which adjudicated him delinquent for committing first-degree sexual assault of a child, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1), arguing that his motion requesting the suppression of two inculpatory statements should have been granted and that he was denied his constitutional due process right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile's motion to suppress his first confession to police in regards to a charge of sexual assault on a minor should have been granted. Appellant was awakened in the middle of the night and questioned in the back of a police car and was not advised of his Miranda rights before appellant admitted the assault. The trial court erred in failing to apply the correct legal test of whether a reasonable person of appellant's age in appellant's circumstances would have believed he was in custody. However, admission of appellant's second statement to police made later at the police station was proper because he voluntarily repeated his confession after being fully informed of and waiving his Miranda rights. Following the denial of appellant's suppression motion, trial was to the court based on stipulated facts. Appellant asserted that he should have been accorded a jury trial. However, juveniles involved in delinquency proceedings were not entitled to a jury where the juvenile adjudicated delinquent was not subject to placement in an adult prison. Other issues raised for the first time on appeal the court declined to review and the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for sexual assault on a minor was upheld because the denial of appellant's suppression motion as to his confession after receiving Miranda warnings was proper even though appellant's motion as to suppression of his first statement should have been granted for lack of Miranda warnings. Appellant was not entitled to a jury trial where a delinquency adjudication would not subject him to placement in an adult prison.

Mid-Plains, Inc. v. PSC


No. 98-0833


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


228 Wis. 2d 509; 597 N.W.2d 773; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 573



May 27, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant commission challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted a property interest in a federal exemption to respondent, a telecommunications utility.


OVERVIEW: Appellant commission challenged the order of the circuit court that granted a property interest to respondent telecommunications utility in a federal exemption and reversed the commission's determination that respondent had consented to a competitor's entry into its service area. The appellant commission's appeal focused its argument on the court's property-right conclusion. The reviewing court held that any consideration of whether respondent had a constitutionally protected interest was premature and should not have been reached by the circuit court. The circuit court's ruling, with respect to respondent's constitutional argument, constituted obiter dicta and did not have legal or procedural effect. Therefore, the reviewing court affirmed the order insofar as it remanded the case to the commission for further hearings on the waiver/consent issue but reversed as to the premature ruling on the property interest claim.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order that granted a property interest to respondent telecommunications utility because the issue was not properly before the circuit court. The order was affirmed in part to remand the case to the commission for further hearings on respondent's consent to the entry of its competitors into its service area.

 

1012 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lo


No. 98-2490-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


228 Wis. 2d 531; 599 N.W.2d 659; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 574


April 13, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
May 27, 1999, Decided  
May 27, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: JOHN J. PERLICH, Judge. Affirmed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the terms of his probation provided by the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) after he was convicted of aggravated battery with intent to cause substantial bodily harm as a gang-related offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to aggravated battery with intent to cause substantial bodily harm as a gang-related offense and was convicted and placed on probation for ten years. The court imposed as a condition of probation a prohibition on defendant's having contact with gang members. Defendant challenged the probation condition, asserting that it was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The court affirmed the probation condition because the definition of gang members set forth in Wis. Stat. §§ 939.22(9), (9g), and 941.38(1)(b) were sufficiently specific to provide defendant with fair and adequate notice as to his expected course of conduct. The court held that the statutes provided an ascertainable standard for enforcement because the statutory definitions would not permit a violation to be found on individualized or arbitrary standards as to what constituted a gang member. The court found that the probation condition was not overbroad because it applied only to current gang members and to persons the defendant reasonably could be expected to know were members of a gang.


OUTCOME: Defendant's condition of probation was affirmed because the applicable statutes provided defendant with adequate notice of what constituted a gang member and set forth ascertainable standards for enforcement of the terms of defendant's probation. The court also found that the condition was not overbroad when given a reasonable construction.

 

1013 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Day


No. 98-3642-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


228 Wis. 2d 512; 597 N.W.2d 775; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 530



May 19, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: BRUCE K. SCHMIDT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgment of Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) convicting him of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and from an order denying his motion to suppress a blood alcohol test result obtained under Wisconsin's Implied Consent Law, Wis. Stat. § 343.305.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated contrary to Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a). At trial, defendant moved to suppress the chemical test result obtained under Wisconsin's Implied Consent Law, Wis. Stat. § 343.305, claiming that the test result violated his constitutional due process right to make an informed choice to either take or refuse the chemical test. His motion was denied. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. A prior decision of the Wisconsin Supreme Court, which was binding on the court, held that the right to refuse a blood alcohol test was simply a matter of statutory privilege and that the information required to be given drivers by Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4) satisfied due process requirements. Further, a Wisconsin driver had no choice with respect to granting his consent to take the chemical test. He was deemed by law to have already consented to submit to a test upon applying for and accepting a driver's license. Informing a Wisconsin driver that he might lose his driving privileges by refusing a chemical test was sufficient to satisfy due process under the United States and Wisconsin Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the order denying his motion to suppress the blood alcohol test. The right to refuse a blood alcohol test was simply a matter of statutory privilege and the information required to be given drivers by Wisconsin's Implied Consent Law satisfied due process requirements.

State v. Moen


No. 98-3679-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


228 Wis. 2d 512; 597 N.W.2d 775; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 518



May 18, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEAN W. DiMOTTO and RICHARD J. SANKOVITZ, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of driving while under the influence of an intoxicant and denied him postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: At his trial for driving while under the influence of an intoxicant, defendant requested a 12-person jury, but was tried before a 6-person jury. Defendant's counsel specifically stated that it was merely a request, not a constitutional challenge. Defendant was convicted and denied postconviction relief. The reviewing court found that the conviction was proper. While the statute mandating trial before a six-person jury, Wis. Stat. § 756.096(3)(am), was found to be unconstitutional, defendant was not entitled to review because, except for unusual circumstances, constitutional issues must be raised in the trial court before they will be considered on appeal. His trial was otherwise error-free, so the conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: A decision that convicted defendant of driving while under the influence of an intoxicant and denied him postconviction relief, was affirmed because he did not raise the constitutional issue of the size of the jury at trial.

Katzman v. State Ethics Bd.


No. 98-2884


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


228 Wis. 2d 282; 596 N.W.2d 861; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 495


February 26, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
May 6, 1999, Decided  
May 6, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B. O'BRIEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. Before Dykman, P.J., Eich and Deininger, JJ.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the granting of injunctive and declaratory relief by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), to plaintiff lobbyist and plaintiff wife. Plaintiffs had filed an action seeking such relief after defendants investigated them for possible violations of Wis. Stat. § 13.625(1)(c), which prohibited lobbyists from making contributions for partisan elective state office, except during specified periods.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff lobbyist was investigated by defendants for possible violations of Wis. Stat. § 13.625(1)(c), which prohibited lobbyists from making contributions to incumbents and candidates for partisan elective state office, except during a specified period preceding general elections. Plaintiff lobbyist's wife was not a lobbyist, but made several contributions to incumbents. Defendants issued subpoenas to plaintiffs requiring them to appear for a deposition and bring with them copies of checks issued for political contributions and check registers. Plaintiffs filed this action, seeking declaratory and injunctive relief, claiming that the board erred in interpretation of § 13.625(1)(c), asserting that the statute did not restrict plaintiff wife's contributions, and the investigation of plaintiff wife violated her constitutional rights. The lower court granted relief to plaintiffs, and defendants appealed. This court affirmed, holding that the lower court properly interpreted the statute to not apply to a political contribution made by a plaintiff wife from marital funds because the statute only prohibited activities by plaintiff lobbyist, not his wife.


OUTCOME: This court affirmed the granting of declaratory and injunctive relief to plaintiffs. The court held that the lower court properly interpreted the statute to not apply to political contributions made by plaintiff wife from marital funds because the statute only prohibited activities by plaintiff lobbyist, not his wife.

State v. Normington (In re Normington)


No. 98-1129


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


228 Wis. 2d 509; 597 N.W.2d 773; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 496



May 6, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied November 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7665.
Review denied by State v. Normington, 228 Wis. 2d 174, 602 N.W.2d 760, 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 208 (Wis., July 23, 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Normington v. Wisconsin, 528 U.S. 1013, 120 S. Ct. 517, 145 L. Ed. 2d 400, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7665 (Nov. 15, 1999)
Subsequent appeal at State v. Normington (In re Normington), 2002 WI App 56, 251 Wis. 2d 479, 640 N.W.2d 564, 2002 Wisc. App. LEXIS 51 (Jan. 17, 2002)
Decision reached on appeal by State v. Normington, 2017 Wisc. App. LEXIS 321 (Wis. Ct. App., Apr. 25, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Rock County: JAMES E. WELKER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, adjudged to be sexually violent, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), committing him to the health department for treatment.


OVERVIEW: After appellant sexually abused children, a jury found him sexually violent, and the trial court committed him to the custody of the health department. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not err in refusing to strike venirepersons where appellant did not show manifest bias on the part of the jurors and failed to question equivocal jurors before they were seated. The trial court, however, properly questioned the equivocal feelings of the venirepersons, who determined that they would be able to serve without prejudice. He also waived any objection to the venirepersons against whom he exercised preemptory challenges by not specifically naming them for review of impartiality. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting expert witness testimony based in part upon an improperly viewed presentence investigation report because the trial court's retroactive release of the report cured any error. Nor did the trial court err in admitting expert testimony based upon certain scientific conclusions because the validity of the expert's opinion did not affect its admissibility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of commitment; appellant did not prove that the seating of jurors who had previously expressed equivocal feelings caused manifest bias; appellant failed to specifically object to certain jurors; the admission of certain expert witness testimony was not an abuse of discretion.

Herek v. Police & Fire Comm'n


No. 98-1927


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


226 Wis. 2d 504; 595 N.W.2d 113; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 447


March 8, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
April 28, 1999, Decided  
April 28, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MARIANNE E. BECKER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police officer appealed, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 62.13(5)(i), an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County, (Wisconsin) upholding a disciplinary decision of defendant police and fire commission to terminate his employment, contending that defendant violated U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV in refusing to suppress his false responses to questions posed during an internal investigation and that defendant exceeded its jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff police officer was charged with violation of six general orders of the police department related to investigation of a crime. It was undisputed that plaintiff made false statements during a department's interview regarding the incident. At a disciplinary hearing before defendant police and fire commission, plaintiff sought to suppress those statements, which were the basis for a charge of untruthfulness. Plaintiff alleged that defendant did not have just cause under Wis. Stat. § 62.13(5)(em) for the imposed discipline and that defendant's decision to terminate his employment was unreasonable, arbitrary, capricious, and not supported by evidence. He also argued that defendant erred when it denied his motion to suppress based on the department's failure to provide him with warnings during his interview, pursuant to Garrity v. New Jersey, 385 U.S. 493, 17 L. Ed. 2d 562, 87 S. Ct. 616 (1967). The court affirmed the order upholding the disciplinary decision, concluding that the false statements made by plaintiff during the course of the police department's internal investigation were not entitled to immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order upholding the disciplinary decision, concluding that defendant proceeded on a correct theory of law and did not exceed its jurisdiction by terminating plaintiff. The court concluded that the false statements made by plaintiff during the course of the police department's internal investigation were not entitled to immunity.

 

1018 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Seidl


No. 98-2990-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


226 Wis. 2d 563; 596 N.W.2d 502; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 407



April 13, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ROBERT C. CRAWFORD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction upon a guilty plea for operating a motor vehicle after license revocation in violation of Wis. Stat. § 343.44(1) from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was arrested for operating a vehicle while intoxicated and with a revoked license, he pled guilty to the to the revocation charge and was acquitted by a jury of the intoxication charge. At defendant's sentencing, the trial judge considered evidence of defendant's blood alcohol level and the fact that he was driving while over the legal limit. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence, and the court affirmed. The court held that defendant's double jeopardy rights were not violated by the trial court's consideration during sentencing that he was driving while intoxicated even though he was acquitted of that charge. Consideration of evidence submitted at trial did not amount to a second prosecution. The court further held that defendant's due process rights were not violated by the trial court's use of evidence disclosed during the intoxication trial. Sentencing courts could consider all the facts and circumstances surrounding an offense and were not bound by rules of evidence. Further, sentencing courts were allowed to consider conduct for which a defendant was acquitted.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction upon a guilty plea of driving after license revocation was affirmed. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by considering evidence submitted during a trial on the driving while intoxicated charge, of which defendant was acquitted, during sentencing on the revocation charge.

 

1019 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lowery


No. 96-3568


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


226 Wis. 2d 561; 596 N.W.2d 501; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 389



April 6, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which adjudged respondent a sexually violent person and committed him to a secured facility for treatment, on the grounds that the evidence was insufficient to support the commitment and that Wis. Stat. ch. 980 was unconstitutionally applied to him.


OVERVIEW: Holding that the testimony of two doctors was sufficient evidence to sustain the commitment order and that Wis. Stat. ch. 980 was not constitutionally infirm, the court affirmed the order. The court held that in order to commit respondent, the state had to prove under Wis. Stat. § 980.02(2) that respondent had been convicted of a sexually violent offense, suffered from a mental disorder that predisposed him to engage in acts of sexual violence, and was dangerous to others because he had a mental disorder which created a substantial probability that he would engage in acts of sexual violence. The court noted the testimony of respondent's sexual sadism and antisocial personality disorder, and held that credibility determinations were for the trial court. The court held that Wis. Stat. ch. 980 did not violate double jeopardy or ex post facto safeguards because it was a civil, not criminal, proceeding imposing no punishment. The court also held that it, therefore, did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. The court further held that the fact that respondent entered an Alford plea to the underlying sex charge was sufficient to establish a conviction for ch. 980.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent's civil commitment as a sexually violent person because the psychiatrists' testimony, if believed, established that respondent was a mentally disturbed sexual sadist predisposed to committing further sexual assaults, and the credibility of the doctors was for the trial court. The court confirmed the constitutionality of the commitment laws in the face of respondent's ex post facto and double jeopardy challenges.

State v. McCain


No. 97-2119


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


226 Wis. 2d 158; 594 N.W.2d 418; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 362



March 30, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which committed defendant to a secure mental health facility as a sexual violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980, and denied his motion for postcommitment relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, following a court trial, was committed to a secure mental health facility as a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. ch. 980. He appealed his commitment along with an order denying his motion for postcommitment relief. The reviewing court affirmed and held that the lower court properly admitted expert testimony, even though the expert was not a licensed psychologist. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 938.35(1) did not bar the use of delinquency adjudications as evidence in the ch. 980 proceeding. The court also held that the evidence was sufficient to allow the assumption that a sexually violent person with "antisocial personality disorder" would engage in sexual violence in the future. This fact adequately satisfied the mental disorder criterion of the definition of "sexually violent person" under Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7). Moreover, the court held that § 980.01(7) was constitutional because "antisocial personality disorder" was not a vague or ambiguous term. Finally, the court held that plaintiff state's evidence was sufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that it was "substantially probable" that defendant would engage in acts of sexual violence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's commitment to a mental health facility because of his history of sexual violence, his diagnosis of "antisocial personality disorder," and the likelihood that he would commit further acts of sexual violence in the future.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which, following a jury trial, committed him to a secure mental health facility as a sexually violent person under Wis. OVERVIEW: Petitioner state sought to commit appellant as a sexually violent person pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980 because appellant had convictions for rape and sexual perversion; and, while on parole, appellant allegedly engaged in two acts of sexual misconduct. OUTCOME: The court found that there was sufficient evidence to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant would commit another sexually violent crime and that under Wisconsin law, he was properly committed as a sexually violent person. Accordingly the judgment of the trial court committing appellant to a secure mental health facility was affirmed.

State v. Davis


No. 97-3772-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


226 Wis. 2d 159; 594 N.W.2d 418; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 296



March 23, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Davis, 228 Wis. 2d 173, 602 N.W.2d 759, 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 175 (Wis., 1999)
Subsequent civil proceeding at Davis v. Milwaukee County, 225 F. Supp. 2d 967, 2002 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 19595 (E.D. Wis., 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Davis, 2014 Wisc. App. LEXIS 236 (Wis. Ct. App., Mar. 25, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of sexual assault of a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2). Defendant also appealed the denial of post-conviction relief. Among other claims, defendant argued that the complaint was vague and duplicitous and that the trial court made errors, including admitting other acts evidence and imposing an unduly harsh sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction for sexual assault of a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2) and the denial of post-conviction relief were affirmed. Defendant contended, among other claims, that the complaint was vague and duplicitous and that the trial court erred by admitting other acts evidence and imposing an unduly severe sentence. The appellate court held that the two-month time period in the complaint was sufficiently specific. Defendant was not denied his right to a unanimous verdict because the evidence described a pattern of conduct, and the jurors did not have to decide which act constituted the crime charged. The trial court did not abuse its discretion when it found that other crimes evidence regarding additional assaults on the victim was relevant to show motive, intent, and plan under Wis. Stat. § 904.04(2), and that the probative value was not substantially outweighed by unfair prejudice. When reference was made to defendant's first trial, the trial court properly considered the facts and arguments and offered a cautionary instruction. The record showed that the trial court considered the appropriate factors and did not abuse its discretion in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant of sexual assault of a child and an order denying post-conviction relief were affirmed. The complaint was sufficiently specific, and it was not duplicitous where the evidence described a pattern of conduct. Other crimes evidence involving other assaults on the victim was relevant to show motive, intent, and plan. The sentence was not an abuse of discretion.

State v. Byrge

Thorp v. Town of Lebanon


No. 98-2358


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


225 Wis. 2d 672; 593 N.W.2d 878; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 261


February 4, 1999, Submitted on Briefs  
March 11, 1999, Decided  
March 11, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: DANIEL W. KLOSSNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order from the circuit court for Dodge County (Wisconsin), in which the court dismissed plaintiffs' claims alleging a violation of plaintiffs' procedural and substantive due process rights and a violation of the equal protection clause.


OVERVIEW: The judgment dismissing plaintiffs' claims for a violation of plaintiffs' procedural and substantive due process rights and a violation of the equal protection clause was affirmed in part. In affirming the decision, the appeals court found that there was no procedural due process violation because plaintiffs had state remedies available to them. According to the appeals court, when a deprivation of property or liberty resulted from the random and unauthorized act of an official, procedural due process was satisfied if the state made available adequate post-deprivation remedies. The appeals court also held that substantive due process could not be read to include equal protection claims. In partially reversing the judgment, the appeals court found that plaintiffs did state a claim for relief under the equal protection clause. The appeals court held that if there was no suspect class or fundamental interest at stake, an ordinance violated the equal protection clause if the classifications were not rationally related to the asserted purpose of the ordinance. The appeals court found that plaintiffs' factual allegations were sufficient to state a claim for relief.


OUTCOME: The appeals court partially affirmed the dismissal of plaintiffs' procedural and substantive due process claims because plaintiffs had adequate state remedies available and because plaintiffs' substantive claims were the same as their equal protection claims. The appeals court partially reversed the judgment because plaintiffs' factual allegations stated an equal protection claim.

State v. Smith


No. 98-1426-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


226 Wis. 2d 160; 594 N.W.2d 419; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 246



March 9, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ROBERT C. CRAWFORD, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), convicting him following a jury trial of lewd and lascivious behavior contrary to Wis. Stat. § 944.20(2) (1993-94).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a prisoner housed at a county house of correction and confined to a solitary confinement cell. A female correctional officer went to defendant's cell to deliver some medication to him. Defendant made a gesture towards her regarding her breasts, stated that he had something for her, and exposed his penis practically hanging out of the cell. Defendant was convicted following a jury trial of lewd and lascivious behavior in violation of Wis. Stat. § 944.20(2) (1993-94), criminal damage to property, and habitual criminality. Defendant's postconviction motion was denied. Defendant appealed his conviction of lewd and lascivious behavior, asserting that the state failed to prove that he committed the crime publicly and that the officer observed him voluntarily because she was under a duty to observe him in her capacity as a correctional officer. The court affirmed, holding that defendant committed the crime publicly because defendant was well aware of the officer's presence and that she could observe his behavior, and the officer did not observe defendant in her official capacity as a correctional officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of lewd and lascivious behavior, holding that defendant committed the crime publicly because he was well aware that the officer was present and could observe his behavior, and the officer did not observe defendant in her official capacity as a correctional officer.

 

1026 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Collins v. Morgan


No. 98-0689


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


224 Wis. 2d 936; 592 N.W.2d 318; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 179



February 11, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: ROBERT DECHAMBEAU, Judge.
Collins v. State, 91 Wis. 2d 848, 284 N.W.2d 120, 1979 Wisc. App. LEXIS 3343 (Wis. Ct. App., 1979)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granting defendant prison officials' motion for summary judgment and dismissing plaintiff's claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for declaratory relief and monetary damages based on alleged violations of his procedural due process rights at his prison disciplinary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff inmate brought an action for declaratory relief and monetary damages against defendant prison officials under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 alleging violations of his procedural due process rights at a prison disciplinary hearing. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment and dismissed plaintiff's claim, and plaintiff appealed. On appeal, defendants contended that plaintiff's claim was not cognizable under § 1983 because a judgment in his favor would require recalculation of his good time credits. The court agreed and affirmed the trial court's order on this basis. The court explained that when a state prisoner sought damages in a § 1983 suit, the court was required to consider whether a judgment in favor of the plaintiff would necessarily imply the invalidity of his conviction or sentence. If it would, the complaint was to be dismissed unless the plaintiff could demonstrate that the conviction or sentence had already been invalidated. Plaintiff's claim for damages based on allegations of deceit and bias on the part of defendants necessarily implied the invalidity of the punishment imposed. Thus, the claim was not cognizable under § 1983.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted defendants' motion for summary judgment and dismissed plaintiff's claim under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because a judgment in favor of plaintiff's claim would have necessarily implied the invalidity of plaintiff's sentence.

Conservatorship of Prom v. Sumitomo Rubber Indus.


No. 98-0938


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


224 Wis. 2d 743; 592 N.W.2d 657; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 169


December 7, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
February 10, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Ozaukee County: THOMAS R. WOLFGRAM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff conservator sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Ozaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed plaintiff's defective tire complaint against defendant manufacturer for lack of personal jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff motorcyclist was severely injured in an accident, declared incompetent, and placed in a conservatorship. Plaintiff conservator brought suit against defendant manufacturer, a Japanese corporation, claiming that the accident happened because of a defective tire. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss. The court affirmed. Plaintiff failed to achieve proper service on defendant, and thus the trial court lacked personal jurisdiction over defendant. Plaintiff had not served defendant within the sixty-day period required by Wis. Stat. § 801.02. Contrary to plaintiff's assertion, Hague Convention art. 15 did not provide a six-month time limit, or any time limit, for service of process. Because the Hague Convention did not expressly state a time period for service of process to be completed, it did not conflict with Wis. Stat. § 801.02. Thus, the trial court properly applied Wis. Stat. § 801.02. Further, plaintiff's service of process on the secretary of state pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 180.847(4) was improper because defendant lacked sufficient contacts with the state and thus was not a foreign corporation transacting business in the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that dismissed a defective tire suit by plaintiff conservator against defendant manufacturer, a Japanese corporation, for lack of personal jurisdiction. Plaintiff had not complied with the sixty-day limit for service of process mandated by state law, and the relevant article of the Hague Convention did not preempt the applicable state law.

State v. Wanta


No. 98-0318-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


224 Wis. 2d 679; 592 N.W.2d 645; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 134


November 11, 1998, Submitted on Briefs

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Wanta, 225 Wis. 2d 490, 594 N.W.2d 384, 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 911 (Wis., 1999)
Related proceeding at Wanta v. Wis. Dep't of Revenue, 2005 Wisc. App. LEXIS 993 (Wis. Ct. App., Nov. 15, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Dane County: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him for intentionally filing fraudulent individual income tax returns, with the intent to evade income tax in violation of Wis. Stat. § 71.83(2)(b)(1), and intentionally concealing property upon which levy was authorized, with the intent to evade collection of taxes in violation of Wis. Stat. § 71.83(2)(b)(3).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for intentionally filing false and fraudulent income tax returns and concealing property with the intent to evade taxation under Wis. Stat. §§ 71.83(2)(b)(1), 71.83(2)(b)(3). Defendant appealed the conviction. He claimed that Wis. Stat. § 971.14(4)(b) unconstitutionally required proof of incompetence by clear and convincing evidence when an accused claimed to be competent, evidence did not support conviction, venue was improper, certain jury instructions denied him a fair trial, he was denied effective assistance of counsel, he was denied counsel of his choice, and he paid the amount owed. State v. Hart


No. 98-2321-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


224 Wis. 2d 938; 592 N.W.2d 319; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 127



February 2, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL J. BARRON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), entering judgment of conviction of receiving stolen property in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.34(1)(a), and habitual criminality under Wis. Stat. § 939.62.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with receiving stolen property under Wis. Stat. § 943.34(1)(a), and habitual criminality under Wis. Stat. § 939.62. The evidence showed that a security officer stopped defendant, who was walking through an apartment parking lot with a bundle on his shoulder, and asked him where he was going and what the bundle contained. Defendant said that he had been in an apartment, but he could not give the names of any residents, and said that he was carrying laundry. The officer, feeling objects in the bundle, searched and found home entertainment equipment. Defendant then attempted to escape. The trial court convicted defendant. On appeal, the court affirmed. The evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction as defendant's evasiveness and escape attempt supported a conclusion that defendant knew the property was stolen. Defendant failed to prove that § 943.34(1)(a) established a presumption that one carrying concealing property knew that the property was stolen; the statute was thus constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of receipt of stolen property and habitual criminality; the evidence supported the jury's finding that defendant knew that the objects he carried were stolen, and the statute outlawing receipt of stolen property was constitutional.

 

1030 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harvey


Nos. 98-2578-CR, 98-2579-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


224 Wis. 2d 645; 590 N.W.2d 283; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 111



January 28, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Juneau County: JOHN W. BRADY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Juneau County (Wisconsin), which convicted him, after a six-person jury trial under Wis. Stat. § 756.096(3)(am), of operating a motor vehicle after revocation. The court also denied defendant's petition for postconviction relief. Defendant argued that he should have been granted a new trial, because the Wisconsin Supreme Court declared that § 756.096(3)(am) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted, by a six-person jury pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 756.096(3)(am), of operating a motor vehicle after revocation. The trial court denied defendant's petition for postconviction relief. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred when it refused to grant him a new trial, because the Wisconsin Supreme Court declared in State v. Hansford, 219 Wis. 2d 226, 230, 580 N.W.2d 171, 173 (1998), that § 756.096(3)(am) was unconstitutional. Defendant also argued that his trial counsel was ineffective for not requesting a 12-person jury. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision and held that defendant waived his right to a 12-person jury and that defendant did not establish his trial counsel's failure to request a 12-person jury was outside the range of professionally competent assistance. The court found that defendant provided no support for his claim that the right to a 12-person jury was a fundamental right that needed to be personally waived by defendant. The court also found that the supreme court did not even accept certification of the issue of the constitutionality of § 756.096(3)(am) until over a month after defendant's trial.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's petition for postconviction relief after his conviction of operating a motor vehicle after revocation. The court held that defendant waived his right to a 12-person jury. The court also held that defendant failed to establish that his trial counsel's failure to request a 12-person jury was outside the range of professionally competent assistance.

 

1031 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Farr


No. 96-2551-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


224 Wis. 2d 641; 590 N.W.2d 281; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 115



January 28, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6321.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: WILLIAM D. JOHNSTON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Dane County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of using a dangerous weapon and extortion, Wis. Stat. §§ 939.63 and 943.30(1), for brandishing a rifle before two electric company workers, who were disconnecting his service for non-payment, and telling them they should reconnect the service, following a verdict in his favor in involuntary mental commitment proceedings.


OVERVIEW: When two electric company workers came out to his house to disconnect his service for non-payment, defendant carried his rifle over to them and said, "If I were you, I would hook that back up." The workers then left immediately. Soon thereafter, proceedings were commenced to involuntarily commit defendant for mental illness. When a verdict was entered for defendant, criminal proceedings were commenced. Defendant was charged with using a dangerous weapon and extortion, Wis. Stat. §§ 939.63 and 943.30(1), but his first trial ended in a hung jury. When he was convicted on re-trial, he appealed. In affirming, the court ruled, inter alia, that the prosecution was not barred by double jeopardy because the commitment proceedings were civil in nature. Claims of prosecutorial vindictiveness were waived because defendant did not raise these issues prior to trial. Moreover, his actions and statements were sufficient to sustain the charges and convictions, even though his threat was implied, and it was no defense, under Wis. Stat. § 939.14, that the workers may have been trespassing. Issues raised by defendant for the first time in a pro se reply brief were not considered.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed because double jeopardy did not preclude prosecution following civil commitment proceedings; claims of prosecutorial vindictiveness were waived since they were not raised before trial; defendant's actions were sufficient to support conviction, even though his threat was subtle; the workers' trespass on his property was not a defense; and issues raised for first time in his pro se reply brief would not be considered.

 

1032 of 2046 DOCUMENTS



State v. Hagenkord (In re Hagenkord)


No. 97-0841


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


224 Wis. 2d 641; 590 N.W.2d 281; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 8



January 12, 1999, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent appellant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), where he was adjudged a sexually violent person in a commitment action brought pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980. Respondent had been convicted for a sexually violent offense against a child.


OVERVIEW: Respondent appellant challenged an order adjudging him a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. § 980 and requiring him to be committed to institutional care. He also appealed from an order denying his motion to reconsider the commitment order. He claimed: (1) the state improperly used expert testimony as a conduit to adduce inadmissible hearsay; (2) the evidence was insufficient to support a § 980 commitment; (3) the trial court denied him the right to the least restrictive setting for serving the commitment; and (4) § 980 was unconstitutionally applied to him. The appellate court affirmed and held that expert testimony was not offered for the truth of the matter asserted. Testimony was admissible for a limited purpose and not for its substantive value. There was sufficient evidence to support the commitment, and determining respondent's proper placement under Wis. Stat. § 980.06 involved a discretionary act. The trial court did not abuse its discretion. Because he was a danger to his community, his equal protection argument failed. Due process only required his commitment to bear a reasonable relationship to the purpose for which he was committed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the decisions of the trial court in the state's commitment action against respondent because expert testimony was properly admitted, there was sufficient evidence to support the commitment, the trial court did not err in its placement decision, and the commitment statute was not unconstitutional as applied to respondent.


 

1033 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Hanson v. Prudential Prop. & Cas. Ins. Co.


No. 98-0692


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


224 Wis. 2d 356; 591 N.W.2d 619; 1999 Wisc. App. LEXIS 21


December 1, 1998, Oral Argument  
January 12, 1999, Decided  
January 12, 1999, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Polk County: ROBERT H. RASMUSSEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed from a grant of summary judgment from the circuit court for Polk County (Wisconsin), which declared that plaintiff insured was an underinsured motorist pursuant to a damages basis definition of underinsured motorist set forth in a automobile liability policy for a prior coverage period.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff insured was involved in an automobile accident and he entered into a settlement with the other driver. Plaintiff demanded underinsured motorist benefits from defendant insurer. Defendant denied plaintiff's demand and claimed that plaintiff did not meet the definition of underinsured motorist under the current policy, although plaintiff did meet the definition of underinsured motorist under a prior policy. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 631.36(5) required that when defendant offered to renew a policy on new, less favorable terms, the defendant must have informed plaintiff that the new terms did not become effective until 60 days after the renewal was sent and that plaintiff had a corresponding 60 days within which to have elected to renew or cancel the policy. Because defendant's right to cancel notice did not provide this information, it was insufficient and defendant was required to continue the policy for an additional period of time equivalent to the expiring policy. Grant of summary judgment that declared plaintiff an underinsured motorist was affirmed. However, the lower court erred when it determined that plaintiff could stack his underinsured motorist benefits.


OUTCOME: Grant of summary judgment that held that plaintiff insured was an underinsured motorist pursuant to a damages basis definition of an underinsured motorist set forth in a automobile liability policy was affirmed because defendant insurer failed to give the statutorily required notices to the insured. However the portion of the judgment allowing plaintiff to stack his underinsured coverage was reversed.

Hull v. Medical Assocs. of Menomonee Falls


No. 97-1246


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


223 Wis. 2d 798; 589 N.W.2d 454; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1468



December 29, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: WILLIAM J. HAESE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant health care providers appealed a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which awarded damages to plaintiffs, patient's estate, husband, and child, in plaintiffs' medical malpractice action. Plaintiffs cross-appealed from that portion of the judgment denying plaintiffs double costs and interest.


OVERVIEW: The trial court concluded that defendant health care providers were causally negligent for a patient's death in that they misdiagnosed the patient's colorectal cancer. Defendants appealed, contending that the trial court failed to consider the patient's contributory negligence, that the statute of limitations barred the medical malpractice action, and that defendants were entitled to a jury trial. The court reversed the judgment that awarded damages to plaintiffs, patient's estate, husband, and child, and remanded the case for a new trial on the issue of liability and damages because the trial court's decision contained several factual inaccuracies and the trial court failed to address the material issue of contributory negligence even though there were facts suggesting that the patient had not taken responsibility for her own well-being. The court held that plaintiffs' action was timely filed under Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1), because under the continuum negligent care doctrine, a cause of action did not accrue until the date of defendants' last negligent act or omission. The court concluded that defendants waived their right to a jury trial by not timely paying the jury fee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment rendered against defendant health care providers and remanded the case for a new trial because the trial court failed to address defendants' contention that patient was contributorily negligent. The court held that the trial court did not err in ruling that the action was timely filed under the continuum of negligent treatment doctrine and that defendants had waived their right to a jury trial.

Sheehy v. Kraler


No. 98-1619


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


223 Wis. 2d 802; 589 N.W.2d 456; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1439



December 23, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 (3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Manitowoc County: PATRICK L. WILLIS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor and hospital appealed from an order of the circuit court of Manitowoc County (Wisconsin), which denied defendants' motion to dismiss a medical malpractice action brought by plaintiff patient and family. Defendants claimed that the action was barred by the statute of limitations and repose in Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant doctor at defendant hospital examined a biopsy of a growth on the body of the plaintiff patient, and misdiagnosed what was a malignant melanoma as a benign tumor. More than five years later, a new biopsy was performed, the misdiagnosis was discovered, and it was determined that the melanoma had metastasized to plaintiff patient's lymph nodes. Six years later, plaintiff patient was diagnosed with malignant melanoma and commenced the action against defendants for medical malpractice. The trial court rejected defendants' claim that the action was barred by the statute of limitations and repose in, and denied defendants' motion to dismiss. On appeal the court reversed. When the misdiagnosis and the development of metastatic cancer was first discovered it was reasonably clear that the misdiagnosis would result in future expenses. At that time plaintiff patient suffered injury for which he had a claim. Accordingly, the action was time barred under Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1)(b) because it was not brought within one year of the date when injury was discovered.


OUTCOME: The order denying the motion to dismiss of defendant doctor and hospital was reversed. The action was time barred because it was brought more than one year after plaintiff patient first discovered injury from defendants' earlier misdiagnosis of a malignant melanoma.

Vincent v. Voight

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


223 Wis. 2d 799; 589 N.W.2d 455; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1447



December 23, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRESEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.

The circuit court held that the current public school funding system was constitutional and did not deny basic education to all.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, school districts, parents, students, and taxpayers, and intervening plaintiffs, education counsel, teachers, and administrators, challenged the constitutionality of Wisconsin's public school funding system, arguing that the state's equalization formula failed to adequately address the substantial disparity in resource levels for various districts, and that it failed to take into account the differing needs of certain children, who were disproportionately located in lower property value districts. Defendants, state treasurer, state superintendent, and department of revenue, and plaintiffs moved for summary judgment. The circuit court granted defendants' motion on the basis that plaintiffs failed to provide the statistical evidence to prove that the current system created greater disparities among lower and higher property value districts than existed when an earlier case was decided by the supreme court. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision, finding that plaintiff failed to objectively establish that the disparities were greater than the disparities in the earlier decided case and that certain children were being denied a basic education.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for defendants, state treasurer, state superintendent, and department of revenue. The court held that plaintiffs, school districts, parents, students, and taxpayers, failed to establish that children were being denied a basic education. For the court to find the finance system unconstitutional, when the supreme court found a similar system to be constitutional, evidence of greater disparities was needed.
