State v. Trevino


No. 97-1748-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


223 Wis. 2d 799; 589 N.W.2d 454; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1448



December 23, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dodge County: JOHN STORCK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) for three counts of second degree sexual assault of a child arguing that his Sixth Amendment right to effective assistance of counsel was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his judgment of conviction for second degree sexual assault of a child. Defendant argued that his right to effective assistance of counsel was violated because his trial counsel did not properly impeach the state's primary witness. In analyzing an ineffective assistance of counsel claim, the first element of the Strickland test required defendant to show that counsel's performance was deficient, that counsel made such serious errors he or she was not functioning as the counsel guaranteed defendant by the Sixth Amendment. The child testified that defendant assaulted her in the morning on Easter Sunday. At trial, however, the child did not explicitly specify the day of the assault as Easter Sunday and defendant's trial counsel did not ask the exact date or attempt to impeach her less precise trial testimony with that of the preliminary hearing. Defendant's conviction was affirmed because assistance of counsel did not fall below the conduct of a reasonably competent attorney where such an attempt to impeach the child may have resulted in the district attorney rehabilitating her by highlighting the large number of assaults that occurred over the years.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for second degree sexual assault of child was affirmed because defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective when counsel failed to impeach the child witness as the decision was strategically made to assist defendant's defense.

Management Computer Servs., Inc. v. Hawkins, Ash, Baptie & Co.


No. 97-2470, 98-1384


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


224 Wis. 2d 312; 592 N.W.2d 279; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1486


November 11, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
December 17, 1998, Decided  
December 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Management Computer Servs. v. Hawkins, Ash, Baptie & Co., 225 Wis. 2d 490, 594 N.W.2d 384, 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 937 (Wis., 1999)
Review denied by Management Computer Servs. v. Hawkins, Ash, Baptie, 225 Wis. 2d 488, 594 N.W.2d 383, 1999 Wisc. LEXIS 870 (Wis., 1999)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: STEVEN L. ABBOTT, Judge. APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: STEVEN L. ABBOTT, Judge.
Management Computer Servs. v. Hawkins, Ash, Baptie & Co., 206 Wis. 2d 158, 557 N.W.2d 67, 1996 Wisc. LEXIS 115 (Wis., 1996)



DISPOSITION: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL Affirmed in part and reversed in part. APPEAL Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff provider instituted an action for breach of contract against defendant customer. A jury awarded the provider damages. The parties appealed the decision of the circuit court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which granted the customer's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict on two claims, and reduced the amount of punitive damages awarded by the jury.


OVERVIEW: The customer contended that the provider was not entitled to interest on the breach of contract damages or the punitive damages from the time of the verdict to the entry of judgment. The court held that when the verdict was reinstated, interest under Wis. Stat. § 814.04(4), accrued from the date of the original verdict regardless of whether the trial court had set aside the verdict by granting a motion for a new trial or one for JNOV. Therefore, the court held that, under the circumstances, it was not inappropriate for the customer to bear the cost of the delay in the provider's receipt of the damages to which it was entitled by virtue of the jury's verdict. The court also held that although it may well have been within the trial court's discretion to award costs on the customer's counterclaim, the trial court did not do so. The court concluded that the trial court's award of costs under the mistaken belief that it was bound by the earlier assessment of costs for the retrial of punitive damages, was erroneous. Therefore, the court reversed the offset allowed in the judgment for costs and interest in favor of the customer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court with respect to the offset for costs and interest and otherwise affirmed the decision of the trial court granting the customer's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict on two claims, and reducing the amount of punitive damages awarded by the jury.

Willow Creek Ranch v. Town of Shelby


No. 97-2075, No. 98-0138


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


224 Wis. 2d 269; 592 N.W.2d 15; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1416


October 14, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
December 10, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for La Crosse County: DENNIS G. MONTABON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff game farm filed two separate suits in the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) against the defendants town and county, and in the second suit the farm added two insurers as defendants. The farm sought declaratory relief and damages for the denial of a change in zoning. The court granted the defendants' motions for summary judgment dismissing both suits. The farm appealed.


OVERVIEW: The farm wished to maintain a bird hunting area. The farm argued, inter alia, that the trial court had erred by granting summary judgment because: (1) game farm regulation was within the exclusive province of the department of natural resources (DNR) and, therefore, not subject to the town and county's regulation; and (2) immunity did not apply because the town and county were engaged in ministerial acts, not discretionary acts. The court of appeals held that the trial court had not erred because: (1) for the farm to operate a game bird farm in the county, it needed to obtain both the necessary permit from the DNR and the necessary zoning approval from the county board, and it failed to obtain the latter; and (2) the DNR's authority to issue a permit for the operation of a game farm was separate from the town and county's authority to create and enforce zoning ordinances, therefore, the town and county did not exceed their authority, nor were they acting ministerially when they elected to enforce the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Faken


No. 98-1974


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


223 Wis. 2d 803; 589 N.W.2d 457; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1407



December 9, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23(3) OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: TIMOTHY M. VAN AKKEREN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin) denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence from a warrantless stop for operating a vehicle with an excessively loud muffler in violation of Wis. Stat. § 347.39. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that defendant's motion to suppress should have been granted. The officer's meager and conclusory testimony did not demonstrate articulable facts to support his opinion that the vehicle was emitting noise disruptive enough to be classified as "excessive or unusual" pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 347.39(1). The officer gave no testimony that he knew what the standard was for a reasonable, usual, or normal amount of noise. Nor was there evidence to show that the muffler on defendant's car was not factory installed, that the officer knew what a "legal" muffler for defendant's type of vehicle sounded like and that the installed muffler was louder, or that defendant ever confirmed that his muffler was excessively loud. Further, the officer did not testify about the approximate distance at which he heard defendant's vehicle, how long the car was audible upon approach and passing, or if the car could be heard with his window up.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

State v. Shaw


No. 98-1396


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


226 Wis. 2d 160; 594 N.W.2d 419; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1394



December 8, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Marinette County: DENNIS J. MLEZIVA, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a civil commitment petition alleging that defendant was dangerous because he suffered from the mental disorder of pedophilia. Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Marinette County (Wisconsin), which required his civil commitment as a sexually violent person and denied his postjudgment motions.


OVERVIEW: The trial court accepted the State's experts' definition of "substantially probable" as "more likely than not," and concluded that defendant suffered from the mental disorder of pedophilia and was dangerous to others because he presented a substantial probability of committing future acts of sexual violence. After the trial court's decision in this case, the court rejected an argument that "substantially probable" meant "extreme likelihood" and concluded that "substantially probable" in Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7), meant "considerably more likely to occur than not to occur." Accordingly, the court reversed and remanded the action to the trial court for its determination under the new standard.The court also held that the trial court erroneously concluded that Wis. Stat. § 908.03(6), allowed the presentence investigation reports (PSI) to be admitted in toto because the presentence investigation reports contained statements by declarants who were not part of the, the organization that prepared the record. Therefore, the court held that the trial court should consider whether to waive the confidentiality of the PSI reports.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court reversed and remanded this case to the trial court for its determination whether it was substantially probable that defendant would engage in sexual violence and to consider whether to waive the confidentiality of the PSI reports.

1044 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. City of Oak Creek


No. 97-2188


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


223 Wis. 2d 219; 588 N.W.2d 380; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1351


September 29, 1998, Oral Argument  
November 24, 1998, Decided  
November 24, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CHRISTOPHER R. FOLEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which concluded that Wis. Stat. § 30.056 (1995-1996) was unconstitutional and granted summary judgment in favor plaintiff state.


OVERVIEW: In a prior action, the court concluded that the city's channelization of a creek violated § 30.12 and that § 30.055, which purported to exempt the creek from the requirements of § 30.12 was unconstitutional. However, after that decision the legislature re-enacted the exemption through § 30.056. The state, through its attorney general, brought an action against the city and challenged the constitutionality of § 30.056. The trial court found in favor of the state and the city appealed. On appeal, the court reversed the decision of the trial court. The court found that the attorney general qualified as "any person" under § 30.294. However, the attorney general could not challenge the constitutionality of § 30.056 because it was his job to defend the statute. Wis. Const. art. VI, § 3 set the scope of the attorney general's authority. The attorney general had no powers other than those specified by the legislature. The attorney general was not authorized to make the constitutional challenge because it was not one of his official duties. Although § 30.294 permitted the attorney general to abate what he considered was a nuisance, he could not assert that § 30.056 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court in favor of the state.

 

1045 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kirchhuebel


No. 98-1258


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


223 Wis. 2d 268; 588 N.W.2d 929; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1317



November 12, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Jefferson County: JOHN M. ULLSVIK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin) which declared unlawful his refusal to submit to a test for intoxication under Wis. Stat. § 343.305.


OVERVIEW: After police stopped defendant's vehicle, the officer requested that defendant perform field sobriety tests and submit to a breath test. Defendant was unable to give a sufficient sampled and refused to take a second test. The trial court found that defendant's refusal to take the breath test was unlawful. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. Defendant contended that he was unable to submit to the breath test because he was missing several lower teeth. A physical inability to take a breath test was the only proper basis on which a driver could refuse to take the test. The trial court's determination that defendant did not meet his burden of establishing that he was physically unable, due to a disease or disability, of providing a breath sample could not be disturbed on appeal unless that finding was clearly erroneous. The trial court's finding here was not clearly erroneous because defendant did prove by a preponderance of the evidence that the absence of lower teeth prevented him from giving a breath sample. Rather, the evidence showed that defendant was playing games and was uncooperative during the attempted testing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that found defendant's refusal to submit to a breath test was unlawful.

City of Milwaukee v. Mohammand


No. 97-2382

November 10, 1998, Released

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: VICTOR MANIAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), entered an order affirming a municipal court's dismissal of appellant city's complaints against appellee building operator for alleged violations of the city's building code. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The building operator was the operator of two residential buildings. The city filed two complaints against him for building code violations at those two buildings. The complaints summoned him to appear before the municipal court and answer the complaints. He failed to appear. The municipal court entered default judgments for the city. The building owner moved to vacate the default judgments. He appeared before the municipal court and asserted both that he was not liable for the violations because he was not the owner of the buildings and that he was never served with the complaints. The municipal court concluded no common law nor statutory authority existed for holding a building operator liable for building code violations and that city ordinances purporting to be the basis for liability were invalid because they conflicted with a state statute. After the trial court affirmed, the appellate court found the state statute did not apply to the city, and thus, the city ordinances could be used to impose liability on the building operator. The case was sent back to the municipal court to determine whether the building owner was properly served.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded.

 

1047 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adams (In re Adams)


No. 96-3136


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


223 Wis. 2d 60; 588 N.W.2d 336; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1304


July 21, 1998, Oral Argument  
November 10, 1998, Decided  
November 10, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MAXINE A. WHITE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State alleged that defendant was a sexually violent person eligible for commitment under Wis. Stat. § 980 and so petitioned. The trial court dismissed the petition. The appellate court reversed and remanded. The Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), after a jury trial, committed defendant to a secure mental health facility as a sexually violent person. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant moved the trial court in limine to preclude reference to his assertion of his Fifth Amendment privilege to remain silent in regard to a psychologist who did an examination that relied on reports of others, without a personal interview. Defendant also sought to be allowed to challenge the examination precisely because the doctor failed to interview him. The appellate court held because defendant challenged the doctor and his examination for the failure to interview, the trial court correctly allowed the State to elicit the doctor's testimony about the refusal so as to rebut the implication that the doctor's examination was thus improper. Diagnosis of "antisocial personality disorder," uncoupled with any other diagnosis but coupled with sufficient evidence establishing that defendant was a "sexually violent person," could constitute a mental disorder that made it substantially probable that the person would engage in acts of sexual violence, under Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7). In allowing "antisocial personality disorder" to meet the "mental disorder" criterion, § 980.01(7) was sufficiently precise to satisfy due process. Reference to a past charge did not warrant mistrial.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Block


No. 97-3265-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


222 Wis. 2d 586; 587 N.W.2d 914; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1255


September 25, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
October 28, 1998, Decided  
October 28, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Winnebago County: THOMAS S. WILLIAMS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) that convicted him as a persistent repeater for assault by a prisoner.


OVERVIEW: While incarcerated defendant attacked a social worker after she informed him that he was being moved to another institution. Defendant was charged as a persistent offender under Wis. Stat. § 939.62(2m)(b) and convicted of assault by a prisoner. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. The persistent repeater statute at § 939.62(2m)(b) did not violate the Equal Protection Clause because the legislature's classification of what constituted a serious felony was rationally related to the legislature's function of determining penalties for crimes. It was entirely within the legislature's power to classify crimes, recognize different degrees of harm that resulted from them, and decide which more urgently needed repression. The court further found that there was sufficient evidence to prove all of the elements of assault by a prisoner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant as a persistent repeated for assault by a prisoner.

 

1049 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Doyle v. Arthur


No. 97-3353


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


222 Wis. 2d 624; 587 N.W.2d 457; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1233



October 22, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Juneau County: JOHN W. BRADY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant attorney landowner appealed from an order of the circuit court for Juneau County (Wisconsin) granting the motion of plaintiff neighboring property owner for default judgment and awarding compensatory damages for restoration costs and punitive damages for actions of the attorney in harvesting trees on his land and that of the neighbor.


OVERVIEW: The attorney entered into a contract to have trees removed from his property, and misled the loggers as to a property line, so that they caused substantial damage to the neighbor's property. The court noted that after an order denying the attorney's motion to dismiss the neighbor's complaint, under Wis. Stat. § 802.06(1) he then had ten days after that date in which to file an answer, which he failed to do. His "answer," and the documents with which he inundated the trial court, not only fail the test of timeliness, but were equally lacking in both form and substance and failed to comply with Wis. Stat. § 802.02(2). The neighbor alleged that the attorney's acts were undertaken in wanton and reckless disregard of her rights and interests, and the court ruled the allegations were sufficient, under Wisconsin's notice-pleading rules, to state a punitive damage claim. The record indicated that the neighbor not only suffered the loss of the trees, but the improper cutting of the logging road through her property caused ecological damage, erosion problems, and changes to the watershed, so there was no error in the trial court's award of compensatory damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the default entered against the attorney landowner, as well as the compensatory and punitive damages awarded for the trespass to his neighbor's land and the removal of trees and vegetation.

 

1050 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Mauston Sch. Dist.


No. 97-1874


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


222 Wis. 2d 540; 588 N.W.2d 305; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1239


August 26, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
October 22, 1998, Decided  
October 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Juneau County: JOHN W. BRADY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff survivors sought review after the Circuit Court for Juneau County (Wisconsin) granted defendant agency's motion for summary judgment in an action for wrongful death, which the survivors had filed against the agency, defendant school district, and defendant insurer. The survivors had settled their claims against the school district.


OVERVIEW: The survivors had alleged wrongful death in their complaints. The decedent was a student in the school district who had been enrolled in a special education program that was run in part by the agency. The trial court consolidated the actions. The agency filed a motion for summary judgment, contending that the survivors had not filed a notice of claim with the attorney general under Wis. Stat. § 893.82(3). The trial court granted the motion. The court reversed and remanded. The notice of claim requirement in § 893.82(3) did not apply because the agency was not a state officer, employee, or agent within the meaning of § 893.82(3). A state "agent" in § 893.82(3) meant an individual and did not mean a state "agency." Even if the complaints had been amended to name an officer, employee or agent of the agency as a defendant, § 893.82(3) still would have been inapplicable because the agency was not a state agency, but was rather a governmental subdivision or agency thereof within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 893.80(1).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the agency and remanded with directions.

 

1051 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of Jefferson v. Renz


No. 97-3512


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


222 Wis. 2d 424; 588 N.W.2d 267; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1203


July 27, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
October 15, 1998, Decided  
October 15, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: JOHN ULLSVIK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction for driving while under the influence of an intoxicant and with a prohibited alcohol concentration from the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), arguing that the statute regulating mufflers, Wis. Stat. § 347.39, violated due process and Wis. Stat. § 343.303 required probable cause to arrest before an officer requested a breath sample for a preliminary breath test.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving while under the influence of an intoxicant after an officer stopped him because of a loud sound of exhaust emitting from defendant's vehicle. Based on a subsequent blood test, defendant was also charged with driving with a prohibited alcohol concentration. In reversing the trial court's judgment of conviction, the court concluded that the muffler statute was not unconstitutionally vague and therefore the officer's detention of defendant for a violation of that statute was proper. Also, the court concluded that Wis. Stat. § 343.303 required probable cause to arrest before administration of the preliminary breath test. The officer, however, did not have probable cause to arrest defendant before asking him to provide a breath sample because instances of unsteadiness during field sobriety tests, when considered in the context of all the evidence, were minimal and did not demonstrate that there was more than a possibility that defendant was under the influence of an intoxicant to the degree that made him incapable of driving safely. Thus, the results of the test were not admissible at the hearing on defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress the results of a preliminary breath test and reversed defendant's judgment of conviction for driving while under the influence of an intoxicant and with a prohibited alcohol concentration.

State v. Eagans


Nos. 97-2508 & 98-0837


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


222 Wis. 2d 217; 587 N.W.2d 214; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1118



September 29, 1998, Released

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from orders of the circuit court for Brown County: WILLIAM C. GRIESBACH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, sex offender, challenged the orders of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin) finding him to be a sexually violent person, and denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The sex offender argued that the trial court erred because he received ineffective assistance of counsel, claiming that his trial counsel failed to: (1) challenge Wis. Stat. ch. 980 as unconstitutional when commitment was based on an adjudication of delinquency; (2) fully investigate and develop the evidence an expert witness presented; (3) argue that an antisocial personality disorder was not a sufficiently precise category for a person to be subject to a ch. 980 commitment; (4) challenge the term "substantially probable" as vague; (5) argue that ch. 980 violated the ex post facto clauses of the Wisconsin and United States Constitutions; and (6) challenge ch. 980 as unconstitutional and by violating his equal protection right. State v. Behm

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


222 Wis. 2d 220; 587 N.W.2d 215; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1124

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Oneida County: ROBERT E. KINNEY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Oneida County (Wisconsin) convicting and sentencing him for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred when it relied on two prior "uncounseled" civil forfeiture OWI convictions to subject him to prosecution and punishment as a third-time OWI offender. This reliance, defendant contended, violated his due process and equal protection rights. The appellate court rejected his arguments because: (1) defendant's conviction as a third-time OWI offender based upon two prior offenses, albeit noncriminal offenses, was consistent with his status as a third-time offender; (2) his sentence properly reflected the legislature's goal of increasing criminal sanctions for repeat drunk drivers; and (3) the fact that defendant was not represented by counsel for his first offense and possibly the second offense did not render those convictions defective.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

 

1054 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Roehl v. American Family Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 98-1207


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


222 Wis. 2d 136; 585 N.W.2d 893; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1099


August 19, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
September 23, 1998, Decided  
September 23, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Washington County: LEO F. SCHLAEFER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insureds appealed a grant of summary judgment for defendant insurer from the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), dismissing a claim for underinsured motorist benefits under automobile liability policies. The issue was whether the insurer was obligated by Wis. Stat. § 631.36(5), its policies, or both to notify the insureds of a limitation in coverage occasioned by the enactment of Wis. Stat. § 632.32(5)(j).


OVERVIEW: The trial court ruled that Wis. Stat. § 631.36(5), which required automobile liability insurers to provide notice when a policy was renewed on less favorable terms, did not apply where a reduction of coverage was triggered by the legislature's action of the legislature. The trial court also ruled that the language of the policies did not obligate the insurer to provide notice. As a result, the "drive other car" exclusions in the policies were enforceable even though the insurer had not given the notice that the legislature had validated such exclusions following a judicial decision which had invalidated them. In affirming the grant of summary judgment to the insurer, the court held that the insurer was not required by statute, the terms of its policy, or a combination of both to notify the insureds of changes in coverage due to legislative action. The enactment of Wis. Stat. § 632.32(5)(j) did not unconstitutionally deprive the insureds of their right to contract. Finally, the trial court's ruling did not violate the public policy reflected by Wis. Stat. § 631.36(5).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for the insurer.

State v. Hull


No. 98-0619-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


222 Wis. 2d 220; 587 N.W.2d 215; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1093

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Oneida County: MARK A. MANGERSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Oneida County, Wisconsin, convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OWI), in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a). Defendant was sentenced to 75 days in jail, fined $ 1,800, had his licensed revoked for 30 months, and was ordered to complete an alcohol assessment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of OWI in February 1988, and received a first offense civil forfeiture. In June 1996, defendant was convicted of OWI a second time. Defendant did not retain counsel for either of those civil forfeiture convictions. In May 1997, defendant was cited for OWI a third time. It was defendant's third OWI offense within the 10-year statutory period and the trial court counted his two prior OWI forfeiture convictions to convict and sentence defendant as a third-time offender. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by relying upon two prior uncounseled civil forfeiture OWI convictions to subject him to prosecution and punishment as a third-time OWI offender as it violated his due process and equal protection rights under the Wisconsin and United States Constitutions. The appellate court concluded that uncounseled civil forfeiture OWI convictions were valid for all purposes including providing a basis for incarcerating defendant. Therefore, defendant's due process challenges failed. In addition, the appellate court held that defendant's equal protection argument failed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1056 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Randall


No. 97-0519-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


222 Wis. 2d 53; 586 N.W.2d 318; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1073


April 7, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
September 17, 1998, Decided  
September 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: JOSEPH E. WIMMER, Judge.
State v. Randall, 192 Wis. 2d 800, 532 N.W.2d 94, 1995 Wisc. LEXIS 50 (Wis., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which found that he was still dangerous and recommitted him to the custody of the Wisconsin Department of Heath and Social Services at the Winnebago Mental Health Institute (WMHI).


OVERVIEW: While defendant was a minor, he committed a series of burglaries and car thefts that culminated in three murders. A jury found defendant guilty of, inter alia, first degree murder, but determined that he was not responsible for the homicides because he was suffering from paranoid schizophrenia. Defendant was committed to a state hospital. Over the years, defendant successfully completed WMHI treatment programs. Defendant filed a petition for re-examination and conditional release. A jury found that defendant was still dangerous and the trial court recommitted him. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in framing a dangerousness instruction because Wis. Stat. § 971.17 (1987-88) specified no particular dangerousness level. Further, the instructions, taken in context, made clear that defendant could be released with the imposition of certain court-imposed conditions. Moreover, the evidence was sufficient to support a finding of dangerousness. Finally, an individual showing that confinement was necessary to address a particular medical treatment was not required. Thus, defendant was not denied substantive due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision finding that defendant was still dangerous and recommitting him to the custody of the WMHI.

State v. Hollister


No. 97-2838-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


222 Wis. 2d 218; 587 N.W.2d 214; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1054



September 15, 1998, Released

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Trempealeau County: ROBERT W. RADCLIFFE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Trempealeau County, Wisconsin, that convicted him of one count of first-degree sexual assault and one count of burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) the trial court erred by admitting the victim's statements to a social worker because they were inadmissible hearsay; (2) evidence should have been suppressed; (3) the fingerprint evidence was insufficient; (4) his due process rights were violated; (5) the trial court erroneously refused to permit the jury to take notes; (6) Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1) was unconstitutional; and (7) he was denied his right to effective assistance of counsel. The trial court properly admitted the social worker's statement. The trial court found the child to be a verbal and bright six-year-old who was able to differentiate between truth and falsity. The trial court was entitled to conclude that inconsistencies among the child's various statements were not so great as to outweigh other factors bearing on reliability. The record reflected a reasonable exercise of discretion by the trial court in denying defendant's request to permit the jury to take notes. Because defendant must have realized that touching a child's vaginal area constituted sexual assault, § 948.02(1) was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendant was not denied the right to effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cemetery Servs. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Regulation & Licensing


No. 97-2115


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


221 Wis. 2d 817; 586 N.W.2d 191; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1034


March 9, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
September 10, 1998, Decided  
September 10, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: ROBERT R. PEKOWSKY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, funeral home corporation and cemetery corporation, sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment to defendant Wisconsin Department of Regulation and Licensing, declaring that the corporations violated Wis. Stat. §§ 157.067(2), 445.12(6), which prohibited certain connections between cemeteries and funeral homes.


OVERVIEW: The funeral home corporation and the cemetery corporation were established as separate state corporations under a larger umbrella funeral home corporation in order for the larger funeral home corporation to operate funeral homes and cemeteries within the State of Wisconsin, because Wis. Stat. §§ 157.067(2), 445.12(6), prohibited one corporation from owning and operating both cemeteries and funeral homes. The funeral home corporation and cemetery corporation filed a complaint against the Department, and summary judgment was granted to the department. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the status of the funeral home corporation and the cemetery corporation as subsidiaries of a larger corporation created impermissible financial connections that violated Wis. Stat. §§ 157.067(2), 445.12(6) on its face. The court further held that Wis. Stat. §§ 157.067(2), 445.12(6) were not void for vagueness because the statute gave fair notice that funeral establishments and cemeteries were not to have financial connections to each other. The court finally dismissed the remaining constitutional arguments for failure to properly brief the issues.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the Department.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction by the Circuit Court for Racine County (Wisconsin) for misdemeanor false swearing in violation of Wis. Stat. Ann. § 946.32(1). Defendant sought to withdraw his guilty plea, contending that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to convict him because the statute of limitations had expired on the charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was originally charged with felony false swearing for giving inconsistent testimony in depositions in civil lawsuits under Wis. Stat. Ann. § 946.32(1). He sought a dismissal, contending the prosecution was barred by the statute of limitations. The trial court denied his motion, finding that the statute of limitations was tolled, under Wis. Stat. Ann. § 939.74(3), while defendant was incarcerated out of state, which ruling was affirmed on appeal. Defendant then pled guilty to misdemeanor false swearing as a habitual offender under Wis. Stat. Defendant claimed that the amended complaint was time barred, but the court affirmed the conviction because it was clear from the record that defendant had waived the objection through an informed guilty plea. However, the court vacated the fine because the fine in the oral pronouncement, which was controlling, was less than that in the judgment of conviction. The state argued that the difference was the costs imposed, but could not verify that from the record. The court directed the state on remand to provide the trial court with documentation of the costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for misdemeanor false swearing. However, the court vacated defendant's fine and remanded with directions to the trial court to ascertain the amount of costs associated with it.

Eberle v. Dane County Bd. of Adjustment

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH O'BRIEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developers sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed various constitutional and damage claims in the developers' action against respondent Dane County Board of Adjustment. The Board filed a cross-appeal from the circuit court's granting of the developers' petition for certiorari, holding that the Board erroneously denied the developers' application for a special permit.


OVERVIEW: The developers filed an application with the Board for a special permit, which the Board denied, and the developers filed a petition for certiorari, which the circuit court granted, and the Board appealed. The developers also filed a complaint alleging various constitutional and damage claims, which the circuit court dismissed, and the developers appealed. The court found that the trial court properly denied the developers' other claims because they took advantage of the state-law remedy available via certiorari and prevailed and thus, there was no cognizable "taking" of their property. The court concluded that the developers were not entitled to attorney fees as they had not prevailed on their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment dismissing the developers' constitutional and damage claims against the Board. The court also affirmed the circuit court's judgment granting the developers' petition for certiorari and ordering the Board to issue a special permit to the developers.

State v. Hahn


No. 97-3065-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


221 Wis. 2d 670; 586 N.W.2d 5; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 958


June 9, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
August 20, 1998, Decided  
August 20, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: JOHN ULLSVIK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), in which he was convicted of intentionally collecting proceeds of a gambling machine, as a party to the crime, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 945.03(5). Defendant claimed that Wis. Stat. § 945.01(3), which defined a gambling machine, was unconstitutionally vague, that there was insufficient evidence, and that the State did not obey a discovery order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned and managed several video poker machines and, through his employees, allegedly collected the proceeds of the machines. Defendant was convicted of such, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 945.03(5), and he appealed. The court affirmed, holding that Wis. Stat. § 945.01(3) was not unconstitutionally vague because it was capable of being construed according to the ordinary principles of statutory construction so as to make its meaning reasonably definite and provided a person of ordinary intelligence adequate notice of the conduct prohibited. The court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's verdict, finding defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of collecting proceeds from gambling machines knowing that the machines were being used for gambling and that the proceeds were from gambling. The court concluded that the trial court properly exercised its discretion in denying defendant's motion to exclude the testimony of certain witnesses based on the State's failure to comply with a discovery order because the trial court considered the relevant facts, applied the proper standard of law, and used a rational process to reach a reasonable conclusion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, convicting defendant of intentionally collecting proceeds of a gambling machine, as a party to the crime.

 

1062 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rodriguez


No. 97-3097-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


221 Wis. 2d 487; 585 N.W.2d 701; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 957


May 11, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
August 20, 1998, Decided  
August 20, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: MICHAEL J. MULROY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which denied defendant's motion to withdraw his Alford plea to a charge of second degree sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with second-degree sexual assault as a habitual offender, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 940.225(2)(d) and 939.62(2); criminal trespass, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.14; and criminal damage to property, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 943.01(1). Defendant entered an Alford plea to a reduced charge of second-degree sexual assault. Defendant filed a motion to withdraw his plea claiming that it was not voluntarily and knowingly entered because the plea was based upon defendant's mistaken belief that he was a United States citizen. Defendant was not a citizen, and the Immigration and Naturalization Service filed a notice of investigation to determine if defendant was subject to deportation. The trial court denied defendant's motion, and defendant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that defendant's misunderstanding of his citizenship status did not render his plea unconstitutionally infirm as not voluntarily, knowingly and intelligently entered. There was no evidence that defendant's mistaken belief of his citizenship status was based upon any information he received from the State or his own counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied defendant's motion to withdraw his Alford plea to a charge of second degree sexual assault.

 

1063 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Town of Jackson v. O'Hearn


No. 98-0237


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


221 Wis. 2d 598; 586 N.W.2d 699; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 910



August 12, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Washington County: ANNETTE K. ZIEGLER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant farmer challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a meat shop from his farm in violation of the Town of Jackson, Wis. Zoning Ordinance § 3.03(a).


OVERVIEW: The farmer received a building permit for a pole barn to store hay to feed his bison. Instead of using the barn for storage, however, he opened a retail store for the sale of bison meat. On appeal, the court rejected his challenges to the ordinance. The court held that the definition of "farming" under Wis. Stat. § 102.04(3), which permitted direct distribution to consumers, was not synonymous with "agribusiness" as used in the ordinance. The ordinance clearly did not authorize agribusiness as a separate land use. Further, the farmer showed no evidence of intentional, systematic, or arbitrary discrimination by the town's enforcement of the ordinance. Finally, the town's amendment of the ordinance allowing the sale of certain items but not the sale of meat did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. There was a distinction with a difference surrounding the sale of meat and other farm-produced items. Given the purpose of the ordinance to provide for, maintain, preserve, and enhance agricultural lands historically utilized for crop production, regulating the nature of any commercial use of the property was reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted the farmer of violating the zoning ordinance.

 

1064 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Rasmussen v. Rasmussen


No. 96-2898


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


221 Wis. 2d 595; 586 N.W.2d 698; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 899



August 6, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and orders of the circuit court for Jefferson County: J. R. ERWIN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), which entered judgment in favor of respondent ex-wife on her petition for divorce.


OVERVIEW: The ex-wife brought suit against the ex-husband seeking divorce. The circuit entered judgment in favor of the ex-wife and issued various orders in connection with the divorce. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the circuit court did not err in basing the ex-husband's child support obligations on his earning capacity rather than his actual earnings. Despite the ex-husband' argument to the contrary, the court held that the circuit court was not required to accept the expert testimony on the ex-husband's earnings even though it was uncontradicted. The court further held that the circuit court did not err in denying the ex-husband's request to leave maintenance open for him indefinitely because he did not offer a reason or basis for his request. The court noted that awarding maintenance was discretionary with the circuit court. The court also determined that the circuit court decision permitting the ex-husband to claim his son as an exemption on his income tax only if he was current in his child support did not constitute a "per se abuse" of discretion. The court reasoned that Wis. Admin Code § HSS 80.03(6) sanctioned a conditional order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order entering judgment in favor of the ex-wife in her suit against the ex-husband seeking divorce.

 

1065 of 2046 DOCUMENTS



State v. Kienitz (In re Kienitz)


No. 97-1460


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


221 Wis. 2d 275; 585 N.W.2d 609; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 867


April 7, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
July 30, 1998, Decided  
July 30, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B. O'BRIEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Since 1963, defendant was convicted of sex crimes against children three times and had probations revoked for similar offenses. After the supreme court upheld Wis. Stat. ch. 980's constitutionality, the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), on remand and trial to the court, ordered defendant to be committed to a secure mental health facility as a sexually violent person, and denied postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that defendant had been convicted of a sexually violent offense and was dangerous because he suffered from a mental disorder, pedophilia, which made it substantially probable that he would commit sexual violence. The trial court thoroughly summarized each of the three presented experts' opinions and found defendant's expert to be more persuasive than the State's, whose methods were not validated by any scientific testing and because they used clinical judgment, a poor predictor of recidivism. The decision leaned heavily on those opinions and the history of deliberate violations. The appellate court found that "substantially probable" in Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7) meant: considerably more likely to occur than not. The dictionary definition sufficed. The phrase was not unconstitutionally vague. "Substantial evidence" review for criminal cases applied. The trial court did not have to rely on experts to find sexual violence to be probable and was free to weigh their testimony. The expert testimony on recidivism did not have to be based on actuarial methodology. Legal and medical definitions had to be kept separate in the context of ch. 980.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


 

1066 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Revels


No. 97-3148-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


221 Wis. 2d 315; 585 N.W.2d 602; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 866


June 9, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
July 30, 1998, Decided  
July 30, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Vernon County: MICHAEL J. ROSBOROUGH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed an interlocutory appeal of the order of the Circuit Court for Vernon County (Wisconsin) requiring him to give the prosecutor a summary of his expert witness's findings and the subject matter of his testimony under Wis. Stat. § 971.23(2m)(am). Defendant, charged with causing death by the intoxicated use of a vehicle, argued that the statute was unconstitutional and that disclosure would violate his right against self-incrimination.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was ordered to produce a summary of his expert witness's findings and testimony. On interlocutory appeal, the court affirmed the order, finding that Wis. Stat. § 971.23(2m) was procedural rather than substantive and, thus, was not subject to challenge as being void for vagueness. The court ruled that the statute was not overbroad and that disclosure of the expert's opinion would not violate defendant's right against self-incrimination because it did not compel testimony, but merely accelerated the timing of the disclosure. The court found that the self-incrimination privilege was personal, adhering to the person not to information that may incriminate him, and that information compiled by the expert was not personal to defendant. The court ruled that the order did not infringe on defendant's right to counsel or the attorney-client privilege because he could seek a protective order or in camera review to resolve these claims. The court found that defendant had to disclose a summary of the expert's findings or testimony and any test results to be offered at trial, and that his initial response that the expert would present the results of his examination was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's interlocutory order requiring defendant to provide the prosecutor with a summary of his expert witness's findings and the subject matter of the witness's testimony and remanded the case for trial.

 

1067 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kiernan


No. 97-2449-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


221 Wis. 2d 126; 584 N.W.2d 203; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 853


January 6, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
July 22, 1998, Dated  
July 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: JOHN B. MURPHY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), convicting her of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1)(a) and 346.65(2)(c), and operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited blood alcohol concentration, Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1)(b) and 346.65(2)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1)(a) and 346.65(2)(c), and operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited blood alcohol concentration, Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1)(b) and 346.65(2)(c). Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred when it refused to strike for cause jurors who earlier rejected the identical theory of defense to be employed by defendant. The court ruled that a determination by a trial court that a prospective juror could be impartial was overturned only where the prospective juror's bias was manifest. Further, the court held that a prospective juror's bias was manifest whenever a review of the record did not support a finding that the prospective juror was a reasonable person who was sincerely willing to put aside an opinion or prior knowledge or did not support a finding that a reasonable person in the juror's position could set aside the opinion or prior knowledge. The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that the trial court erred when it failed to honor defendant's motion to strike the jurors for cause.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was reversed.

 

1068 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hnanicek


No. 98-0782-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


221 Wis. 2d 223; 584 N.W.2d 235; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 849



July 21, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY K. BRENNAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to suppress evidence, after which he pled guilty to possessing marijuana under Wis. Stat. §§ 961.14(4)(t), 961.01(14), and 961.41(3g)(e). Defendant argued that the police found the marijuana as the result of an illegal arrest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for violating a city ordinance against knowingly resisting or obstructing an officer while he was doing any act in an official capacity and with lawful authority. When an officer found marijuana in his pocket, he was charged with drug possession, but not the ordinance violation. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress, ruling that the officer had probable cause to arrest. Defendant pled guilty. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the officers acted lawfully in approaching a group of men and asking questions while investigating drug activity in the area. The court ruled that the officers had the right to chase and apprehend defendant when he ran from the group because his flight destabilized the situation and interfered with the officers' ability to talk to the others, in violation of the ordinance. The court found that the arrest was lawful because the officers had reasonable grounds, or probable cause, to believe that defendant violated the ordinance. The court concluded that, because defendant's arrest for violating the ordinance was lawful, the search incident to the arrest was lawful and the motion to suppress was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of possession of marijuana, after denying defendant's motion to suppress.

State v. Curiel


No. 97-1337


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


221 Wis. 2d 596; 586 N.W.2d 698; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 844



July 21, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted the State's petition and found defendant to be a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7).


OVERVIEW: The State filed a petition alleging that defendant was a sexually violent person under Wis. Stat. § 980.01(7). The State alleged that defendant was convicted of second degree sexual assault as the jurisdictional basis for the petition. The trial court granted the petition after finding that defendant was at a high risk of committing another sexual offense and ordered defendant committed. Defendant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to sustain the trial court's conclusion. The court noted that two out of three experts testified that it was substantially probable that defendant would reoffend. It was irrelevant, the court said, whether these experts believed that it was more likely than not or much more likely than not that defendant would commit another offense. The court said that the legislature used the term "substantially probable" and that the State had proven beyond a reasonable doubt the defendant suffered from a mental disorder that made it substantially probable that he would engage in acts of sexual violence. The court found that the experts said defendant suffered from pedophilia and displayed several risk factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order that granted the State's petition and held defendant to be a sexually violent person.

City of Milwaukee v. Allos, Inc.


No. 97-3372


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


221 Wis. 2d 222; 584 N.W.2d 234; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 807



July 7, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: CLARE L. FIORENZA, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant subsequent owner appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which had entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff city. The city had begun a civil forfeiture action in the municipal court against the subsequent owner after he failed to comply with an order to correct the condition of a premises for a building code violation issued by the City of Milwaukee Department of Building Inspection.


OVERVIEW: The Department had issued an order to an owner for a violation of Milwaukee, Wis., Code of Ordinances § 275-32-3-g. The owner did not respond to the Department but conveyed his interest in the duplex to the subsequent owner. The subsequent owner recorded the deed but did not notify the Department. The Department discovered that the subsequent owner had title to the duplex so the Department notified the subsequent owner who did not reply. The city commenced a civil forfeiture action against the subsequent owner for failing to remedy the violation. The municipal court found in favor of the subsequent owner, and the city appealed. The circuit court reversed the decision of the municipal court and entered a judgment in favor of the city. The subsequent owner appealed, and the court affirmed the decision of the circuit court. The court held that when the owner transferred his ownership interest in the property to the subsequent owner, the order to correct became effective against the subsequent owner. The court ruled that § 200-12 complied with the mandates of the due process clause and was constitutional. The subsequent owner had a duty to know the condition of the property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

State v. Mendoza


No. 97-0952-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


220 Wis. 2d 803; 584 N.W.2d 174; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 798


May 20, 1998, Oral Argument  
July 7, 1998, Decided  
July 7, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: LAURENCE C. GRAM, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction by the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) for possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, as a second or subsequent offense. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by not suppressing evidence seized during a pretextual administrative search, by not suppressing evidence seized from his car and by removing four jurors for cause solely because they had criminal records.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, as a second or subsequent offense. The court reversed defendant's conviction finding that the trial court improperly removed four jurors for cause solely because they had criminal records. The court found that absent more, a showing that a juror had a criminal conviction was not grounds for disqualification within the meaning of Wisconsin Stat. § 756.01. Essentially, the court found that the disqualification for cause gave the prosecution four additional preemptory challenges. The court also remanded the issue of whether the trial court erred when it denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence discovered in the storage room of a tavern during an administrative search. The court reasoned that the trial court improperly neglected to determine if the officers were conducting an administrative inspection or was the inspection an impermissible pretextual search.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, as a second or subsequent offense.
