1074 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Armstead


No. 97-3056-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


220 Wis. 2d 626; 583 N.W.2d 444; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 717



June 23, 1998, Dated  
June 23, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 1, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a non-final order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DANIEL A. NOONAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed from a non-final order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied her motion to dismiss the charge of first-degree intentional homicide, party to a crime, and ordered that she should not be "reverse waived" to the juvenile court, but instead, should remain subject to the jurisdiction of the adult court pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 938.183 and 970.032.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to the trial court denying defendant's motion to dismiss and ordering that defendant should not be "reversed waived" to juvenile court, defendant appealed. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred because the "reverse waiver" statutory scheme violated her constitutional rights to equal protection and due process. The court concluded that a decision regarding defendant equal protection claim, as well as claims of ineffective assistance of counsel, cruel and unusual punishment, and the Wis. Const. art. I, § 6 claim would have been based on hypothetical or future facts. Therefore, these claims were not ripe for review and the court refused to address them. The court noted that if defendant was convicted on one of the lesser-included offenses of first-degree intentional homicide, a juvenile disposition could occur. However, defendant's trial had not occurred at the time of the appeal and the claim was not ripe for review. The court also held that neither Wis. Stat. §§ 938.183 and 970.032 were vague or ambiguous. The statutes provided the trial court standards with which to decided whether to retain jurisdiction or send defendant's case to juvenile court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charge of first-degree intentional homicide, party to a crime, and ordered that she should not be "reverse waived" to the juvenile court.

 

1075 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Benzel


Nos. 97-3528-CR, 97-3529-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


220 Wis. 2d 588; 583 N.W.2d 434; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 694


May 18, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
June 16, 1998, Dated  
June 16, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Outagamie County: JOSEPH M. TROY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion for post-conviction relief under Wis. Stat. § 974.06, for his conviction under Wis. Stat. § 139.95 for possession of drugs without a tax stamp. Defendant alleged violations of his constitutional rights and ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Section 139.95, which prohibited the possession of drugs without a tax stamp, was declared unconstitutional by the Supreme Court of Wisconsin, but the trial court declined to apply that determination retroactively to defendant's case because he pleaded no contest the charges. The main issue on appeal was whether to retroactively apply that holding to the present case; that is, whether retroactive application was warranted when the conduct in question could not constitutionally be punished in the first place. The court held that retroactive application of a controlling judicial precedent that declared a criminal statute to be unconstitutional was required because failure to do so led to the untenable result that a person was convicted for conduct that was held constitutionally immune from punishment. Therefore, where the trial court had no subject matter jurisdiction over a non-existent crime, even if the conviction was based on a plea agreement, or by a plea of no contest as in defendant's case, the conviction had to be vacated. An offense created by an unconstitutional statute was no longer a crime, and a conviction under such statute could not be a legal cause for imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for possession of drugs without a tax stamp, as well as the order that denied postconviction relief, and remanded to the trial court with instructions to vacate defendant's drug tax stamp law conviction.

 

1076 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Pace v. Oneida County


Nos. 97-3263, 98-0059-W


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


220 Wis. 2d 717; 583 N.W.2d 674; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 645



June 2, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Oneida County: MARK A. MANGERSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant boathouse owners sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Oneida County (Wisconsin), which denied their motion for substitution of judge after the trial court concluded that there were no issues pending before it in their action against respondents, a county and related parties. The owners maintained that the trial court's determination was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: The owner's boathouse was destroyed by fire. The county denied their application to rebuild, and the board of adjustment affirmed. The owners later sought a permit under a newly enacted statute, Wis. Stat. § 30.121(2), which permitted reconstruction after fire, but it was denied. The owners then rebuilt the boathouse and sought a declaratory judgment that the ordinance prohibiting wet boathouses was unconstitutional. The county filed a separate action seeking forfeiture. The trial court ordered forfeiture. On appeal, the court affirmed the forfeiture but remanded solely for a determination whether the county ordinance constituted an unlawful taking. The trial court resolved the constitutional issue in favor of the county. On a second appeal, the court reversed the trial court's determination with respect to constitutionality and held that, in view of the new legislation which permitted rebuilding, the constitutionality of the ordinance need not be addressed. The court held that the parties had not yet litigated the scope of the new statute and its applicability to the boathouse constructed by the owners. Thus, the court ruled that the issue was not properly before the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1077 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Michael L.P-L.


No. 98-0498, 98-0499, 98-0500


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


220 Wis. 2d 359; 582 N.W.2d 505; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 789



May 21, 1998, Decided


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for La Crosse County: DENNIS G. MONTABON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of orders from the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which terminated her parental rights to her three minor children after a jury found that the La Crosse County Department of Human Services had established that the mother's children were in continuing need of protection or services (CHIPS).


OVERVIEW: After a hearing, the circuit court terminated the mother's parental rights finding her children fell under the heading of CHIPS. The mother claimed the orders violated her constitutional right to due process because she was denied appointed counsel at the plea hearing in previous court proceedings to declare the children to be in need of protection or services. Additionally, the mother claimed that the term "substantial progress" in Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2)(c), was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court affirmed the orders holding that the first claim was not supported by the appellate record because there was no transcript of the hearing in the appellate record. The court held that parents did not have a constitutionally protected right to counsel in all child protective hearings and absent a transcript, the decision would not be overturned. The court held that the mother had additionally not met her burden on the second claim of establishing the unconstitutionality of the statute in question because the term "substantial progress," while it left some discretion to the courts, there was no right to make minimal progress so her argument failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the three orders terminating the mother's parental rights.

 

1078 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Waupun v. Hermans


No. 97-3610


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


220 Wis. 2d 358; 582 N.W.2d 505; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 581



May 7, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dodge County: ANDREW P. BISSONNETTE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction in the Circuit Court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant and operating with a prohibited alcohol concentration in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and (b). Defendant argued that he was arrested at his residence without probable cause, and therefore the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: A woman reported that defendant had been drinking, and had slashed his wrists at her residence. When one officer arrived at the residence he observed a vehicle that was stopped in its lane of traffic in the road, which accelerated faster than normal, turned into the driveway of the residence, and drove into the garage. Defendant was ordered out of the car; and when he eventually exited the vehicle, officers observed wounds on his wrists. A struggle ensued and defendant was placed in custody for his own protection. Based upon observations of defendant while he was transported to the hospital and other information, defendant was arrested at the hospital for driving under the influence. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress; and on his appeal of his convictions, the court held that under Wis. Stat. § 51.15(1)(a)1 and (b)1 the officers, believing defendant to be mentally ill and a danger to himself, had authority to take him into custody. The court held that the officers' beliefs were based upon reliably reported information and their own observations. Therefore, the court held that the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entered on defendant's conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant and operating with a prohibited alcohol concentration. The court ruled that the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence.

 

1079 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Telemark Dev., Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 97-3133


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


218 Wis. 2d 809; 581 N.W.2d 585; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 548


April 7, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
April 30, 1998, Decided  
April 30, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) affirming the Tax Appeals Commission's confirmation of a determination of respondent Department of Revenue. The order found that the taxpayer's sales of "flexible" time-share interests in a condominium resort development were subject to sales tax.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was in the business of selling time-share units in condominiums via land contracts and deeds. After an audit, the Department assessed delinquent sales taxes against the taxpayer for the flexible time-shares. The taxpayer challenged the Department's decision and the Commission affirmed its order. The Commission's decision was later affirmed by the circuit court. On appeal from that order, the court affirmed. Applying due-weight deference to the Commission's decision, the court found that the Commission could have reasonably concluded, on the facts, that the flexible time-share sales were not fixed as to either unit or starting time within the meaning of Wis. Stat. § 77.52(2)(a)1. The court further held that it was reasonable for the Commission to have concluded that the flexible time-share sales were subject to taxation under § 77.52(2)(a)1. The court determined that the taxpayer had not established beyond a reasonable doubt that the legislature's decision to tax the sale of flexible time-shares, while not taxing the sale of guaranteed time-shares, resulted in the type of invidious discrimination the equal protection clause was designed to protect against.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order upholding the Commission's decision to confirm the Department's assessment against the taxpayer for delinquent taxes on the sale of flexible time-shares.

 

1080 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schultz


No. 97-3414


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


218 Wis. 2d 798; 582 N.W.2d 113; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 554


March 23, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
April 28, 1998, Decided  
April 28, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Barron County: EDWARD L. BRUNNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bar owner sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin) that declared his bar a nuisance because he permitted prostitution to occur within it. The bar owner argued that Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 823.09 and Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 823.10, unconstitutionally violated his federal due process and freedom of association rights, contrary to U.S. Const. amend. I and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: In a claim brought by respondent State, pursuant to Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 823.09 and Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 823.10, the trial court declared that the bar owner's bar was a nuisance because he permitted prostitution to occur within it. The bar owner on appeal argued that § 823.09 and § 823.10 unconstitutionally violated his federal due process and freedom of association rights. The court reasoned that §§ 823.09 and 823.10, and Wis. R. Civ. P., Wis. Stat. § 823.11 provided the bar owner the opportunity to rebut the prima facie evidence that he had knowledge of the prostitution activity and to collaterally attack the convictions supporting the nuisance case. Therefore, the court concluded that the statutes did not deprive the bar owner of due process. Further, the court held that the bar owner was free to associate with whomever he desired. However, under §§ 823.09, 823.10 and 823.11, he could not permit his property to be used for acts of prostitution. The court concluded that the statutes in question did not violate constitutional rights to freedom of association, the protection against government establishment of a religion, and equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that declared the bar owner's bar a nuisance on the grounds that the bar owner permitted prostitution to occur within it.

State v. Jones

PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: STANLEY A. MILLER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of armed robbery, party to a crime, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(1)(b), (2) and 939.05.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of armed robbery, party to a crime, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 943.32(1)(b), (2) and 939.05. Defendant contended on appeal that he was denied his constitutional right to equal protection of law when the State exercised three peremptory challenges to strike minority jurors from the panel. The court affirmed the judgment against defendant. The court concluded that the proper timing of a Batson objection was after the composition of the jury was made known, but before the jury was sworn. The court found that defendant had waived his right to raise the issue on appeal because he failed to timely object to the State's striking of the minority jurors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of armed robbery, party to a crime.

 

1082 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jocius v. Jocius


No. 96-2746


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


218 Wis. 2d 103; 580 N.W.2d 708; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 421


January 7, 1998, Submitted on Briefs  
March 31, 1998, Decided  
March 31, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 1, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment 1 of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DOMINIC S. AMATO, Judge.


1 The trial court refers to its decision as a "judgment." However, for purposes of this appeal, we will refer to it as an order in our opinion.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) entered in favor of petitioner mother, which denied him any periods of physical placement with his three children, permanently prohibited him from petitioning for any change in physical placement rights, changed the children's surnames, and ordered the domestic abuse injunction converted to a permanent injunction.


OVERVIEW: The father had been in prison for most of the children's lives and the trial court found he was unfit to have or to ever seek physical placement of them. The father argued that the trial court lacked the statutory authority to make a prospective order and to change the children's surnames. The court reversed those orders, finding that the trial court exceeded its authority. The guardian ad litem submitted an affidavit which served as the underpinnings for obtaining a child abuse temporary restraining order. The record was insufficient to review the court's discretion in that order. The mother also brought a temporary restraining order, which was not appealed. The finding that the father was an unfit parent, based on the testimony of one of the expert witnesses, was sufficient to invoke Wis. Stat. § 767.24(4)(b). However, Wis. Stat. § 767.325(4)(b), did not permit the trial court to make a prospective order prohibiting the father from requesting a change in physical placement in the future. None of the procedural steps in Wis. Stat. § 786.36 were followed, therefore the trial court's order changing the names of the children was in contradiction to the statute and was void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders changing the children's surnames and prohibiting the father from seeking placement of the children in the future and remanded the issue of payment of fees to the trial court.

State v. Evans


No. 97-2303-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


218 Wis. 2d 166; 578 N.W.2d 210; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 391



March 26, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock County: JOHN W. ROETHE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin) for carrying a concealed weapon in violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.23, obstructing an officer in violation of Wis. Stat. § 946.41(1) and disorderly conduct in violation of § 947.01. The trial court admitted evidence discovered during a pat-down search for weapons pursuant to a seizure by police.


OVERVIEW: A police officer testified that he discovered an unoccupied vehicle blocking the lane of traffic. As he approached the vehicle, defendant appeared and told the officer that the vehicle was his. The officer instructed defendant to wait in the vehicle and the officer returned to his squad car to run the license plate information through dispatch. Defendant then approached the squad car and did not stop when told to do so. The officer held defendant against the vehicle and patted him down. After his arrest, defendant filed a motion to suppress the three-inch steak knife that the officer found in his pocket. The trial court concluded that the search was not a seizure within the meaning of the Fourth Amendment and alternately, that there were articulable facts that provided a reasonable ground for the officer to believe that defendant was violating a traffic law. On appeal, the court agreed with defendant that a seizure took place when the officer directed him to sit in his vehicle. The court concluded, however, that both the seizure and the pat down were supported by the necessary reasonable suspicion and were therefore, constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for carrying a concealed weapon, obstructing an officer and disorderly conduct.

Olson v. Olson


No. 97-2484


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


218 Wis. 2d 167; 578 N.W.2d 210; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 373



March 19, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Grant County: GEORGE S. CURRY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Grant County (Wisconsin), which held her in contempt, in favor of appellee ex-husband, for failing to seek work as required under a modified divorce judgment. The ex-wife also challenged a subsequent order denying her motion to modify the order, which committed her to jail but stayed the commitment provided she met two conditions, one of which was that she continued to seek work.


OVERVIEW: The ex-wife was ordered to seek work for the purpose of providing support for the minor child of the parties. Custody of the minor child had been awarded to the ex-husband. The ex-wife contended that because she was disabled and received Supplemental Security Income (SSI), the trial court lacked authority to countermand the federal determination of disability by ordering her to seek work. The court concluded that ordering a party to seek work as part of a child support order was within the discretion of the trial court. Further, the court held that it had previously determined that an SSI recipient could have been ordered to seek work. The court further held that an order to pay child support where the obligor's only source of income was her SSI benefits would have violated the protection from legal process provided to Social Security benefits under Wis. Stat. § 49.96. However, the court reasoned that the ex-wife was not precluded from seeking work due to her dyslexia.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, in favor of the ex-husband, which held the ex-wife in contempt for failing to seek work as required under a modified divorce judgment.

 

1085 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City News & Novelty, Inc. v. City of Waukesha


No. 97-1504


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 357



March 18, 1998, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.



DISPOSITION: Pursuant to RULE 809.61, STATS., this court certifies the appeal in this case to the Wisconsin Supreme Court for its review and determination. 1



1 The parties raise and argue additional issues in the briefs; however, we certify only the following three issues for supreme court review.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensee challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court (Wisconsin) in a certiorari action for judicial review of the denial of its license to operate an "adult-oriented establishment" by respondent City of Waukesha. The licensee asserted that Waukesha, Wis. Code § 8.195 (1995) failed to preserve the status quo during the license renewal process and was facially unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The licensee sought to renew its license to operate an "adult-oriented establishment," pursuant to Waukesha, Wis., Code § 8.195 (1995). The City, by its common council passed a resolution that found the licensee had committed several violations of the ordinance and, as a result, denied the renewal of its license. The licensee sought administrative review, which affirmed the City's decision. In a certiorari action, the trial court upheld the denial, and the licensee appealed, challenging the constitutionality of § 8.195 because it failed to preserve the status quo during the license renewal process. The court concluded that there was no Wisconsin law and no Supreme Court statement on whether the absence of an explicit status quo provision rendered an ordinance facially unconstitutional. Because it concluded that the issue would greatly impact local municipalities' regulation of adult-oriented establishments, the court requested the Wisconsin Supreme Court to decide the issue. It further requested a determination of two related issues: the constitutionality of no express time limits for judicial review and the propriety of denying renewal without first invoking a lesser sanction.


OUTCOME: The court requested the state's highest court to accept jurisdiction and to decide the issues related to the constitutionality of the local licensing ordinance in an action by the licensee against the City, seeking to invalidate the ordinance.

 

1086 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of Kenosha v. C & S Mgmt.


No. 97-0642


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 361



March 18, 1998, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.



DISPOSITION: Pursuant to RULE 809.61, STATS., this court certifies the appeal in this case to the Wisconsin Supreme Court for its review and determination.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, an adult bookstore operator, was charged with violating Kenosha County, Wis., Ordinance No. 9.10.2 for selling allegedly obscene videotapes. At trial, defendant stipulated to that the videotape was sold for commercial purposes and was sexually explicit, leaving only the issue of whether the tape was obscene. A jury in the Circuit Court of Kenosha County (Wisconsin) returned a non-unanimous guilty verdict, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county ordinance which defendant was charged with violating was identical to Wis. Stat. § 944.21 in all respects except that the penalty provisions varied and prosecution under the statute requires the approval of the attorney general, while prosecuting under the ordinance did not. At trial, the parties stipulated the fact that the videotape was sold for commercial purposes and that defendant knew the tape was sexually explicit, leaving as the only contested issue whether the tape was "obscene material." No Wisconsin court had determined whether the statute regulating obscenity was constitutionally permissible, and if it was, whether the Miller standards of obscenity were applicable. The statute had state-wide criminal and forfeiture consequences, and a court of appeals affirmance or reversal of defendant's case would have simply delayed the inevitability of supreme court review. Because attempts to regulate adult-oriented establishments and materials had spawned unique legal problems of state and federal significance without establishment of clear precedent, the court felt it necessary to request that the Wisconsin Supreme Court accept jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court certified the appeal questions concerning the constitutionality of the state statutory prohibition, and respectfully requested that the Wisconsin Supreme Court accept jurisdiction.

Miriam T. v. Church Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 96-0329


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


218 Wis. 2d 163; 578 N.W.2d 208; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 298



March 10, 1998, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JACQUELINE D. SCHELLINGER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant church members challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint against respondents, insurance company and church. This action involved the existence of insurance coverage for respondent pastor of the church.


OVERVIEW: The church members attended services at the church and were active members. The female church member went to the pastor for marriage counseling. According to the female church member, during the course of providing counseling, the pastor made sexual contact with her on numerous occasions and this caused her mental and/or emotional injury. The female church member filed a complaint against the pastor, which was later amended, alleging that he provided negligent counseling services and that he violated the sexual exploitation by therapist statute, Wis. Stat. § 895.70. The circuit court dismissed the complaint. The court held that the church members did not present any relevant facts to the court as to why their case constituted one of limited circumstances under which a negligent supervision claim could be asserted successfully against a religious organization. The negligent supervision claim was also barred by U.S. Const. amend. I. Also, the pastor's initiations of sexual contact with female church member were outside the scope of his employment. The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which dismissed the complaint of the church members against the insurance company and the church in an action involving the existence of insurance coverage for the pastor of the church.

 

1088 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


No. 97-0201-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


218 Wis. 2d 164; 578 N.W.2d 208; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 260



March 3, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DAVID A. HANSHER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of first-degree reckless injury and resisting an officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with attempted first-degree intentional homicide, first-degree reckless injury, and resisting an officer as a result of a drunken attack on a city police officer. Defendant was convicted of first-degree reckless injury and resisting an officer. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. The court stated that a jury could conclude that a victim suffered "great bodily harm" as long as the victim suffered an injury that was "serious," defining the term as it was ordinarily understood, regardless of whether the injury created a substantial risk of death, permanent disfigurement, or impairment. The court determined that the testimony established that defendant placed the officer in a choke hold, causing her to stop breathing, and this evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict that defendant caused great bodily harm to the officer under circumstances that showed utter disregard for human life under Wis. Stat. § 940.23(1). The court held that defendant's proposed jury instruction could have erroneously misled the jury to believe that if a particular injury fell within the definition of substantial bodily harm, it could not qualify as great bodily harm.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

State v. Rapey


No. 97-0279-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


218 Wis. 2d 830; 581 N.W.2d 593; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 264



March 3, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ELSA C. LAMELAS and JOHN A. FRANKE, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) upon a conviction for violating an anti-stalking statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of stalking his wife. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court ruled that the anti-stalking statute was not constitutionally infirm. It was not vague and overbroad. The statute clearly defined the behavior forbidden, provided fair notice, and did not infringe upon constitutionally protected activities. The court ruled that defendant was not denied effective assistance of trial counsel. Evidence of other acts was admissible under Wis. R. Evid., Wis. Stat. § 904.04(2). Thus defendant's trial counsel was not deficient in failing to prevent its admission. The court ruled that defendant's counsel's questioning of witnesses, which evoked other bad acts, was a tactic to demonstrate that the victim did not fear defendant. The court ruled that the strategy was not unreasonable, and defendant's counsel was not deficient. The court ruled that defendant's counsel was not deficient by reason of his failure to object to the admission of certain handwritten notes constituting a diary made by the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction against defendant.

 

1090 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Peterson


No. 97-2730-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


217 Wis. 2d 292; 577 N.W.2d 388; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 156



February 12, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: PATRICK J. FIEDLER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of operating while intoxicated, fourth offense, and operating after revocation, second offense. The trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint and imposed a sentence of confinement in jail, assessment, forfeiture, and driver's license revocation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the lower prohibited alcohol concentration (PAC) of .08 for persons with two or more prior convictions, as compared to the PAC of .1 for persons with one or no prior convictions, under Wis. Stat. §§ 346.63(1)(b) and 340.01(46m), and the correlative lower threshold for the presumption of intoxication under Wis. Stat. § 885.235(1)(c) and (cd), violated his right to equal protection and due process of law. Defendant waived his right to a jury trial and stipulated to a blood alcohol concentration (BAC) of .22 percent. The court held that: (1) because defendant's BAC was well above .1, it was prima facie evidence of intoxication without regard to the number of prior offenses; (2) thus, he was not injured by the lower threshold for the presumption for persons with two or more prior convictions; (3) defendant did not have standing to challenge the statute as unconstitutional, because he failed to show that he was injured by the statute and that he was within the zone intended to have been protected by the constitutional guarantee; and (4) the court declined to reach defendant's constitutional issues because resolution of the issue of standing disposed of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of convictions from the trial court.

 

1091 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Green


No. 96-3140-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


217 Wis. 2d 288; 577 N.W.2d 386; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 111



February 3, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICIA D. MCMAHON and MICHAEL J. BARRON, Judges. 1.


1 The Hon. Patricia D. McMahon presided over the plea and sentencing hearings and entered the judgment of conviction; the Hon. Michael J. Barron entered the order denying Green's motion for postconviction relief.

.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment and order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of second-degree intentional homicide.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first-degree reckless homicide. The State later filed an information for first-degree intentional homicide. Defendant then pled guilty to the charge of second-degree intentional homicide. Defendant challenged his conviction on the grounds that he was coerced into pleading guilty and that the trial court erred in failing to consider mitigating factors and by relying upon inaccurate information in sentencing him. On appeal, the court held that there was no evidence to support defendant's allegation that the State modified the charge to coerce defendant into pleading guilty. The court found that the State increased the charge upon further consideration and after realizing that the evidence could support a conviction of intentional homicide. Thus, the State did not abuse its discretion in altering the charge. Regarding defendant's contention that the trial court erred in sentencing him, the court found that the trial court considered defendant's prior offenses, the gravity of the homicide offense, and the need to protect the public from defendant's violent character. Also, defendant was unable to show that the trial court relied upon inaccurate information.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for second-degree intentional homicide.

State v. Gils


No. 96-3543-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


216 Wis. 2d 383; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 44



January 20, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JOHN J. DIMOTTO, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two counts of armed robbery, one count of aggravated battery, and one count of substantial battery. Defendant also appealed from an order denying his postconviction motion.


OVERVIEW: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of two counts of armed robbery, one count of aggravated battery, and one count of substantial battery. Defendant filed a postconviction motion that was denied. Upon review, the court affirmed. The court found defendant was denied effective assistance of counsel by his counsel's failure to obtain a copy of a preliminary hearing transcript to impeach a state's witness where counsel lacked a reasonable excuse for failing to obtain a copy. The court found, however, that the error did not require reversal where defendant was not prejudiced by the lack of the preliminary transcript because the inconsistent testimony was minor when compared to the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt. The court concluded the trial court erroneously communicated with the jury without defendant being present, but that the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because defendant's attorney was present during the conversation, the conversation did not occur in open court, and did not involve a legal problem. The court determined defendant was not entitled to an instruction on the lesser-included offense of substantial battery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment that convicted defendant of two counts of armed robbery, one count of aggravated battery, and one count of substantial battery.

Pfister v. Milwaukee Econ. Dev. Corp.


No. 96-0314


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


216 Wis. 2d 243; 576 N.W.2d 554; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 28


September 9, 1997, Oral Argument  
January 13, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL and CROSS-APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: GEORGE A. BURNS, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lienholder challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which granted partial summary judgment in favor of respondents, debtor and secured creditors, and one secured creditor challenged the grant of partial summary judgment to the lienholder in an action brought under Wis. Stat. §§ 109.03(5), 109.09(2).


OVERVIEW: A lienholder brought an action against the debtor and the secured creditors to enforce a wage lien against the debtor, which was the lienholder's former employer. The trial court granted partial summary judgment in favor of the lienholder and partial summary judgment in favor of a secured creditor against the lienholder. The parties sought review, and the court affirmed the grant of partial summary judgment in favor of the lienholder. The court held that Wis. Stat. §§ 109.03(5), 109.09(2) were intended to be applied retroactively to include the lienholder's claim. The court reversed the grant of partial summary judgment in favor of one secured creditor and held that Wis. Stat. §§ 109.03(5), 109.09(2) gave wage liens priority over all other secured claims, including pre-existing claims. The court construed the statutes to mean that a wage lien had priority over any secured claim that was not specifically excluded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of partial summary judgment in favor of the lienholder and reversed the grant of partial summary judgment in favor of one secured creditor in the lienholder's action to enforce a wage lien against the debtor.

 

1094 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Marcum v. Gudmanson


No. 96-3447


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


216 Wis. 2d 383; 576 N.W.2d 88; 1998 Wisc. App. LEXIS 2



January 8, 1998, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his state claims filed pursuant to Wis. Admin. Code § Doc 310.025(1) against respondents, certain prison employees. Petitioner further filed federal claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The employees argued that petitioner failed to exhaust his remedies under the inmate complaint review system. The court affirmed as to the state claims and reversed as to any federal claims. The corrections complaint officer filed an affidavit that stated he searched all records and did not find a request for review of the complaint which petitioner filed pursuant to Wis. Admin. Code § Doc 310.025(1). Petitioner's affidavit did not rebut the officer's assertion that no request for review was filed. The court concluded that no dispute of material fact existed as to whether petitioner exhausted his administrative remedies before filing the action and held that he did not. The court determined that the exhaustion requirement of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1997e(a) did not apply to petitioner's federal complaint because it was filed three days before the enactment of § 1997e(a). The court reversed the dismissal of petitioner's 42 U.S.C.S. 1983 claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of petitioners state claim against certain prison employees. The court reversed and remanded the dismissal of petitioner's federal claim against certain prison employees.

State v. Sankovich


No. 97-2313-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


216 Wis. 2d 117; 573 N.W.2d 902; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1502



December 23, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: JOHN R. RACE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin) entered defendant's conviction for operating under the influence of an intoxicant (OWI), second offense, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 347.39(1), a muffler ordinance, claiming that it was vague. The instant court held that an officer had probable cause to make an investigatory stop of defendant's vehicle on the basis of defendant's loud muffler. A determination on the constitutionality of the ordinance would not have negated the validity of the OWI arrest.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed.

 

1096 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown (In re Brown)


Nos. 96-1211, 96-1393


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


215 Wis. 2d 716; 573 N.W.2d 884; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1494


November 4, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
December 23, 1997, Decided  
December 23, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DIANE S. SYKES, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant allegedly sexually violent persons challenged orders from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which denied the allegedly sexually violent persons' requests for judicial substitution in civil commitment proceedings brought by respondent State under Wis. Stat. ch. 980.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied the allegedly sexually violent persons' requests for judicial substitution in civil commitment proceedings that the State instituted pursuant to Wis. Stat. ch. 980. On appeal, the court reversed the orders and remanded the cases to the trial court with directions to honor the requests for judicial substitution. The court concluded that the civil commitment procedure for sexually violent persons under Wis. Stat. ch. 980 was subject to the provisions of Wis. Stat. chs. 801-847. The court held that the right to judicial substitution embodied in Wis. Stat. § 801.58 applied to the civil commitment proceedings against the allegedly sexually violent persons because Wis. Stat. ch. 980 did not prescribe a different procedure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders that held that there was no right to judicial substitution in the State's civil commitment proceedings against the allegedly sexually violent persons. The court remanded the case with directions for the trial court to honor the allegedly sexually violent persons' requests for judicial substitution.

 

1097 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watson


No. 95-1067


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


216 Wis. 2d 112; 573 N.W.2d 899; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1426



December 11, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As revised December 15, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which determined that the State failed to establish probable cause to believe that defendant was subject to commitment under the sexual predator law, Wis. Stat. § 980. At the time when defendant had been about to complete serving his sentence on a false imprisonment conviction, the State had filed the commitment petition against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to a term of imprisonment on a false imprisonment conviction. When defendant was about to complete his sentence on that conviction, the State filed a petition to have defendant committed under the sexual predator law, Wis. Stat. § 980. The trial court dismissed the State's petition, as it determined that the State failed to establish probable cause to believe that defendant was subject to commitment. The court reversed the trial court's determination that § 980 was unconstitutional, but affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the petition. The court held (1) that the trial court erred when it determined that § 980 was unconstitutional, as the supreme court had upheld the law on several occasions; and (2) that the trial court properly dismissed the petition, as the State's expert witness's testimony was based on inadmissible evidence and was not admissible under § 907.03.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's ruling that the sexual predator law was unconstitutional. However, the court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the State's petition to commit defendant.

 

1098 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hansford


No. 97-0885-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1443



December 11, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFICATION BY COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three misdemeanors shortly after the effective date of 1995 Wis. Laws 427, § 2. Defendant filed a motion for a 12-person jury on the ground that Wis. Stat. § 756.096(3)(am), which reduced the number of jurors in misdemeanor cases from 12 to six, was unconstitutional. The trial court (Wisconsin) denied the motion. Defendant was convicted on two of the misdemeanor counts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that a series of appellate decisions had interpreted Wis. Const. art. I, §§ 5, 7 as requiring a 12-person jury in misdemeanor cases. The State responded that no Wisconsin case had held that legislatively mandated six-person juries in misdemeanor cases violated a defendant's constitutional right. The statute controlling the size of misdemeanor juries was used daily in the court system. Its constitutionality was a matter of statewide importance with administrative and fiscal implications. Because a decision on the issue could have affected a large number of pending and completed cases, the appellate court found that it was in the public interest to have the issue decided quickly and with finality. The arguments in the case required analysis and interpretation of the state constitution and previous decisions of the supreme court. These tasks were best performed by the supreme court.


OUTCOME: The case was certified to the supreme court to decide whether the statute reducing the number of jurors in misdemeanor cases from 12 to six violated the Wisconsin Constitution.

 

1099 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Buchanan


No. 96-2453-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


216 Wis. 2d 113; 573 N.W.2d 899; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1423



December 9, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICIA D. MCMAHON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County, Wisconsin, for three counts of second-degree sexual assault and one count of kidnapping. Defendant appealed his kidnapping conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of kidnapping and sexually assaulting an 85-year-old widow in her home. He contended that the evidence was insufficient to convict him of kidnapping because his confinement of the victim was solely incidental to the sexual assaults. Alternatively, he argued that Wisconsin's kidnapping statute was unconstitutionally vague and that the kidnapping charge was not appropriate. The appellate court noted that the State proved that defendant confined the victim without her consent and with the intent that she be held to service against her will, and held that the evidence was sufficient to establish the crime of kidnapping, regardless of the incidental role of that crime to the sexual assault. The appellate court further held that a party whose conduct was clearly proscribed by a statute in question did not have standing to challenge it on the grounds of being vague as it might be applied to others. The appellate court concluded that if any of the elements of proof of a crime required were different in the crimes charged, they could be considered separate crimes.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1100 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


St. Joseph's Hosp. v. Department of Health & Soc. Servs.


No. 97-0958


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


216 Wis. 2d 115; 573 N.W.2d 900; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1399



December 4, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospital appealed an order of the circuit court for Dane County (Wisconsin) from an order granting summary judgment to the defendant Department of Health and Social Services (DHSS). The hospital argued that DHSS exceeded its authority by adopting criteria that denied it supplemental funding as a rural hospital under Wis. Stat. § 49.45(5m).


OVERVIEW: DHSS established guidelines to establish which hospitals qualified for supplemental funding under the statute. The hospital did not qualify for the rural hospital adjustment, because its operating statistics exceeded the median amount for Wisconsin urban hospitals in each of three statistical categories. Because DHSS had at least one opportunity to analyze § 49.45(5m) and interpret the phrase "rural hospital" as it was used in that section, the court gave due weight deference to DHSS' interpretation. The hospital argued that DHSS' interpretation created an anomaly between its inpatient and outpatient hospital state plans. Therefore, according to the hospital, it qualified for the rural hospital adjustment for the outpatient services that it provided to Medicare and Medicaid participants, but not for inpatient services. Because DHSS reasonably distinguished outpatient services from inpatient services, the court concluded that DHSS' interpretation of "rural hospital" was reasonable. Further, because DHSS' rural hospital adjustment eligibility requirements were not irrational or arbitrary, the court concluded that the hospital was not denied its right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment was affirmed.

 

1101 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kevin L.C.


No. 97-1087-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


216 Wis. 2d 166; 576 N.W.2d 62; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1403


October 2, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
December 4, 1997, Released  
December 4, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Richland County: KENT C. HOUCK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and an order of the Circuit Court for Richland County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of one count of first-degree sexual assault of a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1) and three counts of exposing a child to harmful materials contrary to § 948.11(2)(a), and which denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court violated his constitutional right of confrontation by declaring a child victim of sexual assault "unavailable" to testify at trial, and admitting statements made by her to a social worker under the "residual" hearsay exception, Wis. Stat. § 908.045(6). He also argues that § 948.11, which criminalized the act of exposing a child to harmful materials, was unconstitutional because it did not require the State to prove defendant knew the recipient was a minor. The court rejected defendant's claims. The court concluded that the State satisfied the Confrontation Clause because it had produced the child, whose inability to recall the incident or to respond made her unavailable, and established that her out-of-court statement bore sufficient indicia of reliability. The statement had been given to an experienced social worker with no apparent motive to coerce the child or distort her statement. The court concluded that the lack of a scienter requirement in § 948.11(2)(a), regarding the age of a child, did not render it unconstitutional. The statute reasonably imposed upon defendant the obligation to ascertain the child's age.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of first-degree sexual assault of a child and three counts of exposing a child to harmful materials and its order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief.

 

1102 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Liszewski


No. 96-2395-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


215 Wis. 2d 322; 572 N.W.2d 901; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1370



November 25, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: LEE E. WELLS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being waived from juvenile court into the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), defendant pleaded guilty to attempted first-degree intentional homicide. He filed a postconviction motion to withdraw his plea on the grounds that his counsel was ineffective for not appealing the waiver into adult court. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that counsel was not ineffective because any appeal of the waiver would have been unsuccessful. Agreeing, the court first held that Wis. Stat. § 48.366(1)(a)(1), allowing the juvenile court to extend its jurisdiction in certain cases, clearly and unambiguously did not allow the juvenile court to extend jurisdiction to age 25 in attempted first-degree intentional homicide cases. Next, the court held, applying a rational basis test, that the statute did not violate either substantive due process or equal protection. The court stated that the legislature's intent in enacting the statute was to protect the community from violent juvenile offenders who had been adjudged delinquent by the juvenile court and who could otherwise have been released from custody as early as age 19. Viewed in this light, the court stated, the legislative decision to allow the juvenile court to extend jurisdiction in cases of completed first-degree intentional homicide, but not in cases of attempted first-degree intentional homicide, was reasonable because the legislature was entitled to view juveniles who committed homicide as more dangerous than those who only made attempts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1103 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 96-2961-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


215 Wis. 2d 84; 572 N.W.2d 496; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1312


April 2, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
November 6, 1997, Decided  
November 6, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B. O'BRIEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granted defendant's motion to dismiss sexual assault charges, holding that Wis. Stat. § 940.225(2)(c) was unconstitutionally vague when it proscribed sexual intercourse or sexual contact with a person who was temporarily or permanently incapable of appraising the person's conduct. Defendant had sexual contact on two occasions with one of the mildly retarded adults in his care. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The purported victim was a 22-year old man, who had no prior sexual experience. The court explained that the vagueness standard required the provision of fair notice of the prohibited conduct and an objective standard for enforcement of violations. The court pointed out that, in order for the State to convict defendant, it had to prove that defendant had sexual contact or sexual intercourse with the mildly retarded man, that the man suffered from a mental illness or deficiency, that the mental illness or deficiency rendered the man temporarily or permanently incapable of appraising his own conduct, and that defendant knew that the man had a mental illness or deficiency which rendered him temporarily or permanently incapable of appraising his own conduct. The court was unimpressed by defendant's contention that the statute had no objective standard because he was required to think about the mildly retarded man and whether he lacked the ability to appraise the proposed activity before engaging in sexual acts with him. The court found the statutory requirement little different from requiring one to ascertain the age of a potential sexual partner before initiating sexual contact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the cause with directions.
