Town of Grand Chute v. Gabriel


No. 97-1742


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


215 Wis. 2d 324; 572 N.W.2d 903; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1284



November 4, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: MICHAEL W. GAGE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin) that affirmed a municipal court conviction for obstructing streets/sidewalks in violation of Grand Chute, Wis., Code § 7.05; defendant claimed, inter alia, that the trial court used the wrong standard of review.


OVERVIEW: A police officer arrested defendant for violating § 7.05 after employees of a planned parenthood clinic reported that he was standing at the clinic's driveway entrance, forcing vehicles to stop, and attempting to force pamphlets through open windows. Defendant appealed the conviction without requesting a trial de novo. Thereafter, he declined to testify, yet attempted to introduce new evidence during closing argument. The appellate court held that the circuit court's review was limited under Wis. Stat. ch. 800.14(5) to an examination of the transcript of the municipal court hearing, which revealed sufficient evidence to support the conviction. The municipal court correctly outlined the procedures for the trial and gave defendant every opportunity to testify. Defendant's repeated waiver of the constitutionality issue precluded appellate review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1105 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zarnke


No. 97-1664-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


215 Wis. 2d 71; 572 N.W.2d 491; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1296


October 8, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
November 4, 1997, Released  
November 4, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Eau Claire County: BENJAMIN D. PROCTOR, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order from the circuit court for Eau Claire County (Wisconsin), which dismissed charges against defendant for distributing pictures of children engaged in sexually explicit conduct in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.05(1)(c). Defendant claimed that the statute unconstitutionally relieved the state from proving knowledge of the minority of the child by providing ignorance of age as an affirmative defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged under § 948.05 with capturing off the internet sexually explicit images of young boys and distributing copies of the pictures to others. The trial court dismissed the charges, but on appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the legislature did not intend the affirmative defense of ignorance of age of the child, set forth in § 948.05(3), to apply to those violations of § 948.05(1)(c) that did not concern face-to-face involvement with the child.Because defendant's charges did not concern face-to-face involvement, any burden shifting that could have resulted from the affirmative defense did not apply to his case. The court noted that the burden shifting was permissible in cases where the child's age could reasonably be ascertained, but that it would have been unreasonable to shift the burden in circumstances where it was impossible to employ any one of the statute's methods for ascertaining age.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order dismissing the charges against defendant.

 

1106 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pozo


No. 97-0881


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


214 Wis. 2d 593; 571 N.W.2d 925; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1264



October 30, 1997, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: DENNIS G. MONTABON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant inmate appealed the order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin) denying the inmate's Wis. Stat. § 974.06 postconviction motion to withdraw his guilty plea to a charge of possessing marijuana within 1,000 feet of school.


OVERVIEW: Police discovered a large quantity of cash in the inmate's pockets. One of the officers asked the inmate whether he had a job. The inmate indicated that he did not. The inmate asserted that this should have been suppressed, because he had not been advised of his Miranda rights. Initially the inmate was charged with two drug sale related offenses. Because these two charges were dismissed at the time of the inmate's plea, leaving only the possession charge, the inmate's statement, which went only to the two drug sale related offenses, was found on direct appeal to have played no role in his possession conviction. The inmate argued in the instant motion that, because he entered the plea believing that he was to retain the opportunity to appeal the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress, the appellate court had to conclude that the plea was not voluntarily or knowingly entered. The inmate could not establish that he failed to enter the plea knowingly, as the statement the inmate sought to suppress was immaterial to the charge of which he was convicted. The statement the inmate made was evidence of the drug sale charges, not of possession.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1107 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lawinger


No. 97-1924-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


214 Wis. 2d 594; 571 N.W.2d 926; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1272



October 30, 1997, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sauk County: PATRICK TAGGART, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of her conviction by the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin) for operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited blood alcohol concentration (PAC) in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding in a posted 15-mile-per-hour zone. She was given an Intoxilyzer test after failing several field sobriety tests. Defendant alleged that a motion to suppress evidence was improperly denied because the officer did not have a reasonable basis to stop her as the speed limit sign was illegal and contrary to a state statute. On appeal, the court affirmed. Although the State conceded that the speed limit sign was improperly posted, the court held that the officer was unaware at the time of the traffic stop that the speed limit sign was illegal. The court determined that the officer had a reasonable basis to stop defendant because he observed her driving at 27 miles per hour in a 15-mile-per-hour zone. Although defendant argued that the officer should have been aware that the traffic sign was illegal, the court found that the police were not required to check the validity of all traffic signs before they stopped someone for speeding. The court noted that, at the time of the stop, no court had found that the traffic sign, or the ordinance on which it was based, invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1108 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ruesch


No. 96-2280-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


214 Wis. 2d 548; 571 N.W.2d 898; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1279


March 7, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
October 30, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for La Crosse County: RAMONA A. GONZALEZ, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County, which convicted him of violating the stalking law, Wis. Stat. § 940.32.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of stalking. The court affirmed the conviction. Wis. Stat. § 940.32(4), which excepted various lawful conduct from the law, did not provide any elements of the crime of stalking and, thus, the State proved all the elements necessary to support a conviction of the violation charged. Moreover, § 940.32 was not unconstitutionally overbroad as applied by limiting defendant's "freedom of movement." Furthermore, the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it provided defendant with fair notice that his conduct would contravene the statute and the statute provided a "reasonable person" standard for evaluating defendant's conduct. Additionally. defendant's right to equal protection under the law had not been violated because the statutory distinction between defendant's conduct and labor disputes was rationally related to a valid legislative purpose. The stalking law did not create an arbitrary classification. Thus, defendant did not meet his burden of proving that the stalking law was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction.

 

1109 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Schmidt v. City of Kenosha


No. 96-2380


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


214 Wis. 2d 527; 571 N.W.2d 892; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1258


August 29, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
October 29, 1997, Decided  
October 29, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha County: ROBERT V. BAKER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, owners of land outside a city's limits, sought review of the grant of summary judgment by the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) in favor of respondents, the city and its common council, in the owners' action for a writ of certiorari to declare that Kenosha, Wis., Zoning Ordinance 79-94 (1994), establishing an airport zoning overlay ordinance up to three miles outside an airport, violated due process and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: The owners claimed that the ordinance, which placed permanent height and use restrictions on land outside of the city limits, was unconstitutional because it placed unreasonable restrictions upon their use of the land. They challenged the state's grant of extraterritorial zoning power to municipalities under Wis. Stat. § 114.136, and claimed that under the principle of "one man, one vote," they should have participated in the election of the officials responsible. On review, the court found that the state's grant of such power was constitutional because political subdivisions were states-in-miniature that were convenient agencies for exercise of the state's police powers to ensure public safety. The court noted that "one man, one vote" did not confer upon individuals the right to vote upon all decisions that affect them, and that state statutes were constitutional unless they rested on grounds wholly irrelevant to the achievement of the state's objective. The court affirmed and found that the common council acted within the bounds of its legislative field, had conducted two studies on land use and growth, and did no more than was authorized by statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment of the trial court in favor of the city and against the owners.

 

1110 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re JACOB D.M.


No. 97-1583


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


214 Wis. 2d 594; 571 N.W.2d 925; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1241



October 28, 1997, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DANIEL A. NOONAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which determined that she was unfit pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(8) and terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: A determination was made that the child was the product of an incestuous relationship. The department of family services brought an action to terminate the parental rights of the mother. The trial court found that the child was a product of an incestuous relationship as defined in Wis. Stat. § 48.415(7) and thereafter terminated the parental rights after determining pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.424(4) that the termination was in the best interest of the child. The mother asserted that the termination statute was unconstitutional because it violated her right of due process and equal protection. The court affirmed the decision that terminated the mother's parental rights and determined that the provision regarding incestuous relationships served compelling state interests in the welfare of children and preservation of the family and the termination did not deny equal protection because the mother's rights were not terminated for the status but after a determination that the termination was in the best interest of the child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court that determined that the other was unfit and terminated her parental rights.

 

1111 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Welter v. City of Milwaukee


No. 96-2770


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


214 Wis. 2d 485; 571 N.W.2d 459; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1240


October 7, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
October 28, 1997, Decided  
October 28, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MICHAEL J. BARRON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) granting summary judgment to respondent class of police officers, in an action for a declaratory judgment that the officers' conversion-age rights were vested when they were first hired by the city and became members of the retirement system.


OVERVIEW: The officers' existing retirement benefits were converted to a service allowance plan at an age lower than the conversion-age in effect when they were hired and became members of the state employee retirement system, thus resulting in a reduction of benefits. The court held that the conversion-age rights vested when the class members were first hired and became members of the retirement system. Given the clear statewide concern to have an efficient, dependable police force functioning in the city, the city could not, under its home rule powers, reduce police-officer retirement-system benefits without the officers' consent below the level existing when the officers were hired. Chapter 441 of the Laws of 1947 §§ 30(2) and 31 were dispositive of this issue. There was no evidence that the officers agreed to allow its union to bargain away their vested rights. The class members were not estopped from objecting to the lower conversion ages agreed to by their union. Receipt of a pension installment payment that was less than that required by contract was a separate breach of that contract and members had six years to sue on any pension installment that was less than it should have been.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court entering summary judgment declaring that the city may not reduce below the conversion-age in effect when a member was hired.

 

1112 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Elfers by Drill v. St. Paul Fire & Marine Ins. Co.


No. 96-3516


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


214 Wis. 2d 499; 571 N.W.2d 469; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1237


September 15, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
October 28, 1997, Released  
October 28, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Polk County: JAMES R. ERICKSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a patient and her parents, appealed the summary judgment granted by the Circuit Court for Polk County (Wisconsin) in favor of defendants, doctors and their insurers, in the patient's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: The child fell from her bicycle and was injured. The doctors treated her for a broken arm, but failed to diagnose a dislocated elbow. Four years later, the arm was x-rayed for an unrelated injury, and it was noted that the elbow was dislocated. Because the elbow was not causing any problems at the time, it was not treated. Four years later, the child began experiencing pain and difficulties in range of motion related to the elbow. The child and her parents filed a malpractice action against the doctors and their insurers. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the doctors and their insurers based on the expiration of the statute of limitations. The child and her parents appealed. The court reversed and remanded. The court held that there was a fact issue as to when a compensable injury actually occurred; therefore, summary judgment was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's summary judgment, which had been in favor of the doctors and their insurers, in the malpractice action filed by the child and her parents.

 

1113 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen M. (In the Interest of Tiffany Nicole M.)


No. 97-0852


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


214 Wis. 2d 302; 571 N.W.2d 872; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1205


September 9, 1997, Oral Argument  
October 21, 1997, Decided  
October 21, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: THOMAS R. COOPER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that, upon the petition of respondent State, terminated their parental rights to one of their daughters based on the parents' incestuous relationship.


OVERVIEW: The parents, biological siblings, participated in an ongoing incestuous relationship that produced three children. The parents abandoned one child at the home of a babysitter. The child was removed from her home and placed in foster care. The juvenile court found the child to be a Child in Need of Protection or Services pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.13(10). The State filed a petition to terminate the parental rights of the parents to the child on the grounds of their incestuous parenthood. A doctor testified that the child, three-and-one-half years old, was previously non-verbal, was not toilet trained, and was not able to feed herself, but had made great progress after time with the foster family. The trial court terminated the parental rights of the parents to the child pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 48.415(7). Affirming the order, the court held that § 48.415(7) was constitutional and was narrowly tailored to serve the State's compelling interests in the welfare of children, preservation of family, and maintenance of an ordered society. The court found that § 48.415(7) did not violate the parents' equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that terminated the parental rights of the parents to a child based on the parents' incestuous relationship.

 

1114 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


City of Monroe v. Furgason


Nos. 97-0891, 97-0892


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


214 Wis. 2d 593; 571 N.W.2d 925; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1191



October 16, 1997, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Green County: JAMES R. BEER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Green County (Wisconsin), which in consolidated cases convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence and with a prohibited alcohol concentration in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and (b).


OVERVIEW: A police officer, after hearing defendant's motorcycle when it was more than two blocks away, stopped defendant to issue a citation for a muffler violation. On appeal defendant argued that the muffler ordinance, Monroe, Wis., City Code § 10-2-1 was unconstitutionally vague, thereby invalidating the stop. The court noted that the United States Supreme Court had already determined that ordinances that prohibited loud noises on motor vehicles did not restrict the communication or discussion of ideas within the meaning of the First Amendment. The court held that a person of ordinary intelligence would have been placed on notice by the ordinance to have an adequate and properly maintained muffler so that his motorcycle could not have been heard from two blocks away. While determinations of what was "excessively loud" must necessarily have been made within an officer's judgment on a case by case basis, standards for the enforcement of the ordinance did exist and were properly applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1115 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re Thomas B.


No. 97-1345


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


214 Wis. 2d 593; 571 N.W.2d 925; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1142



October 8, 1997, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: GARY LANGHOFF, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, juvenile, challenged the dispositional order of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County, Wisconsin, adjudicating him delinquent on one count of disorderly conduct in violation of Wis. Stat. § 947.01, and one count of carrying a concealed weapon contrary to Wis. Stat. § 941.23, and challenged the denial of his motion to dismiss based on the right to juvenile jury trials.


OVERVIEW: The victim reported that while she was inside of her apartment with the windows open she overheard appellant standing below the window telling other boys "oh, that's the car I walked over the other night." The victim's vehicle had been damaged while parked on the street. Appellant was brought to police, and prior to a pat-down, appellant was asked if he was in possession of anything the officer should be aware of. Appellant stated that he had two razor blades in his back pocket, which he carried because people were out to get him and he was afraid. Appellant argued that the juvenile court erred in denying his motion. The appellate court ruled that the denial of the motion to dismiss was proper, as juveniles did not have a state or federal constitutional right to a jury trial. Concerning the concealed weapon adjudication, the appellate court ruled that the State failed to set forth facts demonstrating appellant used or intended to use the razor blades in a threatening manner. Appellant's statements as to his fear for his safety were ordered suppressed, and mere possession without more was insufficient to prove concealment of a weapon.


OUTCOME: Denial of the motion to dismiss was affirmed, and the concealed weapon adjudication was reversed and remanded for a new dispositional hearing on the remaining count of disorderly conduct.

 

1116 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Janssen


No. 97-1316-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


213 Wis. 2d 471; 570 N.W.2d 746; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1115


September 2, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
September 30, 1997, Decided  
September 30, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Outagamie County: JOHN A. DES JARDINS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed from the judgment and order of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin) which dismissed the state's charge of flag desecration against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stole several United States flags and defecated on one. He was charged with theft and flag desecration. Defendant brought a facial challenge to the constitutionality of the flag desecration statute, arguing that it was both vague and overbroad. The trial court agreed and dismissed the count of flag desecration. Defendant was convicted for the thefts. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the flag desecration statute was unconstitutional. Although defendant lacked standing to assert a vagueness challenge against the statute, and his conduct clearly and unambiguously fell within the statutory prohibition against defiling the flag, the part of the statute making it unlawful to cast contempt upon the flag was so vague as to set no standard by which defendant's conduct could be measured. "Casting contempt upon the flag" was language too subjective to guide enforcement of the statute as it did not give reasonable notice as to what conduct was prohibited. The statute was overbroad because the language encompassed acts that constituted protected expression and actually deterred protected expression in a real and substantial way.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the charge of flag desecration against defendant.

 

1117 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kittleson


No. 97-0324


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


213 Wis. 2d 486; 570 N.W.2d 911; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1045



September 16, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Langlade County: JAMES P. JANSEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Langlade County (Wisconsin), which denied his Wis. Stat. § 974.06 motion challenging his 1995 conviction for the offense of firearm possession by a felon, a violation of Wis. Stat. § 941.29.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a felony in Iowa in 1974. He was lately convicted of offending Wis. Stat. § 941.29, which criminalized firearm possession by a felon. He claimed that § 941.29 was an unconstitutional ex post facto law, retroactively punishing him for the 1974 Iowa felony conviction. In affirming the judgment the court held that § 941.29 was not an ex post facto law, because it did not criminalize prior conduct. The court held that § 941.29 criminalized present conduct - the possession of a firearm. The court explained that the prior felony conviction was a predicate to the offense. This was simply a condition precedent to the prosecution for the current firearm possession, and did not raise ex post facto concerns. The court noted that generally a state was free to restrict felons' conduct for the protection of its citizens' health, safety, and welfare.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of firearm possession by a felon.

 

1118 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


County of Walworth v. O'Donnell


No. 97-1084


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


213 Wis. 2d 486; 570 N.W.2d 912; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 998



September 3, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Walworth County: JOHN R. RACE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court for Walworth County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of intoxicant contrary to Wisc. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a), entered after defendant stipulated to a plea of no contest. The stipulation also provided that the imposition of the sentence would be stayed pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of Wisc. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a) and Wis. Admin. Code § 112.05(3)(b). The court dismissed the appeal and found that defendant waived his right to appeal by stipulating to entry of a judgment. Therefore, the court reasoned it need not address defendant's constitutional claims. The court found that defendant could not, by stipulating to the entry of a conditional judgment, obtain a mandatory appeal of an interlocutory order. The court reasoned that a contrary holding would have allowed defendant to circumvent the waiver and finality rules and convert a discretionary interlocutory appeal into an appeal as a matter of right from final judgment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal of the trial court's judgment of conviction.

 

1119 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Knowlin v. Director, Office of Offender Classification


No. 97-0368


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


213 Wis. 2d 123; 570 N.W.2d 253; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 985



August 28, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: PAUL B. HIGGINBOTHAM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed his action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 against defendants, employees of the state Department of Corrections.


OVERVIEW: A prison committee recommended that the inmate participate in a treatment program. Eligibility in the program was conditioned upon an inmate signing a program contract. The inmate brought an action alleging the infringement of his constitutional rights and violations of state law stemming from the conditions for participation in the program. The trial court dismissed the action on the ground that the inmate failed to exhaust administrative remedies as required under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1997e(a) and Wis. Stat. § 801.02(7). The court affirmed. Under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1997e(a), a claim alleging violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 could not be brought if the inmate did not exhaust administrative remedies that the Department had promulgated. Pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 801.02(7), the inmate was required to utilize the Inmate Complaint Review System (ICRS) before seeking court review of determinations regarding placement and classification. Under Wis. Admin. Code §§ DOC 310.04(2), 310.04(5), the ICRS permitted the inmate to seek a change of institutional policies or practices and to file civil rights complaints. Thus, the inmate failed to exhaust administrative remedies available to him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

1120 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Jackson v. Benson


No. 97-0270


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


213 Wis. 2d 1; 570 N.W.2d 407; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 973


July 22, 1997, Oral Argument  
August 22, 1997, Released  
August 22, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: PAUL B. HIGGINBOTHAM, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Milwaukee Parental Choice Program (MPCP), Wis. Stat. § 119.23, provided funds for public school students to attend nonsectarian private schools. When the MPCP was amended by 1995 Wis. Law 27, §§ 4002-4009 to cover sectarian schools, appellees, citizens, teachers, and associations, challenged the constitutionality of the amended MPCP. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) ordered that the MPCP was unconstitutional. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: Citizens, teachers, and associations filed an action against the state pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. I and the religious benefits clause of Wis. Const. art. I, § 18 which challenged the constitutionality of the Milwaukee Parental Choice Program (MPCP), Wis. Stat. § 119.23, as amended by 1995 Wis. Law 27, §§ 4002-4009. The trial court issued an order that the MPCP was unconstitutional under Wis. Const. art. I, § 18. The state sought review. The court held that the trial court properly ordered that the MPCP violated § 18 because it directed the payment of state funds for the education of students at private sectarian schools and thus violated the prohibition against state expenditures for the benefit of religious societies or seminaries. The court held that the invalidation of the MPCP did not violate the Free Exercise Clause of the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The order of the circuit court declaring the Milwaukee Parental Choice Program unconstitutional was affirmed.

 

1121 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Joseph W. v. Catholic Diocese


No. 96-2220


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 925; 569 N.W.2d 795; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 965


February 10, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
August 21, 1997, Decided  
August 21, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a man and his parents, sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which entered summary judgment, dismissing as time-barred appellants' claims against respondent church and diocese. Appellants sought recovery for personal injuries and alleged, among other things, that a priest at the church had sexually abused the man when, as a child, he had attended religious instruction classes at the church.


OVERVIEW: The man had been abused by the priest on numerous occasions as a young teenager but did not reveal the assaults until nearly 10 years after they occurred. The priest had abused several other boys during the same time period and, because they had told their parents, the diocese removed the priest from the church. The man's parents, however, were never told why the priest was removed and, although they sought the help of professionals, never learned why their son had become troubled nor why he had attempted suicide on several occasions. Upon learning of the assaults on their son, the parents filed their claims at the time their son filed his. The court, in affirming the trial court's judgment, agreed that all of the claims were barred by the statute of limitations. The court found that, although the parents' claims were different from the man's, they were derivative and had accrued when the son's did. The court held that the causes of action had accrued on the date of the last assault and, even allowing the parents' claims the benefit of the tolling provisions relating to the son's period of minority as provided under Wis. Stat. 893.16(1), found that the claims were time-barred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which granted summary judgment and dismissed the tort claims of the man and his parents against the church and the diocese.

Schmeling v. Phelps


No. 96-2661


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 898; 569 N.W.2d 784; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 946


June 6, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
August 14, 1997, Released  
August 14, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county executive challenged the decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which invalidated his veto of plaintiff landowner's petition to rezone a parcel of real estate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant county executive sought review of the trial court's invalidation of his veto of plaintiff landowner's petition to rezone a parcel of real estate. Reviewing the matter de novo, the court found that the veto was a legislative act for which judicial review was limited to abuse of discretion, excess of power, or error of law. The court reversed the judgment that invalidated the veto because defendant did not abuse his discretion, exceed his power, or commit an error of law in exercising his veto. The court rejected the trial court's substitution of its judgment for that of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that invalidated defendant county executive's veto of plaintiff landowner's petition to rezone because defendant did not abuse his discretion, exceed his power, or commit an error of law in exercising his veto.

 

1123 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Slawinski v. Milwaukee City Fire & Police Comm'n


Nos. 96-1347 & 96-1524-W


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 777; 569 N.W.2d 740; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 746


May 28, 1997, Oral Argument  
August 12, 1997, Released  
August 12, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICK J. MADDEN, Judge. PETITION for a supervisory writ to the circuit court for Milwaukee County: PATRICK J. MADDEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed. Writ granted, judgment reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, City of Milwaukee Fire and Police Commission and the City of Milwaukee Fire and Police Commissioners Board (FPC), petitioned the court for a supervisory writ ordering the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), either to affirm the demotion of appellee police officer or to apply the statutory review standards in what the FPC considers the required manner following the circuit court's reversal of the demotion action.


OVERVIEW: Following an internal investigation, the police officer was demoted and six charges for causing a disruption, hindering the efficient operation of the department, and making derogatory comments were filed with the Board, which dismissed two of the charges and upheld the demotion. The police officer sought circuit court review of the Board's decision. The circuit court concluded, based on the evidence that the rules were unconstitutionally vague and adequate notice of the charges were not given to the officers. The court held that the issuance of a writ was controlled by equitable principles and, in its discretion, the court would consider the rights of the public and third parties. In granting the writ of supervision, the court concluded that the circuit court did not exceed its authority, under Wis. Stat. § 62.50(21), by considering constitutional due process issues as part of its overall evaluation of the reasonableness of the Board's decision. However, the circuit court erred in basing its decision on those issues without first affording the parties the opportunity to develop a factual record before the Board and offer argument before the circuit court.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition for a supervisory writ. It reversed the circuit court's decision and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1124 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ruiz


No. 96-1610-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


213 Wis. 2d 200; 570 N.W.2d 556; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 926


April 23, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
August 7, 1997, Decided  
August 7, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Wood County: EDWARD F. ZAPPEN, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court for Wood County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of possession of marijuana with intent to deliver, while possessing a weapon, and failure to purchase drug tax stamps.


OVERVIEW: According to an anticipatory search warrant, an investigator stated that on a particular date there would be, upon delivery, a shipping package containing 20 pounds of marijuana at defendant's address, or upon the persons at that address. The warrant further stated that the investigator asked for a no-knock warrant to search the premises for the marijuana and drug paraphernalia. The court held that reversal of the drug tax stamp conviction was required because the drug tax stamp law had been found unconstitutional on the ground that it violated the right against self-incrimination. However, the court determined that the anticipatory search warrant was constitutionally sufficient because it clearly implied that the search was not to commence until the marijuana was delivered. Until delivery, the contraband for which the warrant was issued would not be on the premises. The court did not believe that the warrant could be misunderstood by officers as allowing a search of the premises before delivery. The court concluded that remand was required because the trial court determined that the no-knock warrant was justified under the blanket exception of a case that had been overruled.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court for a hearing on the issue of whether a "no-knock" warrant was justified under the facts and circumstances of the case.

 

1125 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Curtis


No. 96-1987-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


213 Wis. 2d 122; 570 N.W.2d 252; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 907



August 5, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) convicting him, after a jury trial, of possession of a controlled substance, second or subsequent offense; obstructing or resisting an officer; and failure to pay controlled substance tax and denying his postconviction motion for a new trial. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in presiding over the matter because he had filed a timely substitution motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant also argued on appeal that his conviction for failing to pay a controlled substance tax violated his constitutional rights against compelled self-incrimination and double jeopardy. On appeal, the court concluded that the trial court committed reversible error in presiding over defendant's trial and that defendant's conviction for violating the drug stamp law could not stand. The court reversed and remanded. The court noted that the Wisconsin Supreme Court had recently struck down the drug stamp law as unconstitutional. The court further found that the record reflected that once defendant found out that the judge was to preside over his case, he filed a substitution motion. Although the motion was filed after the arraignment deadline prescribed in Wis. Stat. § 971.20(4), the deadline should have been relaxed because the intake system did not provide adequate notice of the assigned judge in advance of arraignment. Accordingly, the court concluded that defendant's substitution motion was timely filed. It was, therefore, reversible error for the judge to preside over defendant's trial. On remand, the court directed the new trial was to be held before a different trial judge.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed and cause remanded with directions.

 

1126 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Heier's Trucking v. Waupaca County


No. 96-3711


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 593; 569 N.W.2d 352; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1010


June 6, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
July 31, 1997, DATED AND RELEASED  
July 31, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waupaca County: DEE R. DYER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a county and solid waste board, sought review after the Circuit Court for Waupaca County (Wisconsin) entered a judgment in favor of plaintiff transporter, which declared that the "flow control" provision of Waupaca County, Wis., Recycling Ordinance § 20.15, was invalid and unenforceable on the grounds that it violated the Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The recycling ordinance required all recyclables collected in municipalities that had designated the county as the "responsible unit" to be delivered to the Waupaca County Processing Facility pursuant to § 20.15(1). The transporter operated its own certified processing facility. After receiving 33 citations for failing to deliver recyclable materials to the county processing facility in violation of the ordinance, the transporter filed an action for declaratory judgment challenging the validity and constitutionality of the county ordinance. The trial court held that ch. 20 and related provisions of § 20.22 of the ordinance were invalid and unenforceable. The court affirmed. The Commerce Clause applied because the county's flow control ordinance was market regulation. The ordinance allowed only one processor to process the waste for the municipalities that had designated the county as the responsible unit, thereby precluding all other in-state and all out-of-state businesses from performing the service. The county had available nondiscriminatory measures to address the health and safety issues posed by waste disposal and to insure the financial viability of its processing facility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the transporter.

 

1127 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Pace v. Oneida County


No. 96-3514


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 448; 569 N.W.2d 311; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 836


June 23, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
July 22, 1997, Released  
July 22, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Oneida County: MARK A. MANGERSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant boathouse owner brought an action against respondent Oneida County, seeking review of the denial of his application for a permit to reconstruct his wet boathouse. While the owner's appeal was pending, Wis. Stat. § 30.121(3r), permitting the rebuilding of wet boathouses, was enacted. The Circuit Court for Oneida County (Wisconsin) concluded that § 30.121(3r) was an unconstitutional private bill, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner's application for reconstruction of his wet boathouse was denied pursuant to a County zoning ordinance, which precluded such reconstruction when the cost exceeded 50 percent of the value of the property destroyed. The owner contended that the zoning ordinance was preempted by Wis. Stat. § 30.121(3r), which provided that prohibitions against the building or reconstruction of wet boathouses when the cost exceeded 50 percent of the equalized assessed value did not apply to wet boathouses damaged by violent wind, vandalism, or fire after January 1, 1984. On review, the court held that § 30.121(3r) was constitutional and preempted the County's zoning ordinance. The statute was not a private bill because it applied to all wet boathouses in the State of Wisconsin destroyed by violent wind, vandalism, or fire. The classification created by the selection of a date prior to which rebuilding or repair was not permitted was reasonable, as was the limitation to specific natural forces. The statute's modification of law to change judicial results was a proper legislative action and did not violate the separation of powers between the judicial and legislative branches.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

1128 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Melvin Range, Inc.


No. 95-3570


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


212 Wis. 2d 638; 570 N.W.2d 61; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 825



July 17, 1997, Released

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant owner appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted the owner of group axle overload and imposed forfeiture.


OVERVIEW: The owner was charged with violating Wis. Stat. § 348.15(3)(c). The state alleged that a truck driven by the owner's agent was carrying a load on the highway that was overweight. The owner filed a motion to suppress, claiming that the driver was arrested without probable cause. The owner further sought dismissal of the action, claiming that § 348.15 was unconstitutional. The trial court denied both motions. After a stipulated bench trial, the trial court entered a judgment of conviction and a forfeiture order, but the time to appeal had elapsed by the time the parties received notice of the order. After additional procedural questions were resolved, the trial court conducted a new trial, again convicting the owner, and again imposing the forfeiture. The owner appealed. The court first held that the trial court properly granted the owner a new trial given the circumstances of the case. The court then affirmed the trial court's refusal of the owner's suppression motion, holding that the stop of the truck and the detainment of the driver were made with probable cause. Finally, the court held that the forfeiture statute did not impose an unconstitutionally excessive fine.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court.

 

1129 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hammad


No. 95-2669


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 343; 569 N.W.2d 68; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 801


February 4, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
July 15, 1997, Dated and Released  
July 15, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: LAURENCE C. GRAM, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant car owner appealed from orders of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which permitted the civil forfeiture of his automobile and denied his motion for reconsideration. The owner argued that the forfeiture action violated the Excessive Fines Clause of the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: During a sting operation, the owner asked an undercover officer to load stolen merchandise in the trunk of the owner's car. The trial court granted plaintiff State of Wisconsin's demand for forfeiture of the car under Wis. Stat. § 973.075(1)(b) and denied a motion for reconsideration. On appeal, the court agreed that the forfeiture implicated the protections guaranteed by the Eighth Amendment's Excessive Fines Clause, but concluded that the forfeiture did not violate the Eighth Amendment. In so holding, the court first noted that a forfeiture under § 973.075(1)(b) was a punishment subject to the limitations of the Excessive Fines Clause. As to whether the forfeiture in the instant case was "excessive" within the meaning of the Eighth Amendment, the case presented an issue of first impression. Using a 1954 Wisconsin Supreme Court decision, the court concluded that the so-called Seraphine multi-factor standard was to be used when analyzing whether a forfeiture of a vehicle under § 973.075(1)(b) was "excessive" within the meaning of the Eighth Amendment. Under that standard, the forfeiture was not excessive because it was neither disproportionate to the crime nor unusual in nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's orders.

State v. Zanelli


No. 96-2159


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 358; 569 N.W.2d 301; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 797


May 13, 1997, Oral Argument  
July 15, 1997, Dated and Released  
July 15, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Outagamie County: DEE R. DYER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner was convicted of two counts of sexual contact with a child, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2). The Circuit Court, Outagamie County (Wisconsin) ordered the prisoner committed to the care of the Department of Health and Social Services. He challenged his civil commitment as a sexually violent person pursuant to the sexual predator law.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted of two counts of sexual contact with a child, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2). Shortly before parole was granted on the first count, respondent State filed a Wis. Stat. § 980 petition alleging that the prisoner had a mental disorder and was dangerous to others because the disorder created a substantial probability of additional sexual violence. The prisoner was ordered committed to the care of the Department of Health and Social Services. The court held that the comments by a psychologist and the prosecutor at trial concerning the prisoner's refusal to be interviewed violated his right to remain silent as provided in Wis. Stat. § 980.05(1m). The Fifth Amendment protected a person from compelled self-incrimination at all times. The court ordered a new trial. The prisoner elected not testify in his own behalf. When the witness and the prosecutor commented on the prisoner's silence, they violated the rule made applicable to the prisoner by virtue of § 980.05(1m), which extended to the subject of a sexual predator trial all the constitutional rights available to a defendant in a criminal proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order, which committed the prisoner to the care of the Department of Health and Social Services pursuant to the sexual predator law. The case was remanded.

Town of Delafield v. Sharpley


No. 96-2458


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 332; 568 N.W.2d 779; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 790


May 22, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
July 9, 1997, Dated and Released  
July 9, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MARK GEMPELER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adjacent landowners challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) in favor of appellee town in the town's complaint of public nuisance, pursuant to Town of Delafield, Wis. Ordinances §§ 10.01, 10.02, 10.05.


OVERVIEW: The adjacent landowners' property was fraught with unworkable cars, trucks, snowmobiles, and one school bus that seemed to house an inhabitant. Hornets' nests had accumulated in the associated junk. Because a single-family neighborhood was nearby, and because the condition of the property violated §§ 10.01, 10.02, 10.05, the town filed a public nuisance action against the landowners. The town filed motions for summary judgment, which were granted as to all claims except one. A trial was had on that final claim and the jury found for the landowners. The trial court granted a judgment notwithstanding the verdict. The landowners appealed. On review, the court found that summary judgment was rightly granted because one of the adjacent landowners did not file an affidavit disputing the town's claims, while the other landowner's affidavit contained entirely conclusory statements. Finally, the court agreed with the trial court in setting aside the jury verdict because the landowners did not have a valid and legal nonconforming use of their properties. Thus, the landowners' claim that their property was subject to a "grandfather clause" was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the town.

 

1132 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baldwin


Nos. 96-1013-CR, 96-2822


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 245; 569 N.W.2d 37; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 717


April 29, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
July 2, 1997, Dated and Released  
July 2, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Sheboygan County: L. EDWARD STENGEL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: No. 96-1013-CR, Affirmed. No. 96-2822, Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants sought review of two separate judgments of the Circuit Court for Sheboygan County (Wisconsin), which convicted each defendant for operating a motor vehicle while having a prohibited alcohol concentration (OMVPAC) and for operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated (OMVWI). The appeals were consolidated by the court and transferred for decision by a three-judge panel.


OVERVIEW: Each defendant separately claimed that his trial court erred in its failure to suppress the breath test results from an untested, unevaluated, and unapproved test instrument. The instrument included components of an approved model and contained replacement parts from an unapproved model where the model was obsolete. The first defendant was convicted of a first offense of both OMVPAC and OMVWI. The second defendant was convicted of a second offense of OMVPAC and OMVWI. The court held that: (1) where test results were obtained using an instrument not evaluated and approved as required by in Wis. Stat. § 343.305(6)(b) and Wis. Admin. Code § Trans 311.04 (1993), the results were no longer entitled to automatic admissibility or to a prima facie presumption of accuracy to establish a defendant's blood alcohol level; and (2) in such cases, prosecutors who wished to rely upon the breath test results were required to present evidence of the instrument's scientific accuracy and reliability and prove compliance with accepted scientific methods as a foundation for the admission of the test results.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed one defendant's conviction for OMVWI as a second offense. The court reversed the second defendant's conviction for OMVPAC as a first offense and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Moore


No. 96-3050-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


212 Wis. 2d 242; 568 N.W.2d 785; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 712



June 26, 1997, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: MICHAEL NOWAKOWSKI, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two counts of disorderly conduct, arising from separate incidents at two university campus libraries.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was approached at a campus library after an employee received complaints he was watching a pornographic video in the multimedia center. Defendant refused to produce identification and left. A few days later a university police officer was dispatched to a campus library after an employee received complaints defendant was watching pornographic material. The officer asked for identification and defendant was arrested and issued a citation. On appeal, the court held it would not substitute its judgment for that of the trier of fact unless the evidence, viewed most favorably to the State and conviction, was so lacking in probative value that no trier of fact acting reasonably, could have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The court rejected defendant's claim that the police provoked him, and that the police asking defendant for identification did not qualify as provocation. The court held it was true that when a police officer required a person to identify himself and prevented him from leaving, the officer performed a seizure subject to the requirements of the Fourth Amendment. However, defendant was free to leave the library and thus his arrest was lawful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Krebs v. Schwartz


No. 96-2596


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


212 Wis. 2d 127; 568 N.W.2d 26; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 650


May 9, 1997, Submitted On Briefs  
June 11, 1997, Released  
June 11, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: BARBARA A. KLUKA, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner challenged the order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) denying his petition for writ of certiorari for review of respondent Division of Hearings and Appeals' (division) determination revoking his probation.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was convicted of first-degree sexual assault of his daughter. He received a stayed prison term and was placed on conditional probation. However he was cited for various violations of his probation and it was revoked. The petitioner argued that the probation condition requiring him to discuss and receive approval from his probation agent before he engaged in an intimate relationship with an adult female was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the revocation of the petitioner's probation and held that the intimate contact condition was both reasonable, not overly broad, and related to the petitioner's rehabilitation. Although it may have been a constriction of a constitutional right, it was not a denial of it. The condition was rationally related to the petitioner's rehabilitation because it forced him to be honest with others by confronting and admitting to his sexually deviant behavior. Moreover, it served to protect the public. The court concluded that it was absurd for the petitioner to presuppose that he could select which treatment program he was willing to attend.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of the petitioner's request for a writ of certiorari.

Devinn C. v. Shelly S.

In addition, § 48.415(2) was constitutional because there were sufficient facts to warrant termination of rights.

Village of DeForest v. County of Dane


No. 96-1574


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


211 Wis. 2d 804; 565 N.W.2d 296; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 562


March 14, 1997, Oral Argument  
May 22, 1997, RELEASED  
May 22, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from orders of the circuit court for Dane County: ANGELA B. BARTELL, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff village sought a declaratory judgment in the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) to have the county zoning board's approval of cross-defendant applicant's conditional use permit overturned. The trial court granted the village summary judgment and denied the applicant's motion. The applicant sought appellate review of the summary judgment and the trial court's dismissal of its counterclaim for damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Under Wis. Stat. § 62.23(7a), the village adopted an interim ordinance for the designated extraterritorial area. The ordinance adopted by reference all then-effective zoning district designations, regulations and use restrictions and provided that the enforcement and administration of the zoning ordinances, including the approval of all conditional use permits, and other former county functions would be handled by the appropriate village board or official. The applicant sought a conditional use variance after the ordinance was adopted but submitted it to the county board rather than to the village board. The court held that all ordinances enacted under § 62.23(7a) were to be liberally construed in favor of cities and villages. The court affirmed the trial court's holding that the village was entitled to a summary judgment due to the applicant's failure to apply for a conditional use permit from it. The court held that the enactment of the interim ordinance did not adversely affect any vested right of the applicant and that the applicant's claim for compensatory relief for a § 1983 violation was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders entered by the trial court and found that the applicant failed to comply with the applicable zoning regulation and that its cause of action under § 1983 was unwarranted.

Debra J.S. v. Thomas L. (In re Stephanie A.L.)


No. 96-1785


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


211 Wis. 2d 889; 568 N.W.2d 652; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 565



May 21, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: ROBERT A. HAASE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a paternity case, petitioner State of Wisconsin appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Winnebago County (Wisconsin) declaring the tax intercept statute, former Wis. Stat. § 46.255(1) (1993-1994), unconstitutional as applied and voiding an interception of respondent father's income tax refund to pay for birth expenses.


OVERVIEW: The State and the father entered into a stipulation resolving all issues in the paternity action. The father was to pay the child's birth medical expenses in weekly installments. The father had remained current on the obligation. Former Wis. Stat. § 46.255(1) (1993-94), providing for the placement of a lien on income tax returns, was amended to apply to those who owed an outstanding amount in birth expense payments as of June 11, 1994. Where the department of revenue intercepted the father's tax returns, the trial court found that the State was not permitted to not fulfill the stipulation that it had made with the father and that application of former § 46.255(1) was a violation of due process. The issue concerning former § 46.255(1) was moot, because the father was paid the intercepted refund. The issue was not reviewable under an exception to the mootness doctrine. Former § 446.255(1) may not have applied to the case, as it was not enacted until after the father entered the stipulations. Also, the issue, whether a pre-1994 judgment debt covered by an installment stipulation was governed by former § 446.255(1), may not have recurred.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

Village of Tigerton v. Minniecheske

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners' association sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin), which granted judgment in favor of respondent Village of Tigerton and enjoined the association from filing the action against the Village without prior approval of the trial court under the harassment injunction statute, Wis. Stat. § 813.125.


OVERVIEW: The association initiated an action against the Village when they were restricted from entering the Village's property. The trial court enjoined the association from filing the action without prior approval under the harassment injunction statute, Wis. Stat. § 813.125. The association sought review. The court held that the trial court had the authority to deny the association the right to initiate the action and further determined that such authority was not an infringement upon the association's right to access to the courts because such right was neither absolute nor unconditional. The court held that the trial court's authority to deny the filing of the action was restricted to frivolous lawsuits. The court affirmed as modified the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as modified an order of the trial court and held that the trial court had the authority to enjoin the association from filing the lawsuit against the Village without the court's approval only when such lawsuit was frivolous.

Thorp v. Town of Lebanon


No. 96-2449


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


211 Wis. 2d 890; 568 N.W.2d 652; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 544



May 15, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order and a judgment of the circuit court for Dodge County: DANIEL W. KLOSSNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After their property was rezoned, plaintiff landowners brought suit against defendant local governments requesting declaratory, injunctive, and monetary relief. The circuit court for Dodge County (Wisconsin) dismissed the complaint for failure to comply with the notice of claim and notice of injury requirements of Wis. Stat. § 893.80(1)(a), (b). The landowners appealed, arguing the statute did not apply to their federal constitutional claims.


OVERVIEW: The zoning was changed from rural development to agricultural. The court pointed out that reliance on the declaratory judgment statute did not change the landowners' claims that the federal constitution was violated. The court ruled that the allegations were sufficient to state a claim for relief on the ground that the zoning amendment deprived the landowners of either the equal protection of the laws or substantive due process because it was arbitrary, unreasonable, and discriminatory. The court concluded, however, that the complaint did not state a claim for a taking under the federal or state constitutional. The landowners alleged neither the use they made under the previous zoning of rural development, nor the actual or anticipated uses that they no longer had. The allegations were thus insufficient to state a claim for that relief. The court further determined that the landowners' claim for a violation of their right to a fair and impartial hearing adequately asserted violations of a right secured by the federal constitution such that the requirements of Wis. Stat. § 893.80(1) did not apply, just as it did not apply to their equal protection and denial of due process claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the landowner's claim for regulatory taking without just compensation. The court reversed the dismissal of the claim that the amended zoning ordinance deprived them of due process and equal protection of the law and their claim for a violation of their right to a fair and impartial hearing.

State v. Fisher


No. 96-1764-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


211 Wis. 2d 665; 565 N.W.2d 565; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 512


March 27, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
May 7, 1997, RELEASED  
May 7, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from judgments and an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: S. MICHAEL WILK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction on three counts of being a party to the crime of sexual assault of a child under the age of sixteen, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 939.05 and 948.02(2) (1993-94), and one count of being a party to the crime of child enticement, in violation of Wis. Stat. §§ 939.05 and 948.07(1), (3), (1993-94).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State's criminalization of consensual sexual relations with children under age sixteen violated both his constitutional privacy right to engage in sexual activity and his privacy right to make decisions regarding procreation. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court rejected his argument that because Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2) infringed upon his right to procreate it had to pass the strict scrutiny test. On the contrary, the court held that sexual conduct involving minors was not to be judged by the same rules as those which governed adults and that, consequently, only a "significant state interest", not a compelling one, was required to support the age-based distinction contained in § 948.02(2). Finding that the State had a strong interest in the ethical and moral development of its children, the court held that § 948.02(2) prohibited defendant's right to privacy as an adult from being enlarged to include sexual intercourse with a child under the age of 16. The court also rejected defendant's argument that his sentence was based on the improper factor of uncharged crimes in that it considered unproven charges of sexual molestation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence and held that the statute criminalizing sexual conduct with a child under 16 was constitutional.

State v. Kehler


No. 96-0854-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


211 Wis. 2d 889; 568 N.W.2d 651; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 494



May 6, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. KREMERS, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of possession with intent to deliver cocaine and failure to acquire tax stamp. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress the cocaine found in his car and in limiting his cross-examination of a State witness regarding consent to search his car.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for driving without Wisconsin license plates and also because the police had information that he was transporting cocaine. Cocaine was discovered in the car, and defendant was subsequently convicted. On appeal, the court ruled that because the Supreme Court of Wisconsin had recently struck down the drug tax stamp law as unconstitutional, defendant' conviction on that charge was reversed. As to the cocaine charges, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that both the stop and the scope of defendant's detention were lawful. The additional intrusion of asking defendant to step out of his car was de minimus. The court declined to review defendant's coercion argument, that he did not voluntarily consent to the search of his car, as defendant's repeated denial at the suppression hearing that he consented foreclosed the argument on appeal that he gave consent but that it was coerced. The court disagreed with defendant's claim that the trial court did not allow him to cross-examine a detective regarding the issue of consent. The trial court did not deny the cross-examination but, instead, merely exercised its discretion by limiting the cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession with intent to deliver cocaine. The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for failure to acquire tax stamp, with an instruction to vacate that conviction.
