State v. Webb


No. 96-1717


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


211 Wis. 2d 889; 568 N.W.2d 652; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 498



May 6, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)(5), STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: DAVID A. HANSHER, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) that convicted him of four counts of second-degree recklessly endangering safety as a party to a crime and as a habitual criminal. He also appealed from the trial court's order that denied his motions for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The evidence revealed that defendant and others fired semi-automatic handguns at alleged vandals. The bullets did not strike any intended targets, however, a bystander was hit, and other bullets were found in the wall of a home that was in the direct line of fire. Defendant was found guilty of four counts of second-degree recklessly endangering safety as a party to a crime and as a habitual criminal. In affirming the conviction, the court held that defendant properly received an enhanced penalty under Wis. Stat. § 939.62 where a presentence investigation report established that defendant was convicted previously of a felony and such conviction was sufficient to form the basis of defendant's repeater status. The court also held that where there was no evidence that the State had brought additional charges that were of doubtful merit, his claim of prosecutorial vindictiveness could not prevail. Finally, the court ruled that defendant could not establish an ineffective assistance of counsel claim based upon his counsel's failure to pursue a futile claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the order denying his motion for post-conviction relief.

 

1143 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Treutelaar


No. 96-3249-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


211 Wis. 2d 892; 568 N.W.2d 653; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 480



May 1, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: WILLIAM F. HUE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Jefferson County (Wisconsin), convicted defendant of possession of drug paraphernalia following the denial of her motion to suppress evidence seized during a warrantless search of an automobile in which she was a passenger. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether a search incident to the arrest of one occupant of a stopped vehicle extended to the private property of any non-arrested occupants. Defendant contended that it was unreasonable to search her private property absent probable cause that she had committed a crime or that evidence might have been destroyed. The envelope at issue was large enough to conceal a weapon or evidence of a crime, and it was easily within the arrested driver's reach prior to the time he stepped out of the vehicle. Defendant left the envelope on the front passenger floorboard when she exited the vehicle. Therefore, the envelope was within an area from which the driver might have gained possession of a weapon or destructible evidence at the time of the search. The ownership of the envelope was irrelevant to the safety of the officers, or the reasonableness of their search. Therefore, the envelope was properly searched incident to the driver's arrest, notwithstanding any privacy interests that defendant might have claimed in its contents, and defendant's suppression motion was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1144 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Brad L. v. Lee D. (In re Brad L.)


No. 94-3050


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


210 Wis. 2d 437; 564 N.W.2d 354; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 456


February 4, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
April 29, 1997, Opinion Released  
April 29, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: RICHARD G. HARVEY, JR., Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant child, by his guardian ad litem, sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which entered findings of fact and conclusions of law in a paternity action brought by the child against respondent father. Respondent mother was also a party.


OVERVIEW: The child challenged the trial court's determination of child support that his father was obligated to pay. On appeal, the court concluded that retroactive application of Wis. Stat. § 767.51(4) did not violate the father's protection against ex post facto laws or the rule favoring prospective application of substantive legislation and, further, that by its explicit terms, Wis. Stat. § 767.51(4) applied to the father's liability for past support of the child for the period after the child's birth despite the father's lack of knowledge of the child's existence. The court concluded further that the trial court improperly based its deviation from the percentage standard and refusal to order past support on an impermissible factor, inconsistent with the mandate of § 767.51(5). The trial court erred in calculating the father's income for purposes of setting the child's support by applying marital property principles and simply presuming the father's income to be one-half of his and his wife's joint income. Additionally, the trial court erred in determining child support with the expectation that it could modify the order after the child reached adulthood to account for his college costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order of paternity, but remanded for further proceedings to properly determine past support for the approximate 15 years preceding the paternity action, and "future" support for the approximate 3 years from the commencement of that action to the time of the child's adulthood.

State ex rel. Bowman v. Dane County Bd. of Adjustment


No. 96-2306


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


210 Wis. 2d 499; 568 N.W.2d 322; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 442



April 24, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: MORIA KRUEGER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Zoning administrator did not interpret the ordinance in the manner requested by Appellant individual which the individual appealed to the county board of adjustment, which affirmed the zoning administrator's decision. A timely appeal was taken to the Circuit Court of Dane County, Wisconsin, which also affirmed. Thereafter, the instant appeal challenged the circuit court's decision.


OVERVIEW: The individual desired to subdivide his twenty-eight acre parcel in order to give a portion to his daughter for her use as a home site. The individual purchased the land in 1964 when it was zoned A-1 Agricultural. A-1 Agricultural zoning would have permitted the individual to make that division. However, in May of 1981, the town adopted a land use plan in preparation for a blanket rezoning, and adopted Zoning Ordinance No. 2807, which rezoned all of the A-1 Agricultural lands in the town to A-1 Agricultural Exclusive. A-1 Agricultural Exclusive zoning did not permit the land division the individual sought to accomplish. If the zoning administrator interpreted the ordinance as the individual requested, the individual claimed that it would have allowed him to divide his property. The individual sought to expand the jurisdiction of the zoning board it by requesting it to determine that the application of A-1 Agricultural Exclusive zoning to his parcel was unconstitutional. However, legal or constitutional challenges to zoning ordinances were not appropriate subject matter for a board of adjustment. The individual's remedy was a declaratory judgment action filed in circuit court.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the holding of the circuit court.

 

1146 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Molitor


No. 96-2673-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


210 Wis. 2d 415; 565 N.W.2d 248; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 450


February 10, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
April 24, 1997, Released  
April 24, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Sauk County: JAMES EVENSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Sauk County (Wisconsin), which, after a jury trial, entered a judgment of conviction against him for the offense of engaging in repeated acts of sexual assault with the same child, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 948.025(1). Defendant also challenged the order that denied his request for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant first argued that Wis. Stat. § 948.025(2) rendered the statute unconstitutional by depriving him of his state constitutional right to a unanimous jury verdict. The court first decided that defendant's claim did in fact attack the face of the statute and therefore was properly before it. However, the court concluded that there was no merit in the attack. When the charged behavior constituted one continuous course of conduct, the requirement of jury unanimity was satisfied regardless of whether there was agreement among jurors as to which act constituted the crime charged. The unanimity requirement was met whether multiple acts could have been said to constitute one continuous unlawful event and chargeable as to one count. Next, defendant asserted that he should have been allowed to withdraw his no contest plea because he did not understand the charge against him and thus his plea was not knowingly and voluntarily made. The court held that the State met its burden of showing that defendant's plea was knowing and voluntary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and the trial court's denial of his motion for postconviction relief.

 

1147 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martinez


No. 96-1899-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


210 Wis. 2d 396; 563 N.W.2d 922; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 444


January 16, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
April 24, 1997, Released  
April 24, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Rock County: MICHAEL J. BYRON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of possession of tetrahydrocannabinol (THC) with intent to deliver more than 2500 grams within 1000 feet of a school, violation of the drug tax stamp law, maintaining a drug house, and possession of drug paraphernalia. Defendant also appealed an order denying postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The court first reversed defendant's conviction under the drug tax stamp law, Wis. Stat. § 139.89. The drug stamp law, Wis. Stat. §§ 139.87-139.96, was unconstitutional because it violated the constitutional right against self-incrimination. Defendant also contended that a tobacco pipe could not be the basis for a charge of possession of drug paraphernalia under Wis. Stat. § 161.573. The pipe contained residue of THC. The court held that tobacco pipes were plainly excluded from the definition of drug paraphernalia in Wis. Stat. § 161.571(1)(b). Although the plain language of the statute led to a result that was seemingly at odds with the general purpose of the statute, the court simply applied the clear language of the statute to the facts presented. The court also held that the jury could reasonably have found that defendant possessed more than 2500 grams of THC with intent to deliver. In calculating the weight pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1r), the court included the stems or branches supporting the marijuana leaves or buds and excluded the mature stalk or main axis of the marijuana plant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the order denying relief for possession of THC with intent to deliver and for maintaining a drug house. The court reversed defendant's convictions and the order denying relief for possession of drug paraphernalia and under the drug tax stamp law.

Lounge Mgmt. v. Town of Trenton


No. 96-1853


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 426



April 22, 1997, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company challenged a decision of the circuit court (Wisconsin), which (1) denied its motion for a preliminary injunction enjoining the enforcement of an ordinance of respondent town that banned public nudity at establishments licensed for the sale of liquor, and (2) granted the town summary judgment declaring the ordinance did not violate the First Amendment.


OVERVIEW: The company, which operated a nightclub, sought to showcase non-obscene nude and semi-nude performers. The ordinance in question banned such performances. The company sought a preliminary injunction banning the ordinance's enforcement, but the trial court found in the town's favor. The court certified the appeal to the Wisconsin Supreme Court for further consideration. The court noted the case law on the subject differed. One published opinion found unconstitutional an ordinance banning nude dancing in licensed establishments. Another published opinion upheld an ordinance that banned nude performances on premises licensed to sell liquor. In light of the fact that the court did not have the power to overrule, modify, or withdraw language of previously published decisions, the court found that certification of the appeal was appropriate. The court rejected the town's issue regarding the company's alleged failure to serve a notice of claim pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 893.80 because case law barred application of the statute to claims made pursuant to the U.S. Constitution, as was the claim in this case.


OUTCOME: The court certified the appeal to the state supreme court for its review and determination.

State v. Janke


No. 95-0685-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


210 Wis. 2d 496; 568 N.W.2d 320; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 406



April 16, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Winnebago County: WILLIAM H. CARVER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Winnebago County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of two counts of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver in violation of Wis. Stat. § 161.41(1m) (1993-94) and two counts of failing to obtain a drug tax stamp. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence resulting from a warrantless separation and seizure of a package mailed to his address.


OVERVIEW: The police received a tip that someone using defendant's phone was selling cocaine. They verified defendant's name and address and asked the local shipper to notify them if any packages came in for delivery to defendant. When a package arrived, the police asked the shipper to hold onto it temporarily. A drug-sniffing dog alerted on the package, a search warrant was obtained, and cocaine was discovered. Defendant was subsequently arrested when he accepted delivery of the package. Defendant challenged his convictions and asserted that the drug stamp tax law conviction was unconstitutional and that the temporary detention of the package, which provided the basis for the search warrant, was improper. The court reversed the tax stamp conviction because the tax stamp statute had been ruled unconstitutional by the Wisconsin Supreme Court. It affirmed the drug possession conviction. The trial court did not err in finding that the police had properly verified the information supplied by the tipster and that the information provided a reasonable suspicion sufficient to justify the detention of the package. The procedure utilized involved minimal invasion of defendant's privacy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed it in part. It affirmed the drug possession conviction but reversed the conviction based upon defendant's failure to obtain a drug tax stamp.

Town of Wayne v. Bishop


No. 95-2387


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


210 Wis. 2d 218; 565 N.W.2d 201; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 399


February 24, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
April 16, 1997, Released  
April 16, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Washington County: LEO F. SCHLAEFER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant adult bookstore operators sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which in a civil forfeiture proceeding brought by plaintiff town for zoning and building occupancy code violations, entered summary judgment against the operators and set forfeitures.


OVERVIEW: The operators leased property for the purpose of opening an adult bookstore. At the same time, the town amended its zoning ordinances and placed special restrictions on such establishments. Under the new ordinances, the operators could not open the bookstore in the desired location, and there was no area of town zoned to allow the bookstore. The operators filed suit challenging the constitutionality of the ordinance and opened the bookstore anyway. In the civil forfeiture proceeding brought by the town, the circuit court ruled for the town. On appeal, the court reversed the circuit court's finding that the operators did not have standing to raise their First Amendment arguments. In reviewing the merits of those arguments, the court determined that the town had the burden of proving that its actions did not impermissibly infringe on the operator's First Amendment rights. The town erred in effectively creating a total ban on the bookstores; therefore, the court reversed the applicable forfeitures. The court found evidence to support the town's forfeiture based on plumbing violations. The town was incorrectly awarded attorneys' fees for the forfeiture proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the forfeiture based on the operators' plumbing violations, but the court reversed the judgment against the operators for violations of the other zoning and building codes.

State v. Grosse


No. 96-2027-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


210 Wis. 2d 172; 565 N.W.2d 174; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 388


February 10, 1997, Submitted on Briefs  
April 10, 1997, Released  
April 10, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Rock County: EDWIN C. DAHLBERG, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of escape for leaving a halfway house to which he was assigned as part of his intensive sanctions program. He also appealed from an order denying his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to a halfway house after he was convicted of burglary. He left the halfway house to visit his mother. After he was returned to Wisconsin, the Wisconsin Division of Intensive Services (DIS) sanctioned defendant with six-months of confinement in a correctional institution. Thereafter, defendant was charged with escape. He filed a motion for postconviction relief, arguing that the conviction for escape was barred by the Double Jeopardy Clause. In affirming, the court determined that defendant did not meet his burden of showing that the sanction and the subsequent conviction were unconstitutional. The court determined that the DIS sanction was not punishment. The primary purpose of the sanction was not punishment. Therefore, the fact that a punitive motive was present did not make the action punishment. Further, any punishment that defendant received was attributable to the burglary conviction. It was not considered punishment for the offense of escape because the change in placement related to the conditions imposed upon the burglary conviction. Finally, both the administrative sanction and the subsequent conviction were authorized by Wis. Stat. § 301.048.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Sutton


No. 96-2778-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


209 Wis. 2d 604; 568 N.W.2d 39; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 309



March 25, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Barron County: JAMES C. EATON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of harassing a police animal but asserted that the charging statute was unconstitutionally vague and that his excessive sentence was based upon an improper weighing of sentencing factors. Defendant appealed the judgment of conviction and sentence entered in the Circuit Court for Barron County (Wisconsin).


OVERVIEW: When defendant fled upon an attempted arrest on an outstanding warrant, a police dog pursued defendant and defendant punched and kicked the dog. Defendant contended that the statute prohibiting harassment of a police animal was impermissible vague since it proscribed casual contact with the animal. Defendant also argue that the sentencing court placed undue weight on defendant's flight from arrest and the trepidation of the arresting officers. The appellate court first held that, regardless of hypothetical applications of the statute, defendant's conduct in striking and kicking the dog was patently within the conduct proscribed by the statute and, absent any implication of First Amendment values, defendant was precluded from challenging the statute for vagueness. Further, the sentencing court, in a proper exercise of its discretion, properly weighed the context of the crime in addition to other appropriate sentencing factors, and defendant's sentence did not exceed the maximum.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence was affirmed.

 

1153 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Dittberner v. Windsor Sanitary Dist. No. 1


No. 96-0877


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


209 Wis. 2d 478; 564 N.W.2d 341; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 282


November 21, 1996, Oral Argument  
March 20, 1997, Opinion Released  
March 20, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: RICHARD J. CALLAWAY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sanitary district sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which voided its attempted amended assessment, done pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 66.60(10), of land belong to respondent property owners.


OVERVIEW: The district amended the assessment after completion of the project for which the assessment was made and included property that was outside the district's boundaries at the time of the original assessment. The court concluded that the district did not exceed its authority. Because § 66.60(10) stated that a reassessment could be made whenever the first assessment was void for any reason, it followed that as long as the assessment could have been levied in the first instance, the fact that it was defective for noncompliance with statutory procedures did not prevent correction of the error by reassessment. The district's ability to reassess was not limited to situations in which construction had not yet commenced. Although the district had no independent authority to alter its boundaries, it properly requested the town board to do so. The court rejected the property owners' estoppel argument. The property owners' due process rights were not violated because they had the same rights to appear and voice their support or opposition at the reassessment hearing as they did in original assessment proceedings. Finally, the front-foot method was not unreasonable as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment voiding the reassessment and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1154 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Sever v. Dane County


No. 96-1473


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


209 Wis. 2d 602; 568 N.W.2d 38; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 259



March 13, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: MORIA KRUEGER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town residents sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint challenging the methods and procedures by which respondent county approved respondent permit applicant's request for a conditional use permit.


OVERVIEW: The residents filed a complaint seeking certiorari review of the county's approval of the conditional use permit (CUP) granting a company the right to extract mineral aggregate from the CUP applicant's 23 acres of land, the Zoning and Natural Resources (ZNR) Committee's failure to review its decision under Wis. Stat. § 68, and the County Board of Adjustment (BOA) refusal to hear the appeal of the ZNR Committee's grant of the CUP. The trial court dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that Wis. Stat. § 59.99(1) authorized only the ZNR Committee's grant of CUPs, not the County Board's review of ZNR Committee decisions; (2) the appeal provisions of § 59.99 were preempted by Dane County, Wis., Ordinances § 10.255(2)(j); (3) the county's authority to give the BOA the authority to review the ZNR Committee's decision derived from Wis. Stat. § 59.97(6); (4) Wis. Stat. § 68 did not apply to the residents' appeal by operation of Wis. Stat. § 68.03(8); and (5) because Dane County, Wis., Ordinances § 10.255(2)(j) provided procedures for administrative review of ZNR Committee decisions, the county elected not to be governed by Wis. Stat. § 68.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the resident's complaint challenging the county's approval methods and procedures for conditional use permits.

 

1155 of 2046 DOCUMENTS



State v. Matzker


Nos. 94-3264, 95-3433


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


209 Wis. 2d 599; 568 N.W.2d 37; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 256



March 12, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The circuit court for Racine County, Wisconsin, found plaintiff, a convicted sex offender, to be a sexually violent person pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 980.05, and committed him to a secure mental health facility. It also denied the offender's motion for a new trial based on ineffective assistance of trial counsel. The offender appealed these orders.


OVERVIEW: The offender had seven prior convictions for sexual offenses against children. The appellate court rejected his claims that the sexual predator act, Wis. Stat. ch. 980, was unconstitutional under the substantive due process, equal protection, double jeopardy, ex post facto law, or cruel and unusual punishment provisions. Miranda did not apply, as a ch. 980 proceeding was civil, and there was no custodial interrogation. Counsel was not ineffective for: (1) failing to challenge an instruction on the effect of the verdict, as she was concerned the jury would be reluctant to find the offender was not sexually violent if it believed he would be released without supervision, and this was a reasonable tactic; (2) failing to challenge testimony by the State's experts, as it was admissible; (3) failing to present expert witnesses on the reliability of the underlying science of predicting future dangerousness, because she did search for such witnesses, but hit dead ends; (4) failing to present learned treatises, as they contained information both helpful and harmful to the defense; and (5) conceding that the offender was a proper subject for commitment, as this was a reasonable strategy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

1156 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Danny P. (In re Dannisha P.)


No. 96-3429


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 156



February 18, 1997, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: MEL FLANAGAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed the order of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which terminated the father's parental rights with respect to petitioner child.


OVERVIEW: The father had sex with the mother at a time that was consistent with his paternity of the child. However, the mother never told the father the child was his until more than three years after the child was born. The father never had any contact with the child until after blood tests confirmed his paternity. The father stipulated that grounds existed for the termination of his parental rights, and the lower court found that the father had good grounds for believing that the child was his issue at the time the child was born. The lower court found that the termination of the father's parental rights was in the best interest of the child, and the court affirmed the lower court's order. The court held that the lower court's finding that the father had good grounds to know that the child was his was not against the great weight of the evidence. The court ruled that Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6)(a)2 did not violate his rights to due process and equal protection because he had no good grounds to claim ignorance of his fatherhood, and, thus, no grounds to claim that women had an unfair advantage over men in termination proceedings on account of their knowledge of their own parenthood.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's order, which held that the father's parental rights to his child were terminated.

State v. Scott


No. 96-3033-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 157



February 18, 1997, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Brown County: VIVI L. DILWEG, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Brown County (Wisconsin), which pursuant to a plea agreement, convicted defendant of a misdemeanor violation of Wis. Stat. § 945.02(3), which prohibited possession of facilities to conduct a lottery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant dealt in slot machines. On appeal, he contended that slot machines could be possessed for sale to Indian tribal casinos, that federal law preempted the Wisconsin gambling statute, that he had permission to possess the gambling devices, that the statute he was convicted under was unconstitutional, and that the facts did not support the charge. The court affirmed. Defendant's appellate brief failed to meet minimal standards. It contained undeveloped or improperly explained arguments, which were unsupported by citation to authority and did not include references to the record. Additionally, many of defendant's arguments were waived through his voluntary no contest plea to the charge. Defendant's argument that there was no factual basis to support the crime to which he entered the no contest plea also failed. Defendant agreed that the facts in the complaint against him as well as those presented in his preliminary hearing could be used as a factual basis for the plea. Further, defendant failed to bring his claim in a postconviction motion to the trial court. Therefore, the argument could not be addressed in an appeal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

1158 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Tracie M. v. Andrew J.W. (In the Interest of Alexis)


No. 96-3534


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 146



February 17, 1997, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Jefferson County: JACQUELINE R. ERWIN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother filed an action against respondent father to terminate his parental rights to the parties' infant daughter. The Circuit Court for Jefferson County (Wisconsin), in terminating the father's rights, determined that he exhibited a pattern of abusive behavior that threatened the child's health, and that he failed to establish a substantial parental relationship with the child. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that because at one point he was the child's primary caretaker, he could not be found to have failed to assume parental responsibility. He also contended that the trial court did not have jurisdiction because it failed to adjudicate his paternity prior to trial. The judgment was affirmed. The court held that (1) the jury had ample evidence to support its determination that the father did not establish a parental relationship with the child, and (2) the fact that the father's paternity had yet to be adjudicated at the time of trial did not affect the validity of the verdict and the dispositional order. The court noted that Wis. Stat. § 48.415(6) contained a non-exclusive list of factors considered to establish a substantial parental relationship. Although the father did take care of the child shortly after her birth, the evidence revealed several instances of abusive behavior wherein the child sustained bruises, broken ribs, and a closed head injury caused by shaken baby syndrome. The fact that there were positive, as well as negative, contacts did not bar the jury from concluding that the father did not establish a parental relationship with his daughter.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment, which terminated the father's parental rights to his daughter, was affirmed.

 

1159 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Szulczewski


No. 96-1323-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


209 Wis. 2d 1; 561 N.W.2d 781; 1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 142


December 9, 1996, Submitted on Briefs  
February 13, 1997, Opinion Released  
February 13, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: MARK A. FRANKEL, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) of battery by a prisoner, Wis. Stat. § 940.20(1). The sentencing court denied defendant's motion for sentence modification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the sentencing court had no authority to order the immediate commencement a five-year prison sentence on his battery conviction because he had not been discharged from his prior commitment under Wis. Stat. § 971.17. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's sentence and conviction upon finding that immediate commencement of defendant's prison sentence on his battery conviction was authorized by Wis. Stat. § 973.15, although the denomination of it as concurrent to the prior commitment was not. The sentencing court erred in ordering the prison sentence on the battery conviction to be concurrent with defendant's not guilty by insanity commitment because the prior commitment was not a sentence under state law. The fact that defendant was found not guilty of certain offenses in 1975 by reason of mental disease or defect, however, did not render him immune from the present imposition of criminal penalties for a new offense. Defendant's claim that his classification as a prisoner for purposes of Wis. Stat. § 940.20(1) violated his constitutional right to equal protection, which was raised for the first time on appeal, was not subject to appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court modified the sentencing court's judgment by striking the phrase "concurrent with not guilty by insanity commitment" and affirmed the order as modified.

 

1160 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Blawat v. Commissioner of Ins.


No. 95-2772


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 102



February 5, 1997, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5. STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: PATRICK L. SNYDER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance agent sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which upheld an order from respondent, the Office of the Commissioner of Insurance (OCI), revoking his license and imposing a forfeiture of $ 10,000 for various violations.


OVERVIEW: The OCI revoked the insurance agent's license and imposed a forfeiture of $ 10,000 after he violated various statutes by distributing health insurance pamphlets that were found to be misleading. The trial court upheld the OCI's order. On appeal, the court found no merit to the agent's claim that the OCI acted unconstitutionally and abused its discretion by revoking his license as retaliation for his exercise of his First Amendment rights. The record showed that the OCI began investigating the agent before he ever spoke out against a rule change. The court could not say that the matter was not handled as promptly as possible under the circumstances. Finally, the court concluded that the OCI acted within the scope of its discretion in imposing the sanctions against the agent. The evidence amply supported the OCI's findings that the agent committed multiple statutory and rule violations, attempted to impede its investigation, and evaded and misrepresented the truth regarding his activities. Based upon the findings, as well as the strong public policy interest in protecting senior citizens from misleading insurance sales practices, the sanctions imposed were reasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

1161 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. National Fire Ins. Co.


No. 96-1299


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


1997 Wisc. App. LEXIS 82



January 30, 1997, Released


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION HAS NOT BEEN RELEASED FOR PUBLICATION IN THE PERMANENT LAW REPORTS. UNTIL RELEASED, IT IS SUBJECT TO REVISION OR WITHDRAWAL.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Monroe County: STEVEN L. ABBOTT, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a minor child and her parents, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin), which granted a motion for summary judgment in favor of defendants, an insurance company, a fair operator, and the horse's owner and its insurer, in a personal injury action brought by plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: A six-year-old girl was walking down the aisle of an open-air horse barn at a county fair. She sustained serious injuries when a horse on exhibit at the fair kicked her in the head. The girl's parents brought an action against defendants. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment on the grounds that they were immune under the provisions of the recreational immunity law found in Wis. Stat. § 895.52. The court found that the girl waived her argument that the statute was unconstitutional because she failed to raise it at trial. The court also found that defendant owner of the horse was not an "owner" within the meaning of the Wis. Stat. § 895.52 (1)(d). Accordingly the court reversed the part of the trial court's judgment that dismissed the action against the horse owner. The court affirmed in all other respects. The court found that the trial court did not err as a matter of law in finding that the girl was engaged in a recreational activity. The court found that the horse's owner who merely leased a space at the fair was not the type of person that the statute sought to protect by its immunity provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the decision of the trial court that granted defendants a motion for summary judgment. The court reversed the entry of summary judgment in favor of the horse's owner and remanded for further proceedings.

 

1162 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Andreshak v. Childrey


No. 96-1876-FT


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


207 Wis. 2d 645; 559 N.W.2d 925; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1647



December 27, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Marathon County: GREGORY E. GRAU, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party defendant insurer appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Marathon County (Wisconsin) denying its motion to vacated a default judgment in favor of third-party plaintiff insurer. Third-party defendant claimed that its failure to timely answer the third-party complaint was the result of excusable neglect.


OVERVIEW: Evidence showed that third-party defendant received the third-party complaint and summons, forwarded them to a claims handler, who sent them to an out-of-state processing office. A technician determined that third-party defendant was not the insurance carrier on the trailer in question and forwarded the papers to a claims processor, who never followed up. The trial court granted third-party plaintiff's motion for a default judgment and then refused to vacate the judgment. On appeal, the court rejected third-party defendant's claim of excusable neglect and concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to vacate the judgment. Excusable neglect was not synonymous with neglect, carelessness, or inattentiveness, but was neglect that might have been the act of a reasonably prudent person under the same circumstances. Third-party defendant was a large and sophisticated insurance company with experience in litigation, and it did not establish that the complaint was processed in any unusual way. It thus failed to establish excusable neglect. Issues of a party's defense or of fairness only had to be considered after excusable neglect was established.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which had denied third-party defendant's motion to vacate the default judgment that had been entered in favor of third-party insurer.

Hermann v. Town of Delavan

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of an order from the Walworth County Court (Wisconsin), which dismissed their Wis. Stat. § 893.80 complaint alleging that respondent town's tax assessment was unfair and violated Wis. Const. art. VIII, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The property owners appealed from a dismissal of their complaint alleging that the town's system of property tax assessment was unfair. The circuit court dismissed the action for failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, concluding that the property owners had failed to exhaust exclusive statutory remedies addressing the complaint's overassessment claims. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. The court held that the action could not be maintained without initial compliance with the statutory mandates for review by the Board of Review. By failing to seek review by the Board, the taxpayers prevented the Board from considering the claimed uniformity violation and concomitantly reviewing the bases for the valuation of properties in the town.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court dismissing the property owners' cause of action against the town was affirmed.

State v. Whaley


Nos. 95-3475-CR, 95-3476-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


207 Wis. 2d 643; 559 N.W.2d 923; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1602



December 17, 1996, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JEFFREY A. WAGNER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of multiple counts of abduction of a child, while armed, and first-degree sexual assault, as well as one count each of armed robbery, kidnapping and theft, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 948.30(2)(b), 939.63(2), 943.32(1)(b) and (2), 940.225(1)(b), 940.31(1)(b) and 943.20(1)(a) and (3)(d)(2), and denied his request for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from a judgment entered after a jury convicted him of multiple counts of abduction of a child, while armed, and first-degree sexual assault, as well as one count each of armed robbery, kidnapping and theft, contrary to Wis. Stat. §§ 948.30(2)(b), 939.63(2), 943.32(1)(b) and (2), 940.225(1)(b), 940.31(1)(b) and 943.20(1)(a) and (3)(d)(2). He also appealed from the trial court's order denying his request for a new trial. The court affirmed. Defendant contended that the trial court exceeded the scope of the court's remand order because it did not limit its consideration to the PEP A test. The court disagreed, stating that it was not only reasonable, but also prudent of the trial court to review all of the evidence in order to make a determination not only because an absolute exclusion would have required a new trial, but also because an absolute exclusion might have meant that defendant was not guilty of the crimes charged. Given the purpose of the hearing, the court could not conclude that the nature of the remand hearing was an erroneous exercise of discretion. There was no error in allowing the DNA evidence to be introduced at the remand hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1165 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Ritter v. Ross


No. 95-1941


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


207 Wis. 2d 476; 558 N.W.2d 909; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1580


September 13, 1996, Oral Argument  
December 12, 1996, Opinion Released  
December 12, 1996, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied December 1, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 7086.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Rock County: JAMES E. WELKER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which found that they were entitled to damages for the retention of sale proceeds over the amount of a tax lien by respondents, a county and its treasurer (county), following a foreclosure sale. The county cross-appealed the judgment. The property alleged violations of the Due Process and Takings Clauses of the Fifth and Fourteenth Amendments.


OVERVIEW: The owners sued the county seeking to void a tax foreclosure and sale of a parcel of non-homestead property they owned in the county and to recover monetary damages and attorney fees on several theories. The county began the foreclosure proceedings when a tax arrearage remained unpaid for several years. The owners did not defend the action and, after obtaining a foreclosure judgment, the county sold the property and retained the entire amount of the sale proceeds. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court with directions to enter judgment dismissing the owners' action. The court held as follows: 1) the county was entitled to retain the excess proceeds of the sale because the State's constitution and tax codes were silent as to the distribution of excess proceeds received in a tax sale and notice of the action met due process requirements; and 2) the notices received by the owners were reasonably calculated to apprise them of the pendency of the foreclosure action, afforded them an opportunity to present their objections, and were thus constitutionally adequate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court awarding damages to the owners and remanded the cause with directions to dismiss the owners' complaint.

State v. Konrath


No. 96-1261-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


207 Wis. 2d 644; 559 N.W.2d 924; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1588



December 11, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: JOSEPH E. WIMMER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) which denied his motion to vacate the seizure of his motor vehicle. He contended the trial court erred when it issued an order specifying the vehicle to be seized without notifying him and then ruled that his subsequent objection was untimely. He also asserted the seizure of his car was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of operating a motor vehicle while intoxicated, a fifth offense. After reaching a plea agreement with the district attorney's office, he pled guilty and was sentenced. The judgment of conviction included 12 months of jail time, a fine, and revocation of his operator's license for three years. Wis. Stat. § 346.65(6) required the court to seize his vehicle. The State requested that the court conduct a review hearing on the matter because the police had not yet located the vehicle. Defendant moved to vacate the seizure order based on his contention that § 346.65(6) was unconstitutional. The appellate court held the trial court properly included the legislatively-mandated penalty in the judgment of conviction. The forfeiture hearing and the due process guarantees which attach to it did not commence until the vehicle was seized. Defendant could have raised the issue of the constitutionality of the forfeiture of his motor vehicle through a timely appeal from the judgment of conviction. Because the forfeiture action was a separate action which was commenced after the vehicle was seized, § 346.65 afforded defendant another opportunity to contest its legality.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Lopez


No. 95-3250-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


207 Wis. 2d 413; 559 N.W.2d 264; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1586


October 31, 1996, Submitted on Briefs  
December 11, 1996, Opinion Released  
December 11, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Washington County: RICHARD T. BECKER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Circuit Court for Washington County (Wisconsin), which entered a judgment of conviction against defendant for possession of marijuana with intent to deliver within 1000 feet of a park. The trial court also denied defendant's postconviction motion. Defendant argued the search warrant of his home was not supported by probable cause, and thus, the evidence seized was found as part of an illegal search.


OVERVIEW: The affidavit that supported the search warrant stated that an informant, who had proven reliable in the past, indicated that he had contact with defendant's brother, who sold marijuana that he obtained from defendant. A detective set up a surveillance outside defendant's brother's home. The informant then purchased one pound of marijuana from the brother, which defendant delivered to the brother's home. During execution of the search warrant at defendant's residence, the officers discovered, among other things, approximately 48.5 pounds of marijuana. Defendant argued that Wis. Stat. § 161.49, the penalty enhancer, was void for vagueness. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that: (1) under the totality of the circumstances of the case, the search warrant affidavit provided a substantial basis for concluding that there was a "fair probability" that marijuana would be found on defendant's premises; (2) the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress based on the doctrine of inevitable discovery; (3) the application of § 161.49 did not violate defendant's due process rights; and (4) § 161.49 was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the order of the trial court.

State v. Castillo

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of orders from the Circuit Court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which ordered his commitment to an institution after he pleaded guilty to the State's petition accusing him of being a sexually violent person.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was institutionalized as a juvenile after he molested his younger sister. Prior to his release, the State filed a petition accusing him of being a sexually violent person and sought his continued commitment. Defendant eventually pleaded guilty to the petition in exchange for the State's promise to secure community placement for him, but when the efforts failed, the State filed a motion to modify the dispositional order to seek commitment to an institution. The court further held that defendant's continued commitment because of the State's breach of the agreement was fundamentally unfair. Finally, the court held that fundamental fairness required that defendant be allowed to withdraw his guilty plea.

S.C. Johnson & Sons v. Town of Caledonia

COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN

October 23, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from order of the circuit court for Racine County: DENNIS J. FLYNN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed an action, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 74.37(3)(d), seeking judicial review of a decision by defendant Town of Caledonia (Wisconsin) denying its claim for a refund of property taxes. The Circuit Court of Racine County (Wisconsin) rejected the Town's argument that the corporation was limited to a certiorari review, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 70.47(13), and the court of appeals granted the Town's request for leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Town of Caledonia assessed property that was owned by a corporation, and the corporation challenged the assessment. A board of review sustained the assessment, and the corporation paid the tax, but filed a claim with the Town, seeking a refund. The Town denied the claim, and the corporation filed an action against the Town, pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 74.37(3)(d), seeking judicial review of its decision. The Town challenged the action, arguing that the corporation was required to seek review under Wis. Stat. § 70.47(13), and it asked the trial court to construe the action as one for certiorari that was limited to reviewing the record generated before the board of review. The trial court rejected the Town's argument, and the Town sought leave to appeal. The appellate court held that: (1) Wis. Stat. § 74.37(3)(d) permitted taxpayers to seek a trial de novo when the taxpayer claimed that a tax imposed by a municipality was excessive, and the trial court's judgment rejecting the Town's argument that the corporation had to proceed under Wis. Stat. § 70.47(13) was correct; and (2) the Town lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of Wis. Stat. § 74.37(3)(d).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings on the corporation's complaint.

City of W. Allis v. Radtke


No. 95-2713


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


205 Wis. 2d 735; 557 N.W.2d 256; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1290



October 8, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: BONNIE L. GORDON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction in Milwaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin), on a no contest plea, for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant.


OVERVIEW: Wis. Stat. § 343.12(2)(d), which required the Department of Transportation to suspend defendant's school bus operator's license upon his conviction for operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, did not violate the equal protection, cruel and unusual punishment, and due process provisions of the federal and Wisconsin constitutions. The legislature could rationally distinguish between school bus drivers and other drivers based on a legitimate interest in protecting children from harm while being transported on school buses. There was no equal protection violation. The license suspension under § 343.12(2)(d) was an administrative sanction rather than a criminal sentence. Hence, the granting of a commercial license was a privilege, not an inherent right. There was no cruel and unusual punishment. The police officer's failure to read defendant the entire "Informing the Accused" form did not require the suppression of the chemical breath test results. There was no due process violation. The remaining due process claims, based on ex post facto considerations, were merely moot hypothetical situations that never came to pass.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Buening v. Wisconsin Dep't of Health & Social Servs.


No. 94-0891


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


205 Wis. 2d 32; 556 N.W.2d 116; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1225


January 13, 1995, Submitted on Briefs  
September 30, 1996, Released  
September 30, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: MORIA KRUEGER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Health and Social Services challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) reversing the Department's decision affirming the Dade County Department of Human Services' (DCDH) action. DCDH had terminated respondent mother's Aid to Families with Dependant Children (AFDC) grant.


OVERVIEW: The mother and her daughter constituted an AFDC assistance unit and received $ 440 per month in AFDC benefits. The mother's partner and their two-year-old child lived with them. The partner was not the daughter's natural, adoptive, or stepfather. In January 1993 the partner began to draw monthly unemployment compensation of $ 652. DCHS determined that upon the partner's unemployment, the two-year old child became a "dependent child." DCHS added both the partner and the two-year old to the mother's "filing unit" and concluded that 42 U.S.C.S. § 607(b)(1)(B)(iv) required that it deduct the partner's monthly unemployment compensation from the benefit. Because the partner's unemployment compensation exceeded the assistance standard, DCHS terminated the mother and the daughter's AFDC grant. The Department affirmed, but the trial court reversed. On appeal, the court held that DCHS incorrectly added the two-year old and the partner to the mother's assistance unit. The court held that a child meeting all other eligibility requirements did not qualify for AFDC when her parent became unemployed but was paid unemployment compensation exceeding the state's level of assistance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment reversing the Department's decision.

 

1172 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Sprague v. City of Madison


No. 94-2983


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


205 Wis. 2d 110; 555 N.W.2d 409; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1205



September 26, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied May 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2890.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: SARAH B. O'BRIEN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant roommates sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of respondent, the Madison Equal Opportunity Commission (MEOC), finding that the roommates violated Madison, Wis. Gen. Ordinance § 3.23(4)(a) when the roommates refused to rent a room to respondent tenant on the basis of her sexual orientation.


OVERVIEW: The tenant sought to rent a room from the roommates. The roommates declined to rent the tenant a room based on her sexual orientation. The MEOC and the trial court found that the roommates violated § 3.23(4)(a) when they declined to rent the room to the tenant. The roommates appealed. The court held that applying § 3.23(4) to the rental of a room within a house with shared common areas was not unreasonable or absurd. The trial court was correct in not considering the roommates' argument that § 3.23 was unconstitutional because they failed to notify the attorney general of their challenge, as required by Wis. Stat. § 806.04(11). However, the roommates' notice to the attorney general subsequent to the trial court's decision cured the defect. The roommates gave up their unqualified right to constitutional protection when they rented housing for profit. The restrictions placed by the city on persons who rent housing for profit were neither unreasonable nor encroached upon the roommates' constitutional protections. Madison, Wis. Gen. Ordinance § 3.23 did not explicitly authorize MEOC to award compensatory or punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which affirmed the decision of the MEOC that the roommates violated city ordinance when they declined to rent a room to the tenant based on her sexual orientation. The court reversed the order of the trial court which affirmed the MEOC's award of damages for emotional distress to the tenant.

 

1173 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clay


No. 95-2048-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


205 Wis. 2d 112; 555 N.W.2d 410; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1215



September 26, 1996, Released


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO RULE 809.23 OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, AN UNPUBLISHED OPINION IS OF NO PRECEDENTIAL VALUE AND FOR THIS REASON MAY NOT BE CITED IN ANY COURT OF THIS STATE AS PRECEDENT OR AUTHORITY EXCEPT TO SUPPORT A CLAIM OF RES JUDICATA, COLLATERAL ESTOPPEL OR LAW OF THE CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Dane County: JACK F. AULIK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought judicial review of a judgment by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) convicting him as a party to the crime of possessing cocaine with intent to deliver and an order by the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) denying postconviction relief. Because appellant was a repeat offender and the offense took place within 1000 feet of a youth center, there were penalty enhancers under Wis. Stat. §§ 161.48(3) and 161.49.


OVERVIEW: Appellant raised issues concerning: (1) trial counsel's effectiveness, (2) the sufficiency of the information, (3) the constitutionality of § 161.49, (4) the sufficiency of the evidence presented at the preliminary examination, and (5) the State's use of a co-defendant's out-of-court statements. Appellant asserted that he was not allowed to testify because his counsel was not prepared to call him as a witness. Counsel asserted that appellant made the decision not to testify because of his extensive criminal record. The circuit court believed counsel. That credibility decision was not subject to reversal. The information provided appellant with sufficient notice of the § 161.49 enhancer. It plainly set forth a set of acts to which a penalty enhancer applied. The State properly charged the § 161.49 penalty enhancer, despite the absence of any evidence pertaining to that enhancer at the preliminary hearing. The circuit court properly allowed testimony concerning a co-defendant's out-of-court statements. The appellate court rejected the argument that the statements were inadmissible because they did not fall within the scope of any exception to the hearsay rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed.

 

1174 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Trepanier


No. 96-0601-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


204 Wis. 2d 505; 555 N.W.2d 394; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1175


September 11, 1996, Oral Argument  
September 24, 1996, Released


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Marinette County: TIM A. DUKET, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified; order reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Circuit Court for Marinette County (Wisconsin), which required him to submit payment to the state's DNA databank program under Wis. Stat. Ann. § 973.046 and denied his subsequent motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary. The trial court ordered him to pay a surcharge to the state's DNA testing program under Wis. Stat. Ann. § 973.046. The statute required convicted burglars to pay the surcharge regardless of whether a sample was actually taken. Defendant was not ordered to provide a sample but was assessed the surcharge anyway. On appeal, defendant did not contest his guilt but claimed that the mandatory surcharge violated his equal protection rights. The court held that Wis. Stat. Ann. § 973.046(1)(a) violated defendant's equal protection rights because the statute gave the trial court discretion to require a class of people to give DNA samples, including accused burglars, but required only convicted burglars to pay the surcharge regardless of whether they gave a sample or not. The court held that the state lacked a rational basis for imposing this payment requirement only on convicted burglars and not on other convicts and that this provision of the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision to required defendant to pay a surcharge to the state's DNA databank even though he had not been required to provide a sample.

 

1175 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. LaPlant


No. 94-2362-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


204 Wis. 2d 412; 555 N.W.2d 389; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1144


June 5, 1995, Submitted on Briefs  
September 12, 1996, Released  
September 12, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: ROBERT W. LANDRY, Reserve Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord sought review of his conviction by the Circuit Court for Milwaukee County (Wisconsin) of unfair residential rental trade practices. Defendant challenged his conviction on constitutional grounds, arguing that Wis. Admin. Code § ATCP 134 was unconstitutionally vague and violated Wis. Const. art. I, § 1 and the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution.


OVERVIEW: A landlord was convicted of unfair residential rental trade practices. The landlord appealed his conviction, arguing that Wis. Admin. Code § ATCP 134, under which he was charged, was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court rejected defendant's claim, finding that the terms of the regulation should have been familiar enough to a landlord to signal when he or she would be engaging in prohibited conduct. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the regulation provided insufficient standards for law officers to enforce it objectively. The court found that the regulation sufficiently delineated landlord conduct that was violative and provided clear standards for enforcement. The court found no merit in defendant's argument that the regulation violated equal protection because it created an unreasonable classification by regulating landlords and not tenants and an unreasonable distinction between residential and commercial landlords. The court found a rational basis for the classification and distinction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court.

 

1176 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Makos v. Wisconsin Masons Health Care


No. 96-0174


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


212 Wis. 2d 692; 569 N.W.2d 592; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1110



September 6, 1996, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [*1] Requested that the supreme court accept certification and address whether § 893.55(1)(b) is constitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the decedent's representative and family, challenged the order of the trial court (Wisconsin), which dismissed their medical malpractice action and entered judgment in favor of defendants, the doctor, patient compensation funds, a laboratory, and insurance companies, because the action was barred by Wisconsin's statute of repose, Wis. Stat. § 893.55(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Nine years after being told that a growth on her leg was not malignant, decedent's growth was diagnosed as metastatic malignant melanoma. Within one year, she and her family filed a medical malpractice arising from the earlier biopsy examination. Decedent died two weeks after the case was filed at the age or 36. Pursuant to § 893(1)(b), the statute of limitations for the action had expired because the action was filed more than five years from the date of the alleged act or omission. The family argued that § 893.55(1)(b) was unconstitutional and, therefore, should not have barred their claim. The court certified the case to the supreme court because (1) there was an inherent conflict between the various statutes of repose within the medical malpractice scheme; (2) under § 893.55(1)(b), plaintiffs could recover nothing, even if they could prove that the prior diagnosis was malpractice that resulted in decedent's death; (3) because the statute created harsh and unequal results, parties would continue to challenge its constitutionality; and (4) a decision by the supreme court could clarify the law, provide guidance to the bar, and eliminate unnecessary challenges to the statute.


OUTCOME: The court certified the appeal in the case to the state supreme court for its review and determination.

 

1177 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Sommers Estates Co. J.A. v. City of New Berlin


No. 95-2024


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1016



August 7, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County: PATRICK L. SNYDER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developers sought review of an order of the circuit court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin) which dismissed their action against respondent city on the ground that the action was barred by the doctrine of res judicata.


OVERVIEW: The developers entered into an agreement with the city for the development of a subdivision. The developers filed a suit against the city for the excess cost of constructing storm sewers. That action was dismissed. The developers then filed another action against the city alleging the taking of land without just compensation, breach of the developers' agreements, and fraudulent conduct by the city regarding sanitary sewer charges, water main connection charges and water fees. The circuit court dismissed the action as barred by claim preclusion. On appeal the developers argued that the action was related to different utilities. They also contended that the causes of action were different because the first suit questioned the city's exercise of discretion and the second suit sought damages for breach of contract, fraud, and unconstitutional appropriation of land. The court concluded that the doctrine of claim preclusion barred the action. In both actions the developers sought reimbursement of certain costs when the developers' agreement provided otherwise. The court was not persuaded that each breach of the contract was a separate cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the developers' action against the city.

 

1178 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


UPS v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 95-2493


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


204 Wis. 2d 63; 553 N.W.2d 861; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 969


March 11, 1996, Submitted on Briefs  
July 31, 1996, Opinion Released  
July 31, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant packaging company sought review of an order from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision of the Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission to uphold the company's franchise tax assessments imposed by respondent state revenue department using the apportionment formula under Wis. Admin. Code § [Tax] 2.46. The company claimed the formula was unconstitutional and that the department erred by not making modifications.


OVERVIEW: The department imposed franchise tax assessments against the company. The Commission upheld the department's decision and the trial court affirmed the decision. The company claimed the formula used by the Commission was unconstitutional and that the department erred by refusing to make modifications for arrivals and departures under Wis. Stat. § 71.07 (1985-1986) and Wis. Admin. Code § [Tax] 2.46. In affirming the trial court's order on appeal, the court found that the company failed to meet its burden of establishing by clear and cogent evidence that the apportionment formula attributed income to the state of Wisconsin out of proportion to business transacted in the state or resulted in grossly distorted figures. The court stated there was no suggestion in Wis. Admin. Code § [Tax] 2.46 that arrivals and departures should have been weighted. Additionally, the court stated that Wis. Stat. § 71.07(5) did not apply because it provided an alternative method for apportionment for corporations, nonresident individuals, and nonresident estates and trusts only. The court found that the company was a financial organization and public utility, which fell under § 71.07(2)(e).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

1179 of 2046 DOCUMENTS



State v. Steven G.B.


No. 93-1658-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


204 Wis. 2d 108; 552 N.W.2d 897; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1032



July 31, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended August 14, 1996. Certiorari Denied February 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 801.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from judgments of the circuit court for Portage County: JAMES EVENSON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Portage County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant on two counts of first-degree sexual assault of a child, Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1). The alleged victims were defendant's two daughters. Defendant challenged the trial court's jury instructions, its exclusion of certain evidence, the sufficiency of the evidence to convict, and the effectiveness of his trial counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and the victims' mother had a contentious relationship regarding the custody of their two daughters. Defendant denied having sexually assaulted the daughters and alleged that the mother made the victims fabricate stories of abuse. The court agreed that the trial court should have allowed defendant to present certain evidence regarding the mother's past behavior to show that the mother's conduct exhibited a pattern of preventing the daughters from having a father around. However, because only part of the evidence had been excluded, the court held that the error was harmless. The court rejected defendant's challenge to the trial court's supplemental instruction to the jury on agreement, which was given after 16 hours of deliberation. Given the length and complexity of the trial, the court held that it was within the trial court's discretion to give the instruction and that it was not error to permit the victims' mother to be present in the courtroom at the time it was given. There was also sufficient evidence to support the conviction. No basis was found for defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The court rejected defendant's points of error and confirmed his conviction for two counts of first-degree sexual assault of a child.

City of Milwaukee v. Hampton


No. 95-1398


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


204 Wis. 2d 49; 553 N.W.2d 855; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 981


March 6, 1996, Submitted on Briefs  
July 31, 1996, Opinion Released  
July 31, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: KITTY K. BRENNAN, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County, (Wisconsin), which entered a judgment of forfeiture for defendant's violation of the City of Milwaukee's ordinance against carrying a concealed dangerous weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating a city ordinance against the carrying of a dangerous weapon by carrying a folding knife with a blade larger than three inches in the glove compartment of his car. Defendant contested the citation, but the City of Milwaukee Municipal Court found defendant guilty of violating the ordinance and ordered him to forfeit $ 269 or spend 10 days in jail. Defendant petitioned the Milwaukee County Circuit Court for a trial de novo, which the trial court granted. Defendant then filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that the "dangerous per se" language of the ordinance created an irrebuttable mandatory presumption, thereby violating the due process and equal protection provisions of the United States and Wisconsin Constitutions and conflicting with state law and public policy. The trial court rejected defendant's constitutional claims, found him guilty of violating the ordinance, and entered a forfeiture judgment for $ 269 or 10 days in jail. Defendant appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the ordinance constitutional because the ordinance's language did not relieve the City of proving that defendant was carrying a concealed "dangerous weapon."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of forfeiture against defendant.
