Krist Oil Co. v. City of Ashland


No. 96-0029


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


204 Wis. 2d 113; 552 N.W.2d 899; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 941



July 30, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Ashland County: ROBERT E. EATON, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an applicant for a license to sell packaged alcoholic beverages, appealed an order of the circuit court for Ashland County (Wisconsin), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant city and thereby upheld the city's denial of the applicant's request for a license.


OVERVIEW: The applicant, a gas station, sought a license to sell packaged alcoholic beverages. The city denied the application, and the applicant filed a complaint in circuit court challenging the constitutionality of an ordinance that disallowed the sale of alcohol by a gas station. The applicant also alleged that the city failed to provide any form of written denial, contrary to Wis. Stat. § 125.12(3m), and that the city had no basis for denying the license, did not have a full quota, and acted arbitrarily. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the city ordinance disallowing the sale of alcohol by a gas station and granted the city a summary judgment of dismissal. The applicant appealed the summary judgment of dismissal, and the court affirmed. The court held that the ordinance did not deny equal protection because the classification was reasonably related to a legitimate purpose of limiting the availability of alcohol to drivers. The court held that the lack of a written denial by the city did not result in prejudice to the applicant, and therefore appellate relief was precluded by Wis. Stat. § 805.18(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the city.

 

1182 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Drew


No. 95-1162-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


204 Wis. 2d 109; 552 N.W.2d 897; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 949



July 25, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Columbia County: ANDREW P. BISSONNETTE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of two counts of first-degree sexual assault of a child in violation of Wis. Stat. § 948.02(1).


OVERVIEW: Five girls, ranging in age from five to ten years and including two of defendant's children, testified that defendant had either molested or had sexual intercourse with them. Defendant entered Alford pleas to two counts of first-degree sexual assault, and three additional counts were read in for sentencing. The court refused to hear defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel because no evidentiary hearing at the trial level with defendant's attorney present was held. Defendant was not entitled to a new trial on the basis of newly discovered evidence. The alleged conversation between defendant's girlfriend and the mother of one of the victim's that someone put the victim up to making the accusations did not rise to the level of manifest injustice. The testimony of five victims made it unlikely that defendant would receive a different result. The court refused to take judicial notice that Wis. Stat. § 948.02 was unconstitutional. The court concluded that the prosecution complied with its obligations under defendant's plea agreement, and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing a sentence that was not in conformity with the plea agreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1183 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


L.L.N. v. Clauder


No. 95-2084


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


203 Wis. 2d 570; 552 N.W.2d 879; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 937


March 11, 1996, Submitted on Briefs  
July 25, 1996, Opinion Released  
July 25, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: GEORGE A. W. NORTHRUP, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff church member sued defendants, the Roman Catholic Diocese of Madison and one of its priests, claiming that the priest, who was assigned by the Diocese as a hospital chaplain and counselor, used his position to engage her in a sexual relationship. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granted the Diocese's motion for summary judgment, and the church member appealed.


OVERVIEW: The church member sought recovery from the Diocese on several grounds, alleging that: (1) the Diocese was negligent in its supervision of the priest; and (2) the Diocese was vicariously liable for the priest's actions under (a) the common-law rule of respondeat superior and (b) Wis. Stat. § 895.70, which created a civil cause of action for one incurring injury resulting from sexual contact with a "therapist." The court reversed the trial court's judgment on the negligent supervision claim. A determination of the standard of care owed by the Diocese would not necessarily violate the First Amendment prohibition against excessive entanglement of church and state, as the trial court had held. However, because unresolved factual issues were central to this claim, summary judgment was improper. The court affirmed the remainder of the trial court's judgment. The priest's sexual relationship with the church member was beyond the scope of his employment, and therefore, the Diocese could not be held liable based on respondeat superior. Because the cause of action provided by § 895.70 related to the therapist only, the Diocese could not be held vicariously liable under its terms.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment dismissing the church member's claim against the Diocese for negligent supervision of the priest and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings on that issue. In all other respects, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1184 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Winter


No. 96-0175-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


204 Wis. 2d 113; 552 N.W.2d 899; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 888



July 16, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Shawano County: ANN WALSH BRADLEY and JAMES P. JANSEN, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction after a bench trial in the Circuit Court for Shawano County (Wisconsin) of violating a harassment injunction issued under Wis. Stat. § 813.125.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 813.125, defendant was enjoined from harassing an individual in violation of Wis. Stat. § 947.013 and a complaint was thereafter filed alleging that defendant made four harassing phone calls to the individual. Defendant was convicted of violating the injunction and challenged the conviction after the trial court denied his motion for postconviction relief. The court held that defendant was not denied due process of law, reasoning that Wis. Stat. § 813.125 was not unconstitutionally vague because it prohibited certain behaviors specifically enumerated in Wis. Stat. § 947.013 that were deemed to be harassing. The court further reasoned that because § 947.013 was sufficiently specific in advising defendant what behavior were prohibited, the injunction prohibiting defendant from violating § 947.013 was therefore sufficiently specific. The court further held that the failure of the prosecution to specifically allege a course of conduct intended to harass was not fatal because the complaint referenced § 947.013, which made such an intent an element of the crime charged. The court concluded that defendant was sufficiently advised of the elements of the crime charged.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Lindsey


No. 95-3392-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


203 Wis. 2d 423; 554 N.W.2d 215; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 887


May 14, 1996, Submitted on Briefs  
July 16, 1996, DATED AND RELEASED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Outagamie County: HAROLD V. FROEHLICH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Outagamie County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of second-degree sexual assault of a child, Wis. Stat. § 948.02(2). The trial court imposed a mandatory life sentence without the possibility of parole pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 939.62(2m)(b).


OVERVIEW: Section 939.62(2m)(b), Wisconsin's "three-strikes" law, mandated life imprisonment without parole for three-time serious felony offenders. Defendant contended that the trial court's imposition of mandatory life imprisonment without the possibility of parole pursuant to § 939.62(2m)(b) was unconstitutional. Defendant also argued that he was denied due process when the trial court failed to afford him the right of allocution at sentencing. In affirming, the court held that defendant failed to prove that § 939.62(2m)(b) was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt. According to the court, § 939.62(2m)(b) did not violate the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment, the separation of powers doctrine, or the equal protection doctrine. The court also determined that although the trial court erred when it failed to afford defendant the right of allocution at sentencing, there was no reasonable possibility that the trial court's error contributed to defendant's sentence. Therefore, the court concluded that the error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1186 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Roberts v. Jennings


No. 95-2151


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


204 Wis. 2d 110; 552 N.W.2d 898; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 860



July 11, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Columbia County: DANIEL GEORGE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court for Columbia County (Wisconsin), which affirmed a decision by appellee town commissioners to lay a road over the landowners' property and awarding them $ 500 in damages.


OVERVIEW: A neighbor sought to acquire a parcel of land owned by the landowners. When the landowners refused to sell, the neighbor sought to have the land condemned by the town pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 80.13. Notice was sent to the landowners' attorney that he needed to file an appearance in order for the landowners to be a party to the action. The attorney failed to do so. The commissioners ruled to condemn the land for the purpose of putting a road on the land. The court rejected the landowners' claims that Wis. Stat. §§ 80.17 to 80.22 were void for vagueness. All the problems complained of by the landowners, such as that the statutes did not require deference to the town board's decision, that there were no mechanisms for ensuring that a person whose land has been taken is given fair market value, and that certain terms were not defined, were not questions of vagueness. The court rejected the landowners' claims that their due process rights were violated because their property was taken in a proceeding in which they were not a party. The landowners were given sufficient notice of the matter through their attorney, who failed to follow through in the matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1187 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Larson


No. 95-1940-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


203 Wis. 2d 270; 551 N.W.2d 870; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 823



June 27, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Rock County: EDWIN C. DAHLBERG, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order and judgment of the Circuit Court for Rock County (Wisconsin), which denied his motion to suppress evidence seized in his home pursuant to a no-knock search warrant and convicted him of possession with intent to deliver a Schedule I controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: The affidavit on which the warrant was issued stated that the officer received a tip that defendant was selling marijuana and cocaine and that trash from his home contained evidence of drug activity. The affidavit requested a no-knock warrant based on the officer's experience that drug dealers would, given time, arm themselves or dispose of evidence. In executing the warrant, the officers knocked on the front door of defendant's home and waited 35 seconds later before using a ram to enter based on concerns about a movement inside and lack of response. The trial court concluded that, while the no-knock provision was erroneously authorized, the officers, after 35 seconds, had reason to believe that evidence was being destroyed. The court on appeal held that, under the "blanket rule," the no-knock warrant and its execution were proper because defendant was convicted of felonious drug delivery. The court held that, due to the inherent violence associated with drug dealing, the police did not need to offer particularized evidence of weapons to show that exigent circumstances existed for entering without an announcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order and judgment against defendant.

State v. Brulport


No. 95-1687-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


202 Wis. 2d 505; 551 N.W.2d 824; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 638


February 16, 1996, Submitted on Briefs  
May 15, 1996, Opinion Released  
May 15, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Kenosha County: S. MICHAEL WILK, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin), which convicted defendant of one count each of possession of explosives, damage to property by explosives and second-degree reckless endangerment of safety pursuant to Wis. Stat. §§ 941.31(1), 943.02(1)(c), and 941.30(2), all as a party to the crime.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the individual components of aluminum foil and drain cleaner encased in a plastic soda bottle did not constitute either an explosive compound or an explosive within the meaning of Wis. Stat. §§ 941.31(1), 943.02(1)(c). The evidence was sufficient to show that defendant possessed an "explosive compound" for purposes of Wis. Stat. § 941.31(1), and that he damaged property by means of an "explosive" for purposes of Wis. Stat. § 943.02(1)(c). The evidence was sufficient to show that defendant created an unreasonable and substantial risk of death or great bodily harm and that he was aware of such risks. The record supported the trial court's finding that defendant created an unreasonable and substantial risk of great bodily harm and that he was aware that his conduct created such a risk. The evidence was sufficient as to all the charges. The court also determined that Wis. Stat. § 941.31(1) was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1189 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Kirsch v. Endicott


No. 94-0359


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


201 Wis. 2d 705; 549 N.W.2d 761; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 511


March 8, 1995, Submitted on Briefs  
April 18, 1996, Opinion Released  
April 18, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: Michael N. Nowakowski, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates appealed a decision of the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin), which dismissed their complaint against defendant warden that sought injunctive relief and damages. The action, which alleged deprivation of liberty and property without due process of law, arose after the warden subjected them to a "Management Continuum" while they were segregated from the general prison population.


OVERVIEW: The inmates were segregated from the general prison population, and they had engaged in systematic destruction of the segregation cells, including breaking the heads off the sprinkler system in the cells and breaking the toilets and sinks. They were subjected to the warden's "Management Continuum" policy, an additional form of segregation of disruptive inmates already in a disciplinary segregation unit. They filed an action for injunctive relief and damages, alleging that the warden had deprived them of liberty and property without due process of law. The trial court dismissed their petition, and they appealed. The court affirmed, holding that their rights to due process applied to the proceedings which resulted in the segregation and were not an issue at the Management Continuum stage. The Continuum itself did not affect good time and it did not cause so major a change in the conditions of the inmates' confinement as to implicate a liberty interest protected by the Due Process Clause. Segregated inmates could reasonably anticipate they could be subjected to sanctions if they engaged in the type of activity that merited the Continuum.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the inmates' complaint against the warden for injunctive relief and damages.

 

1190 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


La Crosse Queen, Inc. v. Wisconsin Dep't of Revenue


No. 95-2754


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


201 Wis. 2d 537; 549 N.W.2d 261; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 436


March 11, 1996, Submitted on Briefs  
April 4, 1996, Opinion Released  
April 4, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Dane County: MICHAEL B. TORPHY, JR., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) that affirmed a determination of the Wisconsin Tax Appeals Commission. The Commission had decided in favor of respondent Wisconsin Department of Revenue that the payments received by the taxpayer for leasing an excursion vessel were not tax exempt because the vessel was not primarily engaged in interstate commerce.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a lessor, rented the vessel to a third party lessee who conducted travel cruises on the Mississippi River along the territorial waters of Wisconsin and Minnesota. The taxpayer appealed to the Commission from a sales tax assessment of the Department on the gross receipts from the lease payments received during three years. The contested judgment of the circuit court that affirmed the Commission was reversed because the Commission incorrectly interpreted the term "interstate commerce." The Commission used an inapposite definition of interstate commerce that only applied when the transportation occurred inside the boundaries of one state. The Commission failed to analyze if the vessel operated in interstate commerce because it also traveled on Minnesota's waters. The court concluded that the vessel was engaged in interstate commerce because it operated upon Minnesota's waters. The court, however, found the record insufficient to decide if the vessel was "primarily" engaged in interstate commerce according to Wis. Stat. § 77.54(13). Therefore, the action was remanded for a determination of whether the vessel's activities were sufficient to qualify under § 77.54(13).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court that affirmed the decision of the Commission entered for the Department. The cause was remanded to the circuit court with instructions to determine if the vessel was primarily engaged in interstate commerce.

 

1191 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mueller


Nos. 93-3227-CR, 93-3228-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


201 Wis. 2d 121; 549 N.W.2d 455; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 402


October 6, 1994, Submitted On Briefs  
March 28, 1996, Opinion Released  
March 28, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALS from judgments of the circuit court for Dane County: DANIEL R. MOESER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from the Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) judgments of conviction against them under the Wisconsin Organized Crime Control Act, Wis. Stat. §§ 946.80 to 946.88.


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed their convictions under the Wisconsin Organized Crime Control Act (WOCCA), Wis. Stat. §§ 946.80 to 946.88. Each defendant was convicted on one count of pattern racketeering activity, Wis. Stat. §§ 946.83(3) and 946.82(2), and for 18 predicate violations of securities fraud under § 551.41(2) and (3). Defendants argued that their prosecution was barred by the statute of limitations since defendants' arrest warrants were signed but never executed. The court disagreed and held the warrants were issued within the relevant time period so prosecution was not barred by the statute of limitations. The court held the prosecution was not required to prove defendants acted with intent to defraud or to knowingly violate the law. The WOCCA did not require proof of knowledge or intent beyond that required for predicate acts that constituted racketeering. The court also held sufficient evidence existed for the jury to find notes were securities and that defendants replaced corporate assets with substantially less valuable assets. Thus, the court affirmed the convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of conviction, holding prosecution was not barred by the statute of limitations and sufficient evidence existed for the jury to find that the notes were securities.

 

1192 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


United Lodges of S.N.P.J. v. City of Brookfield


No. 95-0489


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT TWO


201 Wis. 2d 215; 549 N.W.2d 792; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 378



March 27, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County: MARK GEMPELER, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lodge, ordered by defendant city to raze its dilapidated building, complained of a judgment of the circuit court for Waukesha County (Wisconsin), which granted summary judgment in favor of the city. The lodge had sought a restraining order and damages on the grounds that the raze order deprived the lodge of reasonable use of its property resulting in a temporary taking without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court ruled that the building was dilapidated and properly the subject of a raze order and, because the city reasonably exercised its police powers in issuing the raze order, payment of compensation was not required. The order's failure to refer to Wis. Stat. § 66.05 (1991) did not result in a compensable taking of the lodge's property. Although the lodge complained that the order was not issued pursuant to § 66.05, the lodge sought a restraining order under § 66.05 in its action challenging the order. There was no showing that the lodge was deprived of the relief afforded by § 66.05 or that the city proceeded other than under its police powers. It was undisputed that the building was in a dilapidated condition and was clearly worthy of a raze order. The lodge's president agreed in his deposition that the building was unsafe; his testimony permitted an inference that the building was unusable due to its condition, not as a result of the raze order. The lodge's argument that the raze order prohibited all reasonable use of the property was not sufficiently developed. The city did comply with the provisions of § 66.05 in issuing the raze order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1193 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pusel


No. 95-2348-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


201 Wis. 2d 217; 549 N.W.2d 793; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 337



March 14, 1996, Released


NOTICE: UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Juneau County: PATRICK TAGGART, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court for Juneau County (Wisconsin), which convicted him of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of an intoxicant, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(a), and of operating a motor vehicle with a prohibited alcohol concentration, in violation of Wis. Stat. § 346.63(1)(b). Defendant, a commercial driver, challenged the admissibility of intoxilyzer test results.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for erratic driving, arrested, and given an intoxilyzer test. The arresting officer gave defendant the warnings required by Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4) (1991-92) but did not advise him of the warnings applicable to commercial drivers because defendant was not operating a commercial vehicle nor was he on duty at the time. Defendant appealed and asserted that the intoxilyzer test results were inadmissible because he was not read the portion of the Informing the Accused form relating to commercial drivers as required by Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4m) (1994); he also argued that the jury instructions created an irrebutable presumption of guilt in violation of his due process rights. In affirming, the court held that § 343.305(4m) did not apply because defendant was arrested prior to the statute's effective date. Defendant had been informed of all the rights and penalties relating to him as a regular driver's license holder pursuant to Wis. Stat. § 343.305(4) (1991-92) and therefore the intoxilyzer test results were automatically admissible. The jury was given the option of convicting or acquitting defendant and the instructions did not create an irrebutable presumption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

1194 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shumaker


No. 95-0286-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT ONE


200 Wis. 2d 492; 546 N.W.2d 886; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 230



February 27, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for Milwaukee County: JANINE P. GESKE and MAXINE A. WHITE, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Milwaukee County Circuit Court (Wisconsin) that convicted him of first-degree intentional homicide while using a dangerous weapon as a party to a crime and the order denying his motion for post-conviction relief in the form of a sentence reduction, arguing that the 100-year sentence he received was too harsh and that the evidence was insufficient to convict him of three of the four murder counts.


OVERVIEW: Together with several other individuals, defendant planned the armed robbery of a drug house. In executing the robbery, three teenage girls and one male drug dealer were killed. Defendant was charged with four counts of murder, he was convicted of each offense, and the trial court imposed a 100-year sentence. Defendant moved for post-conviction relief in the form of a sentence reduction. After his motion was denied, he appealed the judgment of conviction and the order denying his motion. In affirming, the court concluded that the sentence imposed by the trial court was not excessive where the crimes were vicious execution-style slayings in which four people, including three teenage girls who were innocent bystanders, were killed. Further, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of the three counts of homicide relating to the three girls even though the physical evidence revealed that the girls were killed from bullets from a gun operated by one of defendant's accomplices. Defendant was charged as a party to the crimes; as such, the fact that the bullets did not come directly from his gun did not absolve him of criminal liability.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the order denying defendant's motion for post-conviction relief were affirmed.

 

1195 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wulff


No. 95-1732-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


200 Wis. 2d 318; 546 N.W.2d 522; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 228


January 17, 1996, Submitted On Briefs  
February 22, 1996, Opinion Released  
February 22, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment and an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: JOHN J. PERLICH, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), defendant was convicted of attempted second-degree sexual assault. Defendant appealed the conviction on the ground that the prosecutor's comment on his refusal to answer police questions denied him due process.


OVERVIEW: Defendant attempted to sexually assault the victim while she was sleeping. Several days after the incident, defendant gave a voluntary statement to a police detective. The statement was very vague; defendant said that he did not recall the events. At trial, he testified in precise detail as to what occurred on the evening of the incident. The prosecutor commented on his alleged inability to recall the evening's events when questioned by the detective and contrasted it with his detailed description at trial. Defendant argued that the comments were constitutionally impermissible. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that the bar against use of post-arrest silence to impeach defendant's exculpatory testimony at trial was inapplicable where defendant opened the door to government questioning by his own remarks.The court observed that the prosecutor was not asking the jury to infer guilt from defendant's silence and his inability to recall events when talking to the detective; she was asking them to consider that silence, and that failure to recall, as bearing on defendant's credibility, given his detailed testimony on those events at trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for attempted second-degree sexual assault was affirmed.

 

1196 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


Krug v. Zeuske


No. 94-3193


COURT COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


199 Wis. 2d 406; 544 N.W.2d 618; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 306


July 27, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
January 18, 1996, Opinion Released  
January 18, 1996, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Dane County: GEORGE W. NORTHRUP, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, state legislators, taxpayers, and elected officials, challenged several laws authorizing payments to cover increased fuel costs made to intervenors, state highway contractors, as violating Wis. Const. art. IV, § 26. The Circuit Court for Dane County (Wisconsin) granted the motions to dismiss filed by defendants, the state treasurer and the secretaries of the departments of administration and transportation. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The department of transportation entered into contracts for various highway improvement projects. Because of a significant increase in fuel prices, five contractors submitted claims to the department to recoup their increased fuel costs after the contracts were performed. The legislature passed bills appropriating funds to pay to the contractors as reimbursement for unanticipated fuel cost increases. The bills were signed into law as 1993 Wis. Laws 431-435. Plaintiffs sought to enjoin the payments on the ground that they constituted "extra compensation" in violation of Wis. Const. art. IV, § 26. The trial court dismissed their action. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the laws were unconstitutional. The court first determined that the presumption of constitutionality applied because the laws concerned matters of substance, not procedure. The payments authorized by the laws were clearly "extra compensation" to the contractors. The court also rejected the trial court's alternative holding that an interdepartmental memorandum incorporated a fuel adjustment clause into the highway contracts.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and order of the circuit court.

 

1197 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


In re ALYCIA v. M. E.


Nos. 95-2967, 95-2968, 95-2969


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT FOUR


199 Wis. 2d 527; 1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 33



January 11, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS from an order of the circuit court for La Crosse County: MICHAEL J. MULROY, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for La Crosse County (Wisconsin), which terminated her parental rights based upon her children's continuing need of protection or services under Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2).


OVERVIEW: The mother asserted that her due process rights were violated because she was inadequately warned of the grounds upon which her parental rights could be terminated. Dispositional orders found her children in need of protection and services, which were extended multiple times. The trial court warned her of the grounds for terminating her parental rights as the law existed before Wis. Stat. § 48.415(2)(c) was amended. The amendment changed the type of conduct for which termination could proceed. Under the old statute, a parent faced termination for culpable conduct or for an inability to meet the conditions established for the children's return to the home. Under the amended statute, a parent faced termination if he or she failed to demonstrate substantial progress toward meeting the conditions established for the children's return. The amendment eliminated the reasons for failure to make substantial progress. The court held that this violated the mother's due process rights because it substantially changed the type of conduct that could lead to the loss of parental rights without notice to the parent. Had the mother been differently warned, she might have acted more cautiously.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded the cause with directions to hold a new trial under the statute as it existed before it was amended.

 

1198 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. Oskey


No. 95-1762


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN, DISTRICT THREE


1996 Wisc. App. LEXIS 20



January 9, 1996, Released


NOTICE:  [*1] UNPUBLISHED LIMITED PRECEDENT OPINION - REFER TO LOCAL RULE 809.23(1)(B)5, STATS.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the circuit court for Pierce County: ROBERT W. WING, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part and cause remanded. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court for Pierce County (Wisconsin) denying injunctive relief against defendant homeowner, whom the State contended exceeded the legal limit of 50 percent of assessed value for structural repairs to nonconforming floodplain buildings. The trial court found the State had not met its burden of proof and dismissed the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner's house was located in a floodplain on an island. The house was subject to Wis. Administrative Code § NR 116.15 and Pierce County, Wis., Ordinance ch. 17.60.190 (Sept. 19, 1978), which prohibited structural repairs to a nonconforming structure in excess of 50 percent of the building's assessed value. The State sought an injunction, contending the homeowner had expanded his house beyond the amount allowed in the permit. The court concluded that adding a new porch, enclosing an existing deck, and adding a half-story to a house created a "substantially different" building as contemplated by the Marris decision. Marris created the substantially different test so that repairs that were reasonably necessary to prevent deterioration might not be classed as structural repairs. The actual cost of the additions approximated their estimated cost, because total estimated cost of the project approximated its total actual cost and because no evidence was presented to the contrary. Cost to the homeowner was the only reasonable interpretation of "value" in Wis. Admin. Code § NR 116.15 and Pierce County, Wis., Ordinance ch. 17.60.020. Neither were unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the part of the judgment that held that the applicable code sections were not unconstitutionally vague, reversed the part of the judgment that misapplied the definition of "structural repair," and remanded the cause for a determination of the precise violations.

 

1199 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State v. C&S Mgmt.


No. 94-3188-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


198 Wis. 2d 844; 544 N.W.2d 237; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1547


November 20, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
December 27, 1995, Opinion Released  
December 27, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Kenosha County: DAVID M. BASTIANELLI, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed an order of the Circuit Court for Kenosha County (Wisconsin) denying its motion for a preliminary examination on its charges of exposing a minor to pornographic materials, a Class E felony.


OVERVIEW: The corporation claimed that excluding corporations from the class of defendants entitled to a preliminary examinations under Wis. Stat. § 971.02 violated state and federal equal protection guaranties. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that a corporate defendant had no fundamental right to a preliminary examination under § 971.02 and that there was a rational basis to support the denial of the statutory right to corporations. The court further held that the fundamental right served by the statute was limited to providing a judicial determination of probable cause for incarcerated defendants or those who would be incarcerated but for payment of a bond. The underlying legislative strategy was to operate an efficient court system by allocating court time that could be used for corporate preliminary examinations to areas where there was a more pressing need.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order denying the corporation's motion for a preliminary examination.

 

1200 of 2046 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Jacobus v. State


No. 94-2995


COURT OF APPEALS OF WISCONSIN


198 Wis. 2d 783; 544 N.W.2d 234; 1995 Wisc. App. LEXIS 1539


October 9, 1995, Submitted On Briefs  
December 21, 1995, Opinion Released  
December 21, 1995, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from an order of the circuit court for Monroe County: MICHAEL J. MCALPINE, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed an order from the Circuit Court for Monroe County (Wisconsin) that denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had previously pled no contest to various charges, including bail jumping based solely on the consumption of alcohol, and was placed on probation. Two years later his probation was revoked and he was incarcerated. Petitioner claimed that he could not be incarcerated because his bail jumping convictions violated state policy under Wis. Stat. § 51.45(1). That statute provided that alcoholics and intoxicated persons could not be subject to criminal prosecution because of their consumption of alcohol, but should receive treatment instead. The court on appeal reversed and granted petitioner's habeas corpus petition. Petitioner did not waive his right to contest his incarceration by previously pleading no contest because his claim for relief was jurisdictional in nature. Under § 51.45(1) the State could not charge petitioner with bail jumping based solely on his consumption of alcohol. The statute did not prohibit alcohol restrictions as a condition of probation. However, the penalty for a violation could only be a revocation of that status, not a separate criminal charge of bail jumping. Therefore, the bail jumping conviction violated state policy and could not stand.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and granted petitioner's habeas corpus petition.
